1201 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Churitch v. State


No. 05-93-00295-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


888 S.W.2d 911; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3222



November 14, 1994, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MA91-58867-E.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court No. 4, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted appellant for the promotion of obscene material.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found appellant guilty of the promotion of obscene material and assessed punishment at 5 days in jail and $ 1500 fine. Appellant sought review and contended that the trial court erred in denying her motion to declare unconstitutional Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Appellant argued that § 43.21 and § 43.23 violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held that the court of criminal appeals had expressly declined to set a different standard for reviewing obscenity laws under article I, § 8, even though it had the power to do so. Appellant urged the court to conduct a separate analysis under article I, § 8. The court stated that they may not apply a separate test in criminal cases that was in conflict with the pronouncements of the court of criminal appeals. The court declined appellant's invitation to conduct a separate analysis under article I, § 8. It overruled appellant's point of error and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which convicted appellant for the promotion of obscene material because the court could not apply a separate test for reviewing obscenity laws that would conflict with the standard used by the court of criminal appeals.

1203 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Patton v. Saint Joseph's Hosp.


No. 2-93-241-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


887 S.W.2d 233; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2769



November 9, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 352ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. BRUCE AULD



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged an order from the 352nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) that granted a directed verdict to appellees hospital and radiologist on fraud, negligence, and gross negligence. A partial directed verdict was granted to appellee surgeon on negligence, gross negligence, and willful and negligent misrepresentation. The fraud and lack of consent claims were submitted to the jury that found in appellee surgeon's favor.


OVERVIEW: Appellee surgeon examined appellant patient. Appellant's sonogram was interpreted by appellee radiologist, who believed that the sonogram showed a large abdominal mass. No mass was found during surgery, but appellee surgeon removed her appendix. Appellant sued appellee surgeon for fraud, negligence, gross negligence, lack of informed consent, and willful and negligent misrepresentation. Appellant sued appellees, radiologist and hospital, for fraud, negligence, and gross negligence. Appellees, hospital and radiologist, were granted a directed verdict. Appellee surgeon was granted a partial directed verdict and the jury found in his favor regarding fraud and lack of consent. Appellant challenged the decision. The court affirmed and held that two of appellant's experts were properly excluded for appellant's failure, without good cause, to supplement the interrogatories as required by Tex. R. Civ. P. 166b(6)(b), 215(5). The court held that appellant failed to show any negligence by appellee radiologist. Therefore, the directed verdict for appellees, radiologist and hospital, was proper. The court found that the partial directed verdict for appellee surgeon was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that two of appellant patient's experts were properly excluded as witnesses due to appellant's failure to supplement the interrogatories. The court upheld the directed verdicts in favor of appellees hospital and radiologist because there was no evidence of negligence. Appellant failed to present a prima facie case of fraud, and a directed verdict for appellee surgeon on the negligence issues was proper.

 

1204 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Moore


NO. 07-93-0294-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


890 S.W.2d 821; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2771



November 8, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 72ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF CROSBY COUNTY; NO. 5451; HONORABLE J. BLAIR CHERRY, JR., JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged a judgment entered by the 72nd Judicial District Court of Crosby County (Texas) in his divorce action against appellee wife. The trial court ordered the parties' divorce and divided the community estate. Appellee's claim for reimbursement for appellant's payments to his ex-wife and the value of his unpaid corporate work was granted. Appellee received a monetary judgment for appellant's breach of fiduciary duty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband controlled all community assets. He was not paid, but devoted time and money to a corporation he co-owned. During his marriage, he paid a debt to his ex-wife. He filed for divorce from appellee. She counterclaimed for divorce and reimbursement for funds paid to appellant's ex-wife. She brought a separate cause of action for breach of appellant's fiduciary duty. The court granted a divorce, divided the marital property, and awarded appellee reimbursement and breach of duty damages. Appellant challenged the decision. The court held it was error to award damages, because a breach of duty claim was not a separate cause of action in a divorce action. If appellee filed a timely remittitur, the court would affirm the judgment. Appellee was entitled to compensation for appellant's efforts in the corporation. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in dividing the marital estate, but erred in allowing the jury to consider appellee's mental anguish claim. The issues of bond ownership, farm equipment value, appellant's annuity, and appellee's reimbursement claim were properly submitted to the jury, whose findings were supported by sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The court held that it was error to award appellee wife damages for appellant husband's breach of fiduciary duty, because this was not an independent cause of action in a divorce suit. The trial court fairly divided the community estate. Sufficient evidence supported appellee's claims for reimbursement and the value of appellant's corporate work. The court ordered appellee to file a timely remittitur and it would then affirm the judgment.

 

1205 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bui v. State


No. A14-93-00541-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2663



November 3, 1994, Rendered  
November 3, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 642166.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his capital murder conviction that was entered by the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas). Appellant argued that the court erred in refusing the jury charge appellant suggested. The charge involved an instruction that suggested the jury might find murder and not capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a conviction for capital murder, complaining of error in the failure to submit requested jury instructions. Appellant shot the victim during a drug transaction. Appellant contended the trial court erred in failing to grant appellant's requested instruction on the lesser-included offense of murder in the event the jury found appellant committed the offense knowingly, rather than intentionally. The instruction requested by appellant advised the jury that if they found appellant knowingly caused the death of the victim, but they had a reasonable doubt whether the defendant intentionally killed the victim, they should have found appellant guilty of murder and not guilty of capital murder. The instruction given by the court adequately set forth the required culpable mental state required for a conviction for capital murder. Both the instruction requested by appellant and the submitted instruction conveyed the requirement of a finding of intentional conduct. When the charge given adequately covered that contained in the refused charge, there was no harm shown. Therefore the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's capital murder conviction was affirmed because the charge given to the jury adequately conveyed that appellant could not be found guilty of capital murder unless his conduct was intentional.

 

1206 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Spring Indep. Sch. Dist. v. Harris County Appraisal Dist.


No. A14-93-00904-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


889 S.W.2d 562; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2664



November 3, 1994, Rendered  
November 3, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 215th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-47808. Chambers, Eugene Hon., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district sought review of a decision from the 215th District Court, Harris County (Texas), dismissing plaintiff's claim that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.12(f), (g) (Supp. 1994), was unconstitutional because it violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, §§ 1, 2, and created non-uniform taxation and/or an unlawful tax exemption in favor of inventory owners.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff school district challenged the trial court's ruling that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.12(f), (g) (Supp. 1994) was constitutional. Statutory subsections (f) and (g) permitted defendant power companies to elect to have their natural gas inventories appraised on September 1 rather than the traditional date of January 1 in tax year 1989, resulting in a substantial loss of property taxes to plaintiff. On appeal, the court held that subsections (f) and (g) violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, §§ 1, 2, which decreed that taxation be "equal and uniform," in three ways. First, the statute permitted a narrow class of property owners, i.e., inventory owners such as defendants, to choose between two different valuation dates in order to minimize their tax burden. Second, the statute discriminated between inventory owners by giving an arbitrary benefit to some, depending upon which tax date was chosen. Third, the statute created a de facto tax exemption if defendants' inventory increased between September 1 and the following January 1. Finding no rational basis for the statute's disparate treatment of defendants, the court declared subsections (f) and (g) unconstitutional and reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision holding that a state tax statute that gave inventory owners the option of electing a more favorable property tax appraisal date than that afforded to other state taxpayers was unconstitutional because such disparate treatment violated the constitutional mandate that taxation be "equal and uniform."

 

1207 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Aerospace Optimist Club v. Texas Alcoholic Beverage Comm'n


No. 3-93-444-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


886 S.W.2d 556; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2648



November 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 23, 1994. As Corrected November 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 92-03400, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, licensee, club, and association, sought review of a judgment from the District of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas) which granted summary judgment to appellees, state beverage commission, treasurer, and attorney general, in appellants' suit to obtain a refund of state taxes under the Texas Bingo Enabling Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, licensee, club, and association, raised funds through bingo operations. After appellants were taxed on these funds, appellants paid state taxes and then sued appellees, state beverage commission, treasurer, and attorney general, to obtain a refund under the Texas Bingo Enabling Act, which had since been repealed. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees. On appeal, the issue was whether the state constitution permitted the legislature to impose taxes on gross receipts of bingo operations under the Bingo Amendment to the state constitution, Tex. Const. art. III, § 47(b). The court affirmed summary judgment to appellees because the court concluded that Tex. Const. art. III, § 47(b) did not prohibit taxes on gross receipts of bingo operations and the court therefore held that the imposition of taxes on bingo gross receipts was constitutional. The court held that the legislature could impose a tax on the gross receipts of bingo game operators and that the bingo amendment to the state constitution neither expressly nor impliedly prohibited the legislature's power to tax gross receipts from bingo games.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment to appellees, state beverage commission, treasurer, and attorney general, because the court concluded that the state constitution did not prohibit taxing gross receipts of bingo operations and the court therefore held that the imposition of taxes on bingo gross receipts was constitutional.

Citizens Ass'n for Sound Energy v. Boltz


No. 07-93-0226-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


886 S.W.2d 283; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2699



November 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 886 S.W.2d 283 at 292.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 116TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY; NO. 89-8439-F; HONORABLE FRANK ANDREWS, JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant in Part and Overrule in Part of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of July 26, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1856.
Citizens Ass'n for Sound Energy v. Boltz, 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 4133 (Tex. App. Amarillo, July 26, 1994)
Citizens Ass'n for Sound Energy v. Boltz, 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1856 (Tex. App. Amarillo, July 26, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Granted in part and overruled in part Appellant's Motion for Rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This case came before the court upon motion for rehearing regarding an order of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), in an action between appellant citizen's association and appellee association members.


OVERVIEW: Appellee association members brought an action against appellant citizen's association. Appellant made a motion for rehearing. The court affirmed in part, holding that assuming appellant had associational standing to assert the rights of its members, the trial court's protective order prevented its members from suffering any injury from the application of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 1396-2.23. Although there was nothing to show that appellant was authorized to assert the rights of nonmembers, the contributors, consultants, and informants, the court's order served to prevent injury to the rights of those individuals as well. Appellant also alleged that application of the court's original holding to the trial court's protective order permitted appellees to inspect appellant's financial activities through the year 1992. Because a question of fact existed as to appellant's entitlement to an exemption under art. 1396-2.23, that portion of the motion for rehearing was granted.


OUTCOME: The portions of the trial court judgment purporting to grant appellee relief were severed and reversed and remanded to the trial court because questions of fact existed. The remainder of the judgment after the severance was affirmed because the statute in question was not unconstitutionally applied.

Chronic v. State


No. 05-93-00417-CR, No. 05-93-00418-CR, No. 05-93-00419-CR, No. 05-93-00420-CR, No. 05-93-00421-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3781



October 31, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 5. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MA92-49906-F, MA92-47175-F, MA92-53690-F, MA92-53689-F, MA92-50043-F.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court No. 5, Dallas County (Texas), convicting him of five counts of promotion of obscene material.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of promotion of obscene material. Appellant claimed on appeal that the trial court erred in denying his motion to declare Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.21, 43.23 unconstitutional. Appellant acknowledged that these sections had historically been held constitutional in the face of claims that the obscenity statutes violate the U.S. Const. amend. I. Appellant urged the court to conduct a separate analysis under Tex. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held that it could not apply a = test that was in conflict with the pronouncements of the court of criminal appeals. Thus, it declined appellant's invitation to conduct a separate analysis under the Texas constitution. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed criminal appellant's conviction for five counts of promotion of obscene material. The court may not apply a separate test in criminal cases that was in conflict with the pronouncements of the court of criminal appeals.

 

1210 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Moffett v. State


No. 05-93-00650-CR, No. 05-93-00651-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3851



October 31, 1994, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 363rd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. F92-69963-TW and F92-69964-TW.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for aggravated assault in the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), alleging his sentences and fines were so disproportionate to the crimes committed that it violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of aggravated assault following an incident where appellant fired shots at police officers. Appellant sought review, alleging his sentences and fines were so disproportionate to the crimes committed that it violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 13. Specifically, appellant argued that the sentences were disproportionate when examined in light of his age, background, and the facts and circumstances involved in the case. The court affirmed, noting that the trial court imposed a sentence of five years in each case and a fine of $ 800 in one case, which was within the punishment range for the offense. The punishments also fell within the middle of the range which was not disproportionate to the facts of the case and appellant's record. Therefore, because the punishment assessed by the trial court in both cases, and the fine of $ 800 was within the permissible statutory range and was not grossly disproportionate to his crime, they did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions for aggravated assault were affirmed because the punishment and the fine assessed were within the permissible statutory range and not grossly disproportionate to his crime; therefore, they did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.

 

1211 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Naranjo v. State


No. 13-93-353-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


890 S.W.2d 467; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2702



October 28, 1994, Delivered  
October 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled December 8, 1994. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 5, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court at Law of San Patricio County, Texas. (Tr.Ct.No. 39040)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the County Court at Law of San Patricio County (Texas), that convicted defendant of possessing an inhalant under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 485.031 (1992).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of possessing an inhalant under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 485.031 (1992), and he sought review, arguing that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 484 and 485 were unconstitutional. Defendant further contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict, and that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on a definition of "inhalant. " Defendant maintained that the trial court erred by referring to the offense incorrectly as "possession of inhalant." The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, finding that the applicable sections were constitutionally valid, because they were not vague, and because the section under which defendant was convicted gave sufficient notice to citizens. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The trial court did not need to define a common word like "inhalant" to the jury. The court concluded that the trial court's use of "possession of inhalant" was an acceptable shorthand phrase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of possessing an inhalant, finding that the law under which defendant was convicted was constitutional. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to convict, and that the trial court properly refused to instruct the jury on the definition of "inhalant."

 

1212 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


2300, Inc. v. City of Arlington


No. 2-94-00135-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


888 S.W.2d 123; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2864



October 19, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion to Publish Granted November 22, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2865. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 342ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Bob McGrath



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult cabaret clubs sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) that denied their request for a temporary injunction to prohibit appellee city from enforcing Arlington, Tex. Ordinance No. 92-117, § 5.01(A)-(B) (1992) that prohibited dancers from touching patrons while in a state of nudity. Appellants asserted the ordinance violated free speech and equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment that denied appellant adult cabarets' request for a preliminary injunction and upheld as constitutional the "no touch" provisions of the Arlington, Tex. Ordinance No. 92-117, § 5.01(A)-(B) (1992) that prohibited dancers at adult cabaret clubs from touching the patrons while in a state of nudity. The court rejected appellants arguments that the ordinance was facially overbroad restrictions on speech and violated equal protection. The court clarified that although Tex. Const. art. I, § 8 provided greater protections than U.S. Const. amend. I, those greater protections did not apply to topless/exotic dancing. The court found that the ordinance was a permissible time, place, and manner restriction on speech when it did not discriminate based on content, was narrowly tailored to effectively promote the government's interest, and left open ample alternative communication channels. The court held that the ordinance did not violate equal protection rights when appellants were not members of a suspect class and the ordinance was applied equally to all adult cabarets.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied appellants' request for a preliminary injunction. The court held that the ordinance was a permissible restriction on free speech when it did not discriminate based on content, was sufficiently narrowly tailored, and left open ample alternative communication channels. The court held that ordinance did not violate equal protection when appellants were not suspect class and were treated equally.

 

1213 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hawks v. State


No. 05-94-00061-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 4102



October 18, 1994, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 194th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F93-67806-VM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the decision of the 194th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted the appellant for retaliation, and denied his motion to quash the indictment.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The appellant was convicted for retaliation. He filed a motion to quash the indictment which was denied. Thereafter, the appellant pled guilty, executed a judicial confession, waived jury trial, and entered into a negotiated plea bargain agreement. The trial court followed the plea bargain agreement. The appellant filed an appeal and argued that trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash because the indictment was fundamentally defective. Th appellant's complaints centered largely on the use of the term unlawful conduct in the indictment. The state contended that the indictment was not fundamentally defective because it tracked the statutory elements and the appellant was not harmed if there was error. The court held that when an element of an offense was unlawful conduct, the indictment need not allege the specifics of the unlawful conduct to charge an offense. The appellant's indictment was not fundamentally defective, and the court overruled the appellant's point of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which convicted the appellant for retaliation, and denied his motion to quash the indictment because the court held that when an element of an offense was unlawful conduct, the indictment need not allege the specifics of the unlawful conduct to charge an offense.

 

1214 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Choyce v. State


No.01-94-00205-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2485



October 13, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
October 13, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 30, 1994.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 11/30/1994
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Choyce v. Thaler, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16356 (S.D. Tex., Feb. 9, 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Transferred by Choyce v. Dir., Tex. Dep't of Crim. Justice-Corr. Insts. Div., 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 160955 (E.D. Tex., Nov. 24, 2015)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Choyce v. Davis, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 96220 (S.D. Tex., June 17, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 653300.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for aggravated robbery in the 337th District Court of Harris County (Texas) and argued that his conviction should be reversed because the state's recommendation of punishment violated a plea bargain agreement and because the trial court erred in denying his motion to withdraw his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for aggravated robbery and entered a guilty plea. The judicial confession form which appellant signed reflected a notation of "no agreed recommendation" in the space provided for sentencing recommendations. At appellant's sentencing, appellant appeared with appointed counsel. The trial court asked counsel for appellant if he had reviewed the presentence report, and if there were any additions, deletions or corrections appellant wished to make to the report. Counsel for appellant responded that after reviewing the report, appellant did not wish to make any changes to it. Appellant subsequently filed a pro se motion to withdraw his plea of guilty, which the trial court denied. The court held that there was no evidence of any agreement for a specific sentencing recommendation. Therefore, the state did not waive its right to present a sentencing recommendation to the trial court. The court further held that the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.129(d) were satisfied by allowing appellant's counsel to review the presentence report, and by offering no objection to the report at trial appellant's counsel waived any error for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery, holding that the trial court committed no reversible error in denying appellant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea because appellant's counsel reviewed the presentence report but did not object to it, waiving any error for appellate review.

 

1215 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wichita County v. Hart


No. 3-93-358-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


892 S.W.2d 912; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2447



October 12, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 15, 1995. Released for Publication March 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 468,081, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), in appellee employees' suit for wrongful termination under the Texas Whistleblower Act. The judgment was entered after the trial court denied appellant's motion to transfer venue, and after a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, law enforcement officers in appellant county's sheriff's department, were terminated after reporting questionable activities. Appellees filed suit under the Whistleblower Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 554.001-.009, in another county pursuant to that act. The trial court denied appellant's motion to transfer venue and appellees prevailed at trial. The court affirmed, holding that the special venue provision of the Whistleblower Act was mandatory. The court found no error in jury instructions, patterned after instructions used in previous whistleblower cases, holding that an actual violation of law was not required for appellees to prevail, and the use of lost wages as the measure of future damages was proper. The court found that evidence supported findings that appellees' conduct was objectively reasonable, that reports were to an appropriate law enforcement authority, and that the sheriff acted with malice in terminating appellees; and findings concerning damages. The court held that the sheriff was a part of appellant's government, and consequently appellant was liable for his misdeeds. The court ruled that the Whistleblower Act was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment against appellee county, holding venue was proper, and finding no error in the jury instructions, patterned after those used in previous whistleblower cases. The court held that evidence supported the jury's findings, including findings of future wage loss and future mental anguish. The court found that appellant was liable for the sheriff's misdeeds. The court held that the Whistleblower Act was constitutional.

 

1216 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tobias v. State


NO. 2-93-386-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


884 S.W.2d 571; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2421



October 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. FRANK DOUTHITT



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for coercion of a public servant by the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which denied appellant's motion to quash the indictment, allowed the state to amend the indictment, and overruled his motion for instructed verdict.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for coercion of a public servant under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.03 (1994), holding that the conviction was supported by the evidence as the state proved the essential elements and negated the statutory exception under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.03(c) (1994). Appellant's pleadings in the underlying suit showed he was a student, not a member of a governing body. The trial court had jurisdiction to allow the state to amend the indictment under Tex. Const. art. V, § 12, as the original indictment was not void. The amendment was proper under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.10 (1989) and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. V or Tex. Const. art. I, § 14 as it did not allege a new offense. Denial of the motion to quash the indictment was not error as the enforcement of § 36.03 did not violate appellant's right to free speech, due process rights, or the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Appellant's threats to appellate judges showed his true intent to threaten and coerce them, the indictment gave appellant fair notice of the charge against him, and appellant's threats could never constitute "official action" under § 36.03(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for coercion of a public servant. Denial of appellant's motion to quash did not violate appellant's right to free speech, due process rights, or the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Constitution. Overruling appellant's motion for instructed verdict was proper as the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The trial court properly allowed the state to amend the indictment.

Metzger v. Sebek


No. 01-92-00912-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


892 S.W.2d 20; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2382



September 29, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
September 29, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 269th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-53676.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in parts, reversed and remanded in parts, and reversed and rendered in part; part of the appeal dismissed for want of jurisdiction


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and his attorneys, challenged the directed verdict entered against them and in favor of appellees, a wife, her attorneys, and medical personnel associated with the case, from the 269th District Court, Harris County (Texas). Appellant claimed denial of a fair trial and trial court error in granting the directed verdict in his multi-cause action. Appellants sought review of the sanctions entered against them.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband and appellee wife were divorcing. Appellant and appellee were awarded joint custody over their three children. One child then exhibited signs of sexual abuse. The trial court entered a divorce decree that granted appellee managing conservatorship over the children, that ordered the abused child to be hospitalized for treatment, and that ordered appellant to pursue therapy. Appellant brought suit in the trial court. After hearing the evidence, the trial court granted a directed verdict for appellee on all causes of action. Certain sanctions were affirmed; others were reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's directed verdict for appellee wife. Appellant husband's theories of liability were legally unsustainable. The court found no trial court partiality or trial judge advocacy that rendered appellant's trial unfair. The court affirmed certain sanctions and reversed the imposition of certain other sanctions against appellant husband and appellant attorneys, remanding the issues to the trial court with instructions.

 

1218 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Stoker v. State


No. 11-93-042-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


886 S.W.2d 443; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2332



September 22, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Court at Law #2 of Taylor County



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for driving while intoxicated by the County Court at Law #2 of Taylor County (Texas), contending that Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 24(a-1) was unconstitutional under the United States and Texas Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of driving while intoxicated, and sentenced to jail time and levied a fine. On appeal, he contended that his conviction demanded reversal because Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 24(a-1) was unconstitutional under the United States and Texas Constitutions. This statute provided for the suspension of an individual's motor vehicle operator license upon a conviction for driving while intoxicated. The court noted that appellant did not challenge his conviction or punishment, rather, he sought only to attack the automatic suspension of his operator's license. Further, applicable law dictated that an ancillary result of a conviction and punishment for appellant's offense, such as a license suspension, was not subject to appeal, as a challenge to that suspension was not truly directed to his conviction and punishment. Further, license suspensions were only subject to appeal where an appeal was authorized by statute. The court in turn found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 31(a) expressly provided that there was no right to appeal an automatic suspension. Accordingly, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because appellant had no right to appeal the automatic license suspension that accompanied his conviction and punishment for driving while intoxicated.

Crum & Forster, Inc. v. Monsanto Co.

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which awarded appellee company over $ 70 million in damages, prejudgment interest, and attorney fees, as well as costs and post-judgment interest. Appellee and appellant insurance companies, which included a holding company and several affiliated insurance companies, were co-defendants in several lawsuits. University of Tex. Medical Branch v. Greenhouse


No. 01-93-00371-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


889 S.W.2d 427; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2263



September 15, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
September 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled December 22, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3103. Reported at: 889 S.W.2d 427 at 432.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 56th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89CV0756.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 10, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 485.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought rehearing after initial review from a 56th District Court, Galveston County (Texas) judgment in favor of appellee in her medical malpractice suit, basing its request on various points including failure to comply with Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.002 (1986).


OVERVIEW: After appellee's medical malpractice suit against appellant hospital was decided in her favor and affirmed on review, appellant moved for rehearing, arguing various points including appellee's failure to comply with the notice provisions of the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.002 (1986). The court found that it was undisputed that appellee had not given appellant written notice of her injury within six months after the day the incident giving rise to the claim occurred. Further, the court held that because appellee's claim against appellant existed only by virtue of the Act, otherwise being barred by sovereign immunity, the fact that appellee had been incapable of complying with the notice requirements because neither she nor appellant learned of her injury within the six-month time frame unfortunately did not excuse appellee from compliance with the Act's notice provisions. Thus, the court reluctantly reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, holding that unfortunately appellee's only recourse against appellant was purely statutory, otherwise being barred by sovereign immunity, and finding that appellee had failed to strictly comply with the relevant statute, such that she could not recover from appellant.

State v. Eversole


No. C14-94-00015-CR, No. C14-94-00016-CR, No. C14-94-00017-CR, No. C14-94-00018-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


889 S.W.2d 418; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2282



September 15, 1994, Rendered  
September 15, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 228th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 677,981; 677,982; 677,983; 677,984. Larry Gist, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted appellee commissioner's motion to quash four indictments involving Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 253.035(h), 254.031(a)(3)(4).


OVERVIEW: Appellee commissioner was indicted for perjury and for failing to file a complete officeholder report as required by Tex. Code Elec. Code Ann. §§ 253.035(h), 254.031(a)(3)(4). The trial court granted appellee's motion to quash the indictments. The state challenged that decision. On appeal, the court sustained three of the state's five points of error, but affirmed the judgment. The court agreed with the state that appellee did not swear to a legal conclusion when he swore that his officeholder report was complete. The court also agreed that § 253.035(h)(1) was plain and unambiguous and that the indictments properly alleged the offense of perjury. The court, however, held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it quashed the indictments because the state was trying to impose upon appellee, by way of a perjury charge, a punishment greater than that intended by the legislature for violations Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 254.041(A)(2). Also, appellee did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence supporting the indictment, but argued that the statutes upon which the state based its indictments were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting appellee officeholder's motion to quash his indictments for perjury and for failing to file a complete officeholder report. The state was attempting to impose upon appellee, by way of a perjury charge, a harsher penalty than that intended by the legislature for failure to file a complete officeholder report.

J.B. Advertising v. Sign Bd. of Appeals


No. 11-93-138-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


883 S.W.2d 443; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2288



September 15, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 193rd District Court of Dallas County



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is reversed, and the cause is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertisers sought review of an order of the 193rd District Court of Dallas County (Texas) that granted the motion of appellee board and appellee city for summary judgment in appellants' proceeding that sought review, by way of certiorari, of a decision by appellee board to remove two of appellants' billboards.


OVERVIEW: In 1983, two billboards owned by appellant advertisers were issued permits as commercial billboards. Three years later, appellee city enacted a new sign code prohibiting commercial billboards, but appellants' two signs were granted nonconforming rights. Subsequently, appellants leased the signs to a car dealership located under the signs. Appellants were then notified the signs lost their nonconforming rights when the type of advertising changed from off-premise to on-premise. Appellants sought review of the order to remove the signs to appellee board. After a hearing, appellee board upheld the decision. Appellants then filed a petition for writ of certiorari in the district court. In response, appellees filed a motion for summary judgment, which the district court granted. Appellants then sought review, arguing in part they were denied the right to cross-examine the only witness called by appellee city during the hearing. The court reversed and remanded because preventing appellants from cross-examining the witness resulted in the denial of their rights to due process under Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, and, thus, appellees failed to prove they were entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted the motion for summary judgment of appellee city and appellee board, and remanded, because appellant advertisers were denied their right to due course of law at the hearing held by appellee board; thus, appellees failed to prove, as a matter of law, they were entitled to a judgment in their favor.

Alvarez v. State


No. 08-85-00281-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


885 S.W.2d 564; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2296



September 15, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 243rd Judicial District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 45258). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Herb Marsh



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 243rd Judicial District Court of El Paso County, Texas, which convicted appellant for aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 60 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted of aggravated robbery, appellant argued the trial court's instruction to the jury of parole law pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 required reversal of the sentence. The court first acknowledged that the statute pursuant to which the trial court had provided instructions on parole law had been found constitutionally invalid. Reviewing the record, the court held that the provision of the instruction constituted reversible error. The court reasoned that specific references to parole and good time laws during voir dire carried a high risk of inducing jurors to consider such issues during their deliberation on punishment. Additionally, the court noted that the fact that the sentence at issue was divisible by three implied that the jurors considered the constitutionally invalid instruction in their deliberations, because the statute from which the instruction was taken provided that a defendant was eligible for release upon serving one third of his sentence. Combined with parole references made during argument and the trial court's failure to give a curative instruction, the court concluded that reversal of the sentence was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's sentence for aggravated robbery because circumstances indicated that the jurors considered an unconstitutional jury instruction that the trial court provided.

Howell v. Mauzy


NO. 3-93-084-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


899 S.W.2d 690; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3294



September 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Ordered Released for Publication May 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 406,958, HONORABLE PETE LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered in Part; Affirmed in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a summary judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District (Texas), ordering that appellant take nothing on his claims against appellees for their alleged failure to report certain campaign contributions and expenditures in accordance with Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 251.001-.019, and a declaratory judgment the court rendered in appellees' favor on their counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: After contested primary elections, appellant and appellee became opposing party nominees in an election for a judicial seat. Appellant filed the present lawsuit shortly before the general election. He sought damages and injunctive relief against his opponent and his wife, who served as campaign treasurer, for alleged violations of campaign contribution and expenditure reporting requirements. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees and also granted a declaratory judgment counterclaim filed by appellees. On review, the court affirmed the summary judgment despite appellant's numerous arguments. For example, with reference to alleged violations that occurred during the primary election, the court held that appellant had no standing to challenge such violations because the statute permitted such challenges only for opposing candidates. Because appellant did not become appellee's opposing candidate until after the primary election, he had no standing under Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 251.011(k) to make such claims. However, the court reversed the trial court's entry of a declaratory judgment in favor of appellees because it presented no new controversy.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellees on appellant's action claiming campaign contribution and reporting violations was affirmed because the court found no error in the trial court's ruling. However, the court reversed that portion of the judgment awarding appellees relief on their declaratory judgment counterclaim, and the attorney's fees awarded in connection with that counterclaim, because it presented no new controversy.

Ex parte Matthews


No. 01-92-00447-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2223



September 8, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
September 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [*1] On Appeal from the 208th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 594707. J. KYLES, Judge

Original Opinion of January 21, 1993, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 96.



DISPOSITION: Writ of Habeas Corpus denied


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed pretrial petition for a writ of habeas corpus, (Texas) to dismiss the indictment for aggravated perjury based on the statute of limitations in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 12.01(5) (Supp. 1994). Appellant claimed that the tolling provision in Tex. Code Crim. Prac. Ann. art. 12.05(a) (1977) violated her U.S. Constitutional rights of travel, due process and equal protection, and was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an out of state resident, misrepresented her educational qualifications when she testified for the state in a murder trial, then returned to her home state. Ten years later, appellee, the state, discovered the perjury and indicted appellant for aggravated perjury. Appellant filed a pretrial petition for a writ of habeas corpus to dismiss the indictment. The court held that the burden of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 12.05(a) (1977) that tolled the three year statute of limitations for aggravated perjury in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 12.01(5) (Supp. 1994) on interstate commerce was minimal compared to appellee's interest in capturing criminals, and that it applied equally to out of state residents who committed crimes in Texas and to Texas residents who fled the state after committing a crime. Thus, appellant's federal constitutional rights under the commerce, equal protection and due process clauses, the privileges and immunities clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, clause 1,and her right to travel were not violated. Because the word accused referred generically to a defendant, the statute was not vague. Therefore, the court denied the writ.


OUTCOME: The court denied the pretrial petition for a writ of habeas corpus to dismiss the indictment for aggravated perjury. The court held that statute tolling the statute of limitations applied equally to Texas residents and to non residents, and that the statute was easily understood by the general public. Thus, the statute did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights, nor was it unconstitutionally vague.

Board of Adjustment v. Patel


No. 06-94-00061-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


887 S.W.2d 90; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2242


August 16, 1994, Submitted  
September 8, 1994, Decided  
September 8, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's & Appellees' Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 10, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2776.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 162nd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court No. 92-6359-I



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Adjustment of the City of Dallas challenged the decision of the162nd Judicial District Court Dallas County, Texas, which granted summary judgment to appellee motel owners in an action involving the closing of a motel because it was operating under a nonconforming use. Appellees cross-claimed that Dallas Developmental Code § 51-4.704(a)(1) was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Tex. Const. art. I §§ 3 and 19.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee motel owners because appellant Board of Adjustment of the City of Dallas failed to amortize the investment of appellees in their motel prior to its use becoming nonconforming. The court held that even though appellees bought the motel after its use became nonconforming they were still entitled to amortization. The court determined that the investment of the person who owned the property at the time the use became nonconforming passed to the subsequent purchaser. Thus, appellees were entitled to amortize that portion of the original owners' investment remaining at the time the use became nonconforming. The court further held that the Dallas Developmental Code § 51-4.704(a)(1) was constitutional because it did not delegate the enforcement of its nonconforming use ordinance to its citizens but allowed them to initiate a nonconforming use terminating procedure. The court found that initiating a complaint did not deny appellees substantive due process or equal protection of the laws under either U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Tex. Const. art. I §§ 3 and 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted summary judgment to appellee motel owners. The court held that appellant Board of Adjustment of the City of Dallas failed to amortize the investment of appellees in its termination proceeding against appellees for nonconforming use and that the procedure was constitutional.

Hernandez v. State


No. B14-92-00704-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2182



September 1, 1994, Rendered  
September 1, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 621,108.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the 338th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied defendant's motion to suppress based on the denial of the right to counsel and an illegal stop and arrest, convicted defendant for capital murder, and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his capital murder conviction and life sentence. The court affirmed, finding no reversible error. The trial court correctly applied the accusation in the indictment to the evidence at trial. The inclusion of the definitions of intentionally and knowingly under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 6.03(a), (b) (1994) in the jury charge did not harm defendant to the extent that he did not receive a fair and impartial trial. The court found no error in overruling defendant's objection to the prosecutor's argument. The trial court did not err in granting the state's challenge for cause of a prospective juror without allowing defendant further cross-examination after he had questioned the juror twice. Defendant's counsel was not deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and life sentence for capital murder because the trial court correctly applied the accusation in the indictment to the evidence at trial, the inclusion of the statutory definitions in the jury charge did not harm defendant, defendant received a punishment within the range authorized by law, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to suppress.

Vaughn v. State


No. 01-93-00385-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


888 S.W.2d 62; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2166

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the 180th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which in a jury trial, found defendant guilty of aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, assessed punishment at six years confinement, probated, and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon. A jury found defendant guilty, assessed punishment at six years confinement, probated, and a fine. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for because the evidence was sufficient to support a finding that defendant assaulted the victim with a deadly weapon and threatened to kill him, trial counsel's comments did not amount to error, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of the relationship between a defense witness and defendant for the purpose of showing the witness's bias. The court believed that state's questions were proper and represented no more than the usual risk a defendant assumed when he or she took the stand to testify. The court overruled defendant's eleven points of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault with a deadly weapon because the evidence supported a finding that defendant assaulted the victim with a deadly weapon and threatened to kill him, a jury could have inferred that the firearm was loaded if it believed the victim and disbelieved defendant, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence to show the defense witness's bias.

Niven v. State


No. 01-92-00789-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2187



August 31, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
August 31, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 618,144.

This Opinion Substituted on Overrule of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 31, 1993, Previously Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2441.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for keeping a gambling place, which was entered after appellant's motion to suppress was denied and appellant entered into a plea bargain with state.


OVERVIEW: Officers found betting slips and gambling paraphernalia on appellant's premises. Appellant was arrested and charged with keeping a gambling place. The trial court denied appellant's motion to suppress and quash the indictment. Appellant later entered into a plea bargain for the offense of keeping a gambling place. The court found that appellant did not perfect his appeal because he did not comply with Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1). Appellant did not indicate anywhere on his notice of appeal that the trial judge had given permission for the appeal, as was required for an appeal for a nonjurisdictional defect after a plea of guilty. Therefore, nonjurisdictional errors were not preserved for review. The court reviewed appellant's assertion of a jurisdictional error. Appellant alleged lack of jurisdiction because Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 47.01(2), 47.01(8), and 47.04(a) were unconstitutional due to vagueness and overbreadth. The court disagreed and found that the statutory language used terms with well-known meanings that were not vague, nor did appellant demonstrate that the statutes implicated constitutionally protected conduct to support a claim of overbreadth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for keeping a gambling place, entered pursuant to a guilty plea, because appellant did not preserve any nonjurisdictional issues for review as appellant's notice of appeal did not show that the trial judge granted permission for the appeal. Additionally, the statutes appellant was charged under were not shown to be vague or overbroad.

Nunez v. Autry


No. 3-93-581-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


884 S.W.2d 199; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2202



August 31, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 492,328, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimants sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), that granted summary judgment to appellee receiver under the Texas Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Act, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C, § 5(2) (1987), for the reason that the residency requirement of § 5(2) violated U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimants sought to recover benefits under the Texas Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Act (Act), Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C (1987) for injuries that resulted from an accident with a truck insured by a company ordered into permanent receivership. Appellee receiver rejected the proof of claim, because neither appellants nor the insured were a resident of Texas as required by Texas Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C, § 5(2) (1987). Appellants brought suit and alleged that the claim was wrongly denied and that § 5(2) violated U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Appellee's motion for summary judgment was granted by the trial court and appellants sought review. The court found that appellants were residents of Mexico and U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, on its face, afforded them no protection. The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee and held that § 5(2) was constitutional because the insurance fund was created for the benefit of Texas residents and the protection of Texas residents from financial loss due to insurance company insolvencies was a legitimate state objective and § 5(2) was rationally related to achieving that objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee receiver and found the residency requirement of the Texas Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Act was constitutional because the insurance fund was created for the benefit of Texas residents and protecting Texas residents from financial loss due to insurer insolvencies was a legitimate state objective and the residency requirement was rationally related to achieving that objective.

Gulf States Utils. Co. v. Coalition of Cities for Affordable Util. Rates


NO. 3-92-046-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


883 S.W.2d 739; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2205



August 31, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled October 12, 1994. Released for Publication October 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 447,502, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Second Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of May 25, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1321.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, agency, agency office, and company, sought review of an order entered by the 250th Judicial District of Travis County (Texas), which reversed and remanded appellant agency's final order in action filed by appellees, municipalities and companies, for judicial review of appellant agency's final order in an electric-utility rate action conducted under Public Utility Regulatory Act (PURA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446(c) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, agency, agency office, and company, challenged an order rendered in a suit for judicial review of appellant agency's final order in an electric-utility rate case conducted under Public Utility Regulatory Act (PURA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c (1994). The trial court reversed appellant agency's final order and remanded to appellant agency with instructions. The court affirmed the judgment in part because appellees, municipalities and companies, failed to meet their burden of proving the prudence of expenditures that resulted in appellant agency's refusal to include those expenditures in rate base, and there was no causal link between the harm appellees suffered due to the exclusion of those expenditures from rate base, and appellant agency's erroneously attempted to afford the utility another opportunity to present more persuasive evidence regarding the prudence of the expenditures. The court reversed judgment including the remand of the matter to appellant agency for reconsideration of deferred expenses for appellant agency acted within its statutory authority, and the judgment disapproving of the offset from deferred expenses for interim revenue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant agency's order because the court approved the entire appellant agency order, exclusive of its decision to reexamine the prudence of the $ 1.453 billion in rate base, a decision the supreme court had already decided was an error of law.

Tri-Steel Structures v. Hackman


No. 2-93-252-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


883 S.W.2d 391; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2213



August 30, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 211TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. SAM HOUSTON



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court establishing the foreign judgment in Texas is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment debtor challenged by writ of error a judgment from the 211th District Court of Denton County (Texas), which established a foreign judgment in favor of appellee judgment creditor.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the establishment of appellee judgment creditor's foreign judgment against appellant judgment debtor under the Texas version of the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act (Act), Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 35.001 et seq. (1986). The court found that the trial court did not err in entering the foreign judgment because a technical violation of the notice provisions of the Act had not kept appellant from a course of redress. If appellee had any defenses to raise, it could have done so in its motion for new trial or could still do so in a bill of review. The court concluded that it should not pass on the validity of the notice provisions of the Act because it would constitute impermissible judicial legislating and because appellant had failed to show that it suffered any harm as a result of the notice provisions of the Act. The court found that the authentication requirements of Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 902(2) were met because the authentication certificate purported to bear the signature of the clerk, an officer or employee of the district, and the judge then certified that the clerk properly certified the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the establishment of appellee judgment creditor's foreign judgment against appellant judgment debtor in Texas. A technical violation of the notice provisions of the Texas version of the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act had not kept appellant from a course of redress and the authentication requirements for public documents had been met.

 

1233 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


R. R. E. v. Glenn


No. 2-92-152-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


884 S.W.2d 189; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2217



August 30, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 16TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. JOHN NARSUTIS.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of July 7, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1773.



DISPOSITION: Appellants failed to receive a fair and just trial before a jury composed of twelve qualified persons. The judgment is reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys sought review of a judgment from the 16th District Court of Denton County (Texas), which returned a money verdict in favor of appellee client in appellee's legal malpractice suit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorneys served as appellee client's attorney in a prolonged divorce suit in which conservatorship and visitation of a minor child were vigorously contested issues. After the divorce judgment became final appellee filed suit alleging that appellants coerced her into agreeing to a settlement and that appellants knowingly misrepresented their qualifications and services. The jury rendered a verdict in favor of appellee, and appellants sought review. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial because the jury was improperly composed. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 20 did not remove all disabilities imposed on serving as a juror by Tex. Const. art. I, § 15, which required the legislature to maintain the purity and efficiency of the jury system. The purity and efficiency of the jury system could not be maintained by allowing felons to serve on juries. The court found that the Constitution did not contemplate full restoration of a felons' rights other than by an executive pardon. Appellants did not waive their constitutional rights. Thus, appellants failed to receive a fair and just trial before a jury composed of twelve qualified persons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a trial court's judgment in favor of appellee client in a legal malpractice suit because appellant attorneys did not receive a fair and just trial before a jury composed of 12 qualified persons. A jury member was disqualified by conviction of a felony.

Caterpillar, Inc. v. Shears


NUMBER 13-92-010-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


881 S.W.2d 923; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2206; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,093



August 25, 1994, Delivered  
August 25, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 138th District Court of Cameron County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: We decline to address appellants' remaining points or error as they are not dispositive of the case. Tex. R. App. P. 90(a). We reverse the award of exemplary damages and render that no exemplary damages be recovered and affirm the remainder of the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer and distributor challenged a judgment by the 138th District Court of Cameron County (Texas), which found them strictly liable and negligent in a product liability action by appellee injured party and family. The jury awarded compensatory and exemplary damages to appellees. The jury found that appellant manufacturer was 70 percent at fault for the injuries and that appellant distributor was 30 percent at fault.


OVERVIEW: Appellee injured party was hurt while operating heavy equipment manufactured and sold by appellants, manufacturer and distributor. The protective canopy had been removed and appellee was rear-ended by another front-end loader. Appellee injured party and family filed a product liability suit against appellants. The jury awarded appellees compensatory and exemplary damages. The jury found appellants strictly liable and negligent and apportioned fault at 70 percent for appellant manufacturer and 30 percent for appellant distributor. Appellants challenged the decision. The court reversed the award of exemplary damages, finding no evidence of gross negligence in the equipment's design equipment or conscious disregard for appellee's safety. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment, upholding the jury's findings of negligence and failure to warn. The evidence supported the jury's apportionment of fault. It was not an abuse of discretion to allow appellee's expert to testify or refuse to grant appellants' motions for continuance. The exclusion of evidence regarding the buy back of the removable canopy was within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the exemplary damages award, finding no evidence of conscious disregard for safety or gross negligence. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment and upheld the jury's finding of negligence and failure to warn. The evidence supported apportionment of fault. Allowing an expert to testify for appellee injured party and family and refusing motions for continuance by appellants, manufacturer and distributor, was not error.

Flores v. State


No. 07-93-0348-CR, No. 07-93-0349-CR, No. 07-93-0350-CR, No. 07-93-0351-CR, No. 07-93-0352-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


883 S.W.2d 383; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2099



August 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 5, 1994. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 2 OF DALLAS COUNTY; NOS. MA92-62532-B, MA92-55654-B, MA92-57843-B, MA92-60906-B, & MA92-64627-B; HONORABLE JOHN HENDRIK, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Each judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for promotion of obscene material entered by the County Criminal Court No. 2 of Dallas County (Texas), arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to declare the obscenity statutes, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 and § 43.23, upon which his prosecutions were based, unconstitutional as a limitation on free speech guaranteed by Tex. Const. art. I, § VIII.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with five separate offenses of promotion of obscene material. He pleaded nolo contendere and was found guilty in a bench trial. Appellant was sentenced to five days in jail and a fine for each offense. He sought review, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to declare the obscenity statutes, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21 and § 43.23, unconstitutional as a limitation on free speech guaranteed by Tex. Const. art. I, § VIII. The court affirmed. As an intermediate appellate court, the court was duty bound to follow the law declared by the Texas Court of Criminal Appeals on matters pertaining to the enforcement of criminal laws and, once the law was declared, the court was not at liberty to impose a different declaration of the law. The refusal of the petition for discretionary review fortified the court's declination to conduct an independent analysis of the obscenity statutes under Tex. Const. art. I, § VIII. It followed that the obscenity statutes were not subject to the claim of unconstitutionality made against them in the appeals. The court affirmed each judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for promotion of obscene material. As an intermediate appellate court, the court was duty bound to follow the law declared by the court of criminal appeals on matters pertaining to the enforcement of criminal laws and, once the law was declared, the court could not impose a different declaration of the law.

Reno v. State


NO. 2-93-208-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


882 S.W.2d 106; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2126



August 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 15, 1995. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NUMBER ONE OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. R.E. THORNTON



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court No. 1, of Tarrant County (Texas), convicting him or murder because his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to object to an improper search and the prosecution improperly commented on the parole laws.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his murder conviction on grounds that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to object to evidence seized during a search of his apartment, and the prosecution committed reversible error during closing argument by encouraging the jury to consider the existence of parole laws in assessing punishment. The court found that the search of appellant's apartment was proper because the searching officer had a parole violation warrant, first looked through a window, and had a reasonable belief that appellant was inside. The court therefore affirmed the conviction, holding that defense counsel was not ineffective by failing to object to evidence seized during a proper search, and that the prosecution's closing argument that appellant was on parole when he committed the murder was not so manifestly improper so as to deprive appellant of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for murder was affirmed because defense counsel was not ineffective by failing to object to evidence seized during a proper search. The court further concluded that appellant was not deprived of a fair trial by the prosecution's argument that appellant was on parole when he committed the murder.
