City of Dallas v. Shade


No. 05-93-00399-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3789



August 19, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 192nd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-6056-K.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged a judgment from the 192nd District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted plaintiff homeowner summary judgment in plaintiff's nuisance suit. Defendant claimed that the statute of limitations had run, that it had governmental immunity, that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the verdict, and that the trial court erred in not submitting certain requested issues and definitions to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city appealed a judgment that granted plaintiff homeowner summary judgment in his suit that alleged that defendant created a nuisance causing raw sewage to back up into his home. The court affirmed the judgment. The court did not address the merits of defendant's claims that the statute of limitations had run, that it had governmental immunity, or that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the verdict. The court ruled that defendant was precluded from meeting its burden on appeal because it did not provide the court with an adequate record, in that numerous exhibits and all of plaintiff's documentary evidence were missing. On defendant's claim that the trial court erred in not submitting certain requested issues and definitions to the jury, the court ruled that because it did not obtain the trial judge's endorsement on the proffered instructions and charges, and because it did not file a bill of exceptions, the alleged errors were waived. On its claim that the jury charge improperly defined the term "nuisance," the court ruled that defendant failed to carry its burden and show reversible error because it did not show harm from the instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that granted plaintiff homeowner summary judgment in his nuisance. Defendant city did not preserve error, provide the court with an adequate record, or comply with the endorsement rule or file a bill of exceptions; thus, the court did not address many of defendant's claims. Defendant did not show that it was harmed by the trial court's definition of "nuisance," and, thus, it did not show reversible error.

Nguyen v. State


No. 01-94-00098-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


882 S.W.2d 471; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1931



August 4, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
August 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Motion for Discretionary Review Refused December 21, 1994. Stat's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied February 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 56th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93CR2088. I. A. LERNER, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 56th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus requesting that his prosecution for theft by receiving stolen property be dismissed with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought a writ of habeas corpus in the trial court to have his prosecution for theft by receiving stolen property dismissed with prejudice under Tex. Crim. Code Proc. Ann. arts. 28.061and 32.01. The state had failed to bring a timely indictment after appellant's admission to bail under art. 32.01. The court denied the writ. On appeal, the court reversed and held that amended Tex. Crim. Code Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 was unconstitutional only in its capacity as an enforcement mechanism of the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1989). Amended Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 was still viable as an enforcement tool of art. 32.01, independent of the Speedy Trial Act. The court also held that amended art. 28.061 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the writ of habeas corpus because appellant was entitled to discharge with prejudice for the state's failure to indict appellant at the next term of court held after his admission to bail. The court found that the applicable discharge statute was still viable as an enforcement tool of the dismissal statute.

Willard v. Davis


NO. 2-94-131-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


881 S.W.2d 907; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1925



August 3, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 17TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. FRED W. DAVIS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, health care provider, sought writ of mandamus from order of the 17th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) seeking to have respondent, judge, rescind order and stay all proceedings for six months in accordance with Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Act, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C, § 17 (1994), in medical malpractice action. Relator asserted that trial court abused its discretion in declaring § 17 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Relator, health care provider, sought writ of mandamus to have respondent, judge, rescind order and stay all proceedings of for six months in accordance with Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Act, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C, § 17 (1994). The parties were conducting discovery in medical malpractice action when relator's liability insurer was adjudged insolvent and placed in receivership. Relator sought a stay of proceedings. The trial court declared § 17 unconstitutional. The appellate court determined that construction of a statute was a question of law for the court to decide. The court presumed the statute was effective and constitutional, Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 311.021 (1988). It was to be presumed that the legislature did not act arbitrarily, and where reasonable minds could differ, a mere difference of opinion was not a sufficient basis for striking down legislation as arbitrary or unreasonable, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C, § 17. The provisions of § 17 were unambiguous and expressly required the granting of a six months' stay if the movant established entitlement to the stay. The writ was granted and all proceedings were stayed for six months.


OUTCOME: All proceedings were stayed for six months as mandated by the Property and Casualty Insurance Guaranty Act. The petition for the writ of mandamus was conditionally granted. The court concluded that the provisions of the Act were unambiguous and expressly required granting of a six months' stay where relator established entitlement to the stay.

McKinney v. State


NO. 2-93-254-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


880 S.W.2d 868; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1972



August 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 7, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NUMBER ONE OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. SHAREN WILSON



DISPOSITION: McKinney's sole point of error is overruled and the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of aggravated sexual assault, from the Criminal District Court Number One of Tarrant County (Texas), arguing that his conviction was not valid as the jury voir dire was presided over by a magistrate instead of the trial judge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review from his conviction of aggravated sexual assault, contending that the conviction was invalid because a critical portion of the trial was conducted by a magistrate who had no authority to act and was nothing more than a mere volunteer. On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court noted that the trial judge asked the parties whether there were any objections to the magistrate in question presiding over jury voir dire, to which both parties responded in the negative. The court held that under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 54.658 (1988) the trial judge may refer to a magistrate any criminal case for proceedings involving a pretrial motion, an examining trial, and any other matter the judge considers necessary and proper. The court noted with respect to instant case, however, that because appellant failed to object at trial to the magistrate conducting voir dire, no potential error had been preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because whatever potential error may have accrued from the trial judge's decision with respect to the magistrate was not preserved for review because appellant failed to object during trial.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO

July 29, 1994, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 31ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF WHEELER COUNTY; NO. 8028; HONORABLE BILL SHEEHAN, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 31st Judicial District Court of Wheeler County (Texas), which awarded appellees monetary damages after a jury verdict based on appellant's negligence in drilling a natural gas well.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was an oil drilling company that was responsible for drilling a natural gas well which eventually experienced a catastrophic blowout allowing a significant amount of natural gas to be lost. 1243 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Universal Servs. Co. v. Ung


No. B14-93-00026-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


882 S.W.2d 460; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1879



July 28, 1994, Rendered  
July 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 151st Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 86-03371. Carolyn Garcia, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 151st Court, Harris County, Texas, which awarded appellees $ 2,500,000 in punitive damages in appellees' worker's compensation wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: The decedent worked for appellant as a member of a crew cleaning debris from the shoulder of the highway. The decedent was killed by a trailer that veered into the workmen. The court affirmed the punitive damages award for appellees. The jury instruction on exemplary damages did not violate the United States and Texas Constitutions. The instruction informed the jury as to the nature of punitive damages and explained that they were not compulsory. The award was not excessive under the United States and Texas Constitutions. There was a rational basis for allowing worker's compensation plaintiffs to recover exemplary damages without having to prove actual damages. The evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support the jury's finding of gross negligence. Former employees for appellant testified that placing the workmen in the place they were located was ultra-hazardous. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct on ordinary negligence because worker's compensation plaintiffs could not recover for ordinary negligence. Appellant was not entitled to any settlement credit because the settling defendants paid no sums representing exemplary damages for gross negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the punitive damages award for appellees in their worker's compensation wrongful death action. The award was not excessive and there was a rational basis for allowing worker's compensation plaintiffs to recover exemplary damages without having to plead and prove actual damages. Appellant was not entitled to a settlement credit because the settling defendants paid no sums for exemplary damages based on gross negligence.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing appellant for murder; inter alia, the trial court committed no error in connection with its evidentiary rulings and its denial of appellant's motion for an instructed verdict, and the jury's verdict was supported by the evidence.

White v. State


No. 05-92-02017-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3607



July 25, 1994, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-00066-UI.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 2 of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of sexual assault and assessed an enhanced punishment of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because he was indicted for sexually assaulting "Opal Mattoxd", but at trial the victim testified her name was "Opal Mattox." The court found that there was sufficient evidence despite the misspelling of the victim's name that any rational trier of fact would have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. Appellant contended that the doctrine of idem sonans, which was applied to overcome the misspelling of the victim's name, was unconstitutional because it allowed a conviction on less proof than the indictment required. The court determined that an objection to the application of the doctrine of idem sonans had to be raised at trial. In affirming, the court concluded that appellant had waived the issue of the doctrine of idem sonans because he had not objected at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's judgment because there was sufficient evidence he committed the crime beyond a reasonable doubt despite the misspelling of the victim's name and because appellant had waived the issue of the doctrine of idem sonans by failing to object at trial.

Gidrey v. Peavy


No. 01-92-00683-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1797



July 21, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
July 21, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 334th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-06853.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a concrete truck chute operator, sought review of a take-nothing judgment that the 334th District Court, Harris County, Texas, entered on a jury verdict in the negligence action that appellant brought against appellees, a truck owner and a truck driver, for personal injuries he sustained while working. The trial court denied appellant's motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a concrete truck chute operator, challenged the take-nothing judgment that was entered against the negligence claim that appellant brought against appellees, a truck owner and a truck driver. On appeal, the court affirmed the take-nothing judgment. Appellant failed to preserve for review issues related to the appointment of the visiting judge, pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code Ann §§ 74.041-.062. Appellant could not raise issues related to jury misconduct because he did not comply with Tex. R. Civ. P. 327. The trial court properly based its Batson rulings on whether the jury strikes were race-neutral. The trial court did not err in admitting a letter from appellant's former attorney because the letter was admissible as non-hearsay under Tex. R. Civ. Evid. 801(e)(2) as a vicarious admission by a party-opponent. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that appellant's foreman was not qualified to render an expert opinion. Appellant could not complain about the admission into evidence of an insurance adjuster's notes because appellant read the contents of the notes to the jury. The jury's verdict was not against the great weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that was entered on the jury verdict, which found that appellees, a truck owner and a truck driver, were not liable for negligently causing injuries sustained by appellant, a concrete truck chute operator. The trial court did not err in admitting or excluding evidence or in denying appellant's motion for new trial. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict.

 

1248 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hogan v. Hallman


No. B14-92-00989-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


889 S.W.2d 332; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1802



July 21, 1994, Rendered  
July 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-021526.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant children challenged the decision of the 11th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment against them in their claim for medical malpractice against appellees, hospital and doctors, arising out of the death of their mother. The issue was whether their action was barred by a statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant children were five years old when their mother died at appellee hospital. At age 18, they sued appellees, hospital and doctors, for malpractice. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees, based on the statute of limitations. On appeal, the court first determined that the wrongful death statute of limitations applied to the case, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003(b) (1986). Appellants' action was barred under that statute in the absence of a tolling provision. The court held that the tolling provision in the statute of limitations for the medical malpractice statute applied, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1993). Because appellants had not brought the action before they turned 14, the action was barred. The result did not violate the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, §13. The court stated that it was bound by a Texas supreme court decision, so it held that the result did not violate appellants' due process or equal protection rights under either the United States Constitution or the Texas Constitution. However, in strong dicta, the court explained its disapproval of that precedent. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that appellant children had not filed their action against appellees, hospital and doctors, within the limitations period. The statute of limitations for wrongful death actions applied. The limited tolling provision for the period of minority in the Medical Liability Act also governed. The result did not violate the open courts provision of the Texas Constitution, or any other of appellant's constitutional rights.

 

1249 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fant v. State


No. A14-94-00013-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


881 S.W.2d 830; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1814



July 21, 1994, Rendered  
July 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted October 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 675,838.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convict sought review of the denial by the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), of appellant's application for a writ of habeas corpus to consider whether double jeopardy barred appellant's trial for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The state had obtained a forfeiture judgment that arose out of the same criminal occurrence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied appellant's application for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellant had asserted that double jeopardy barred appellant's trial for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, which was brought after the state had already obtained a forfeiture judgment that arose out of the same criminal occurrence. The court reversed and rendered judgment that appellant's application was granted. The court found that forfeiture of property was readily characterized as punishment. The court reviewed the history of forfeitures and found that they traditionally had been viewed as punishment. The court noted that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 59.02(c)(2) (1994) contained an innocent owner defense, which indicated the legislature's intent to impose forfeiture as a penalty, making the forfeiture look more like punishment. The court found that the distinction between the labels criminal and civil were distinctions without a difference because a civil sanction constituted punishment when its application served the goals of punishment. The court held that appellant's trial violated U.S. Const. amend. V, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 14.


OUTCOME: A denial of an application for a writ of habeas corpus was reversed and rendered because forfeitures had historically been viewed as punishment, because the language of the governing statute indicated legislative intent that forfeitures was considered punishment, and because civil sanctions were punishment if they served the goals of punishment.

Speer v. State


No. 01-92-00908-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


890 S.W.2d 87; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1705



July 14, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
July 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 598,119.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence in the verdict and the constitutionality of the sentence imposed from the 183rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of capital murder for remuneration and permitted testimony that was excludable hearsay.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a juvenile, was convicted of capital murder for remuneration and sentenced to life imprisonment. Appellant sought review and argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, that the statutory punishment was unconstitutional, and inadmissible hearsay testimony was permitted at trial. The court found that appellant's confession and circumstantial evidence of his state of mind established that he murdered the victim for the promise of money. The court found that the admission of the witness testimony was error because it did not serve to further the conspiracy to murder the victim for remuneration, but the error made no contribution to appellant's conviction. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence because there was sufficient evidence for a rational trier of fact to have found that appellant killed the victim for the promise of remuneration and the statutory life sentence imposed was constitutional because the statutory sentence of the death penalty for adult offenders of appellant's crime was constitutional and appellant's mandatory life sentence did not make him ineligible for parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder and the constitutionality of the mandatory life sentence imposed by the trial court because there was sufficient evidence for a rational trier of fact to have found that appellant killed the victim for the promise of remuneration, and the jury considered mitigating factors when it rendered its verdict and appellant's mandatory life sentence did not make him ineligible for parole.

Morris v. Collins


No. 01-94-00289-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


881 S.W.2d 138; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1712



July 14, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
July 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 12th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 18,410.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the 12th District Court, Walker County (Texas) that denied his petition for a writ of injunction in his effort to enjoin appellee criminal justice director from enforcing Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 501.014(e), which authorized appellee to withdraw funds from an inmate's account to pay specific court-ordered fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate sought to enjoin appellee criminal justice director from enforcing Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 501.014(e), which permitted him to withdraw funds from appellant's account to pay court ordered fees. When the trial court denied his petition for a writ of injunction, appellant sought review. The court found that the elements necessary to be entitled to injunctive relief were the existence of a wrongful act, the existence of imminent harm, the existence of irreparable injury, and the absence of an adequate remedy at law. It reiterated that the fear or apprehension or the possibility of injury was not sufficient. During the trial, appellant admitted that appellee had not even attempted or threatened to levy his account. Neither did he present evidence that suggested that this was the future intent of appellee much less that it was imminent. The court concluded that because appellant's harm was speculative, it was proper to deny his request for an injunction. The court affirmed the denial of appellant's petition for a writ of injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant inmate's petition for a writ of injunction, finding that he was unable to show the existence of irreparable injury because whether appellee criminal justice director would have attempted to withdraw funds from appellant's account was purely speculative.

Dokmanovic v. Schwarz


No. B14-93-00041-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


880 S.W.2d 272; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1754



July 14, 1994, Rendered  
July 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 309th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-030414. John Montgomery, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of the decision of the 309th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which enforced the antenuptial agreement made between appellant and appellee former wife when the court granted their divorce.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former husband and appellee former wife signed an antenuptial agreement, and an amendment the day after their marriage, which provided that income or increases to their separate property would remain the separate property of each party. Appellant challenged the enforcement of the agreement by the trial court in rendering its final divorce decree. Appellant claimed that the agreement was unconstitutional under Texas Constitution, art. XVI, § 15, and that it was unenforceable in appellant's case. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the antenuptial agreement was a valid exchange of income that was to be acquired by the parties during marriage. The court found that no property had been acquired during marriage using commingled funds and that the agreement did not violate Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 15. The court rejected appellant's discovery complaint because he failed to preserve it for review under Tex. R. App. P. 52(a). The court also held that their pleadings were sufficient evidence to establish residency of the parties.


OUTCOME: The enforcement of the antenuptial agreement was affirmed because it was constitutional, operated to keep the parties' separate property separate, and no property fell outside its terms because no property was acquired using commingled funds during the marriage. The appellant former husband and appellee former wife satisfied the residency requirement for presentation of issues in the trial court by admissions in their pleadings.

Fonseca v. State


NOS. 13-93-029-CR, 13-93-030-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI

July 14, 1994, Delivered  
July 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 156th District Court of Live Oak County, Texas


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of their convictions by the 156th District Court of Live Oak County (Texas), for aggravated possession of marihuana, and complained of the trial court's charge to the jury, denial of their motion to suppress, and failure to grant exceptions to the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted for aggravated possession of marihuana. They elected jury sentencing. On appeal, they complained that the trial court erred: in instructing the jury under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4, 2 (1994); in refusing to grant defendants' motion to suppress; and in refusing to grant exceptions to the indictment. On appeal, the court affirmed defendants' conviction, but reversed and remanded for resentencing. The court held that there was probable cause to search the motor home where the drugs were found, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1404 (1997), and that the indictments were sufficient to give the defendants notice of the offense charged and were not fatally defective for failure to allege which type of possession that the state intended to prove. The court used the harmless error test to determine whether the trial court's Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1994), instruction, which incorrectly stated the good conduct time rule, had influenced the jury. The court held that the facts did not clearly demonstrate that the jury instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, and therefore remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions, but reversed and remanded for resentencing, because the court could not determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the trial court's erroneous jury instruction as to good conduct time made no contribution to the punishment imposed upon defendants.

Hart v. Berko, Inc.


No. 08-93-00083-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


881 S.W.2d 502; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1783



July 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 24, 1994. As Corrected August 31, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 3 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 91-12977). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Jack Ferguson



DISPOSITION: Having overruled all of Appellants' points of error and Berko's cross-point, judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance agency sought review of a judgment entered against it by the El Paso County Court at Law No. 3 (Texas), which granted appellee insured actual and treble damages under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art 21.21 (1994) and the Texas Deceptive Trade Practices Act. Appellee brought a cross-point seeking review of the trial court's failure to impose treble prejudgment interest damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellee insured brought suit against appellant insurance agency under the Texas Deceptive Trade Practices Act and the Texas Insurance Code for damages arising out of a dispute over representations concerning the amount of fire insurance coverage in effect at the time of a fire loss. The trial court awarded appellee treble damages under the Texas Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.46 and Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21. Appellant sought review, claiming that there was insufficient evidence of misrepresentation and that an unlisted violation of Tex. Bus. & Com. Code § 17.46 did not trigger the mandatory treble damages provision of Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21, § 16. The court affirmed, holding that appellee had established that her damages were factually caused by appellant's misrepresentation, because she did not need to prove reliance on the misrepresentation. As to the treble damages, the court held that art. 21.21, § 16 did not allow recovery for nothing more than a false or misleading practice under § 17.46. However, the court stated that appellant did not adequately apprise the trial court of this error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellee insured and also overruled appellee's cross-point. The court held that appellee established that her damages were factually caused by appellant insurance agency's employee's misrepresentation. The court further held that appellee had specifically pled a claim for treble damages, as required by statute, and that appellant did not properly preserve error with the trial court.


 

1255 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brumit v. State


No. 05-92-02325-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3488



July 13, 1994, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court No. 3. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 3-812-91.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the County Court, Collin County (Texas), which convicted her for harassment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed she was improperly convicted for harassment based on insufficient evidence. She also contended that the harassment statute was void for vagueness, overbroad, and an impermissible prior restraint of protected speech. On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed the conviction. The evidence showed that appellant placed frequent telephone calls to a third party for several months after learning of that party's romantic involvement with appellant's husband. The calls were constant, vulgar, and threatening, and appellant initially identified herself during the calls, but later she also made anonymous calls that were traced. Further, appellant failed to show that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(4) (Supp. 1994) was void for vagueness or violated U.S. Const. amend. V, XIV, or Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. In particular, the use of the word "repeated" in the statute was not vague and did not fail to provide sufficient guidance. The statute was neither overbroad nor a prior restraint on free speech, as it imposed no pre-speech sanction. Punishment assessed pursuant to the statute occurs subsequent to the proscribed speech and, therefore, was not a prior restraint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's harassment conviction, as there was sufficient evidence of repeated annoying calls to a third party. Appellant failed to show that the harassment law was unconstitutional.

Minnesota Mining & Mfg. Co. v. Nishika Ltd.

May 10, 1994, Submitted

June 30, 1994, Filed

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant photographic materials manufacturing company sought relief from the adverse judgment of the 60th District Court, Jefferson County, Texas, in favor of appellee manufacturers of photographic products in an action that arose pursuant to appellant's sale of certain materials to appellees, which allegedly resulted in appellant's breach of warranties pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 336.2-318 (Supp. 1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant photographic materials manufacturing company sought relief from an adverse jury verdict finding that appellant had breached contract warranties to appellee photographic product manufacturers, appellant's customers. The litigation arose pursuant to appellant's sale of certain materials, emulsion, and backcoat sauce used in photographs produced by appellees. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that there was a complete ground of recovery from appellant photographic materials manufacturing company's liability toward appellee manufacturers of photographic products based on three different and distinct breaches of warranty: (1) implied warranty of merchantability; (2) implied warranty of fitness for a particular purpose; and (3) express warranty.

Autry v. State


No. 05-92-01999-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3602



June 30, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 283rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-62737-T.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 283rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, that convicted and sentenced him for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(b)(1992).


OVERVIEW: An undercover police officer was sold cocaine by appellant's step-daughter after appellant offered the drugs and took the officer to the apartment where the sale was made. Pursuant to a search warrant, appellant was arrested and the drugs were seized. A jury convicted and sentenced appellant for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(b)(1992). On appeal, the court affirmed the order, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict because appellant made the contraband available to the officer and did not have to handle the contraband in order to be convicted as a party. The court did not reach the issue of whether the assessment of a fine in addition to a jail sentence violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions because the fines were not the cause of appellant's confinement. The court concluded that, based on the evidence, the fine and sentence were not grossly disproportionate to the offense committed and any improper comments by the prosecutor were not calculated to inflame the jurors' minds and therefore did not require a reversal of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing appellant for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance because evidence was sufficient to support the verdict and any improper prosecutorial comments did not require a reversal.

Schultz v. State


NO. 07-93-0085-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


879 S.W.2d 377; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1530



June 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted October 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 3 OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 91-486805; HONORABLE MACKEY K. HANCOCK, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged the judgment from the County Court at Law No. 3 of Lubbock County (Texas), which convicted her under Tex. Penal Code § 22.041 (1989 & 1994) of abandonment of a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant left her child and another child living with them alone in her house. During this time a fire was started in the house resulting in the death of her child. The fire was started by children playing with matches. Appellant was convicted of abandonment of a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.041 (1989 & 1994). The court affirmed her conviction, holding that appellant's contention that the charging instrument failed to allege a culpable mental state was waived by her failure to object before trial as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.14(b). The court also held that § 22.041 only required proof that defendant intended to abandon a child, and that the culpable mental state did not have to be connected with the circumstances surrounding the conduct. The court finally held that the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict, as her behavior toward the children as observed by coworkers and neighbors, her extended absences from the house even after her ex-husband threatened to blow it up, and her failure to change the batteries on the smoke alarm, all supported a finding that she had exposed the child to an unreasonable risk of harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that appellant criminal defendant failed to preserve her claim of error regarding the information, that the jury charge comported with the clear and unambiguous statute under which she was charged, and the evidence was sufficient to support her conviction.

Shoulders v. State


No. 01-93-00243-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1493



June 23, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied and Supplemental Opinion of August 4, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1951. Appellants' Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied February 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 627036.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged the decision of the 337th District Court Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of possession of a firearm by a felon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant challenged his conviction of possession of a firearm by a felon. Appellant contended that the trial court erred by refusing to suppress the gun as evidence that was obtained from an illegal detention. Appellant argued that the detention was illegal because a seatbelt law was arbitrarily enforced against him. The court determined that appellant had not preserved this error because appellant failed to raise the issue during the suppression hearing or trial. Appellant also alleged that the gun should have been suppressed because it was obtained by an illegal search of his automobile when impoundment was not required. The court noted that an automobile may be validly impounded and inventoried when the driver is removed from his automobile and arrested an no other alternatives were available to ensure protection of the car. The court also determined that it was permissible for the trial court to use both of appellant's convictions to support habitual enhancement because the involuntary manslaughter was not used as an element in the primary offense. Accordingly, the court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's conviction and sentence because the court found that the officer properly arrested appellant and impounded his vehicle and the trial court did not err in admitting the gun that was found as a result of an inventory search of the automobile.

 

1263 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Cuington v. State


No. 05-93-00523-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3838



June 22, 1994, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 363rd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-70187-SW.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review a decision from the 363rd District Court, Dallas County (Texas), convicting appellant of capital murder and assessing a life sentence after the state waived the death penalty. The state relied on an accomplice witness's testimony in its case in chief, and appellant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction independent of the accomplice witness's testimony.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and was assessed a life sentence after the state waived the death penalty. As part of its case in chief, the state called an accomplice witness to testify. On appeal, the court held that other evidence, exclusive of the accomplice witness's testimony, tended to connect appellant to the murder as required under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.14 (1979). Appellant admitted that his gun was used to kill the victim prior to police awareness of the crime, he admitted that he was with the accomplice witness near the time of the offense, and his fingerprint was found on the victim's car door. The prosecutor never represented that he did not have to prove his case to the jury beyond a reasonable doubt. An instruction to disregard the prosecutor's remarks could have cured any harm if appellant had objected at trial. Even if appellant had objected to his belief that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071, § 1 (1993) was unconstitutional, appellant's point was without merit because there was no requirement for individualized capital sentencing. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder finding no reversible error. The evidence, independent of an accomplice witness's testimony, tended to connect appellant to the murder. The prosecutor never represented in his jury argument that he did not have to prove his case to the jury beyond a reasonable doubt. The burden was on appellant to object at trial to the alleged unconstitutionality of a mandatory sentencing statute.

 

1264 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lackey v. State


No. 05-92-01786-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


881 S.W.2d 418; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2045



June 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 363rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F-9202798-MW



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her conviction from the 363rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), for theft of property valued at $ 750 or less while having been previously convicted two or more times of theft, arguing that the sentence was cruel and unusual punishment. Appellant was caught shoplifting clothing with a fair market value of $ 145.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged her conviction for theft of property valued at $ 750 or less while having been previously convicted two or more times, arguing that the sentence was cruel and unusual punishment. Appellant was caught shoplifting clothing with a fair market value of $ 145. Absent any other criminal record, the offense was a misdemeanor, but appellant was previously convicted not only of theft, but also of motor vehicle burglary and robbery. In a range that permitted confinement for life, or for any term of not more than 99 years nor less than 25 years, the trial court assessed 35 years. Appellant claimed that, even with her criminal history, her sentence was disproportionate, but the court held that the sentence was not grossly disproportionate, because the prior theft convictions were elements of her offense under the habitual offender statute, not enhancements. Appellant's extensive criminal record demonstrated a pronounced and prolonged inability to bring her conduct within social norms. Appellant's prior convictions and punishments did not deter her, so the onus of a recidivist punishment was placed upon her, and the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. As a habitual offender, appellant received a sentence at the lower end of the range, and it was not grossly disproportionate to her offense.

Battaile v. Yoffe


No. 01-93-01168-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


882 S.W.2d 13; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1444



June 16, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
June 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 165th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-016232



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision from the 165th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctors; appellant claimed the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10 (1994) was unconstitutional with regard to minors because it violated the "open courts" provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother brought a medical malpractice suit against appellee doctors on behalf of her minor daughter. At the time the suit was brought, the daughter was 15 years old. Appellant claimed appellees were negligent in failing to properly diagnose and treat daughter for certain seizures and apneic episodes that she suffered in the first three days after her birth. Appellees' motions for summary judgment, claiming that appellant's suit was time barred, were granted. Challenging the decision, appellant claimed the trial court erred in granting summary judgment because the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10 (1994) was unconstitutional with regard to minors because it violated the "open courts" provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court agreed. Because art. 4590i, § 10 cut off a minor's cause of action before the minor was legally able to assert it, and there was no adequate substitute remedy available to the minor, the court held the article to be unconstitutional as applied to minors. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court.


OUTCOME: Because the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability Act violated the "open courts" provision of the Texas Constitution, the court held it was unconstitutional as applied to minors, reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellees and remanded.

City of Houston v. Harris County Outdoor Advertising Ass'n


NO. A14-92-01123-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


879 S.W.2d 322; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1460



June 16, 1994, Rendered  
June 16, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 281st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 87-00827. Louis M. Moore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city, the sign control board, and its administrator, challenged a judgment of the 281st District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found appellants' fees for off-premise operating permits were an unlawful occupation tax in violation of Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1(f) and provisions of the U. S. Const. Appellee outdoor advertising association and its members were awarded damages and attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellee outdoor sign association and its members challenged the validity of the off-premise operating permit fees levied by appellant city under Houston Sign Code ch. 46. Appellees claimed that appellant city, the sign control board, and its administrator violated their constitutional rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Following the enactment of Houston Ord. 89-767 (1989), that doubled the permit fee, appellees amended their petition and alleged the fees were an unlawful tax in violation of the Tex. Const. and the U. S. Const. The trial court rendered judgment for appellees and awarded damages and attorney's fees. Appellants challenged the ruling. The court affirmed and found that the permit fees were so excessive as to constitute an unlawful occupation tax. The court found no direct relationship between the fees and the receipt of services. The fees exceeded the reasonable costs of regulation. The court held that appellant city committed multiple constitutional violations, including violation of appellees' due process rights under U. S. Const. amend. XIV. Accordingly, the court granted recovery to appellees under § 1983 together with an award of attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that appellant city, the sign control board, and its administrator, charged appellee outdoor sign association and its members off-premise operating permit fees that were so excessive that the fees were an unlawful occupation tax in violation of the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court found no direct relationship between the permit fees and the services received.

 

1267 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Vickers v. State


NO. 2-92-362-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


878 S.W.2d 329; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1424



June 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 7, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 6 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Rufus Adcock



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from County Criminal Court No. Six of Tarrant County (Texas) that convicted him of driving while intoxicated. Appellant claimed that the videotape of his custodial statements made before he was given his Miranda rights violated his rights against self-incrimination under U.S. Const. amend. V, Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. §§ 38.21, 38.22 and 38.23.


OVERVIEW: After appellant had a car accident, police officers conducted field sobriety tests on him, and took him to the police station where they videotaped him performing other sobriety tests before giving him his Miranda rights. As a result, appellant was convicted of driving under the influence. On appeal, the court held that because the videotape showed that appellant was mentally confused when he responded to the tests, and because his mental state was at issue, appellant's responses were testimonial. Thus, because no Miranda warnings were given before the tests were performed, and because appellant's imprecise objection to the videotape did not waive error because the correct grounds for the objection were obvious, the admission of the videotape violated appellant's rights against self incrimination under U.S. Const. amend. V, Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. §§ 38.21, 38.22 and 38.23. However, because there was enough other evidence to support the verdict so that the exclusion of the videotape would not have affected the verdict, the error in admitting it was harmless. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for driving under the influence. The court held that the videotape of appellant's responses to sobriety tests that was made before he was given his Miranda rights violated his rights against self incrimination because it showed his confused mental state and his mental state was at issue. However, because sufficient other evidence supported the verdict, the admission of the videotape was harmless error.

Deep E. Tex. Regional Mental Health Mental Retardation Servs. v. Kinnear


No. 09-93-316 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


877 S.W.2d 550; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1398


May 5, 1994, Submitted  
June 9, 1994, Delivered  
June 9, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 1st District Court. Jasper County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 16,299. Hon. Joe Bob Golden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant service agency contested the injunctions issued by the 1st District Court, Jasper County, Texas, which prohibited appellant from constructing a community home in a particular subdivision to house six mentally disabled women. Appellee property owner prevailed in his action to enforce restrictive covenants that limited the use of lots in his subdivision to one-family residences and precluded uses that may become an annoyance or nuisance.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owner sought injunctive relief prohibiting the construction of a community home by appellant service agency, which was to be used to house six mentally disabled women under continual staff supervision. The trial court issued temporary and permanent injunctions prohibiting its construction, on the reasoning that restrictive covenants governing use of subdivision property precluded use for anything but one-family residences, and barred activities that may become offensive, an annoyance, or a nuisance to the neighborhood. On appeal, the court reversed and dissolved the injunctions, holding that the trial court abused its discretion in granting the requested relief. After thoroughly reviewing applicable state and federal law, and constitutional guarantees of equal protection, the court sustained the points of error urged by appellant on the basis that the evidence presented at trial was legally insufficient to support the trial court's judgment. The court emphasized that its holding was independently grounded on statutory law and constitutional considerations, separate and apart from its finding of legal insufficiency.


OUTCOME: The court held that no restrictive covenant or deed restriction can deny or limit the ability of qualified disabled persons to live anywhere they choose in Texas. Concluding that the trial court abused its discretion in ordering a permanent injunction against the construction and operation of the proposed home, the court sustained appellant's points of error on the basis of legal insufficiency, and rendered judgment dissolving the injunctions.

Dallas County v. Sweitzer


No. 05-93-00056-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


881 S.W.2d 757; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2086



May 31, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 14th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-9914-A.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and RENDERED in part, AFFIRMED as MODIFIED in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county and appellee individuals moved for a rehearing of an appeal of a judgment from the 14th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which imposed four-fold penalties against appellant under Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 51.321 for the unlawful collection of court fees and enjoined appellant from further unauthorized fee collections.


OVERVIEW: The court denied both parties' motions for rehearing of an appeal of a judgment favoring appellee individuals which found that appellant county overcharged and collected fees not authorized by law. The court withdrew its prior opinion and held that the trial court erred in applying Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 51.321, which authorized four-fold penalties, to fees appellant collected at filing and in awarding penalties on a law library fee, alternative dispute resolution (ADR) fee, appellate fee, sheriff fee, court reporter fee, and a portion of the clerk fee. Tex. Gov't. Code Ann. § 51.601 and the practice of depositing the sheriff fee in the general revenue fund violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. Tex. Local Gov't. Code Ann. § 118.131 did not authorize the collection of a sheriff fee at the time of filing because there was no evidence of any service provided that the fee supported. The trial court properly enjoined appellant from collecting the court reporter and sheriff fees, but erred by enjoining appellant from collecting the law library fee, a portion of the clerk fee, and the ADR fee. The injunction was affirmed modified.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment that imposed four-fold penalties against appellant county in appellee individuals' suit alleging the improper collection of court fees. The court affirmed the injunction enjoining appellant from further improper collections as modified to remove the proscription against collection of the law library fee, a portion of the clerk fee, and the alternative dispute resolution fee.

Palla v. McDonald


No. 01-93-00078-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


877 S.W.2d 472; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1239



May 26, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
May 26, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 189th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-04761-A.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former patient sought review of a summary judgment from the 189th District Court, Harris County, Texas in favor of appellee doctor that her medical malpractice action was barred by the statute of limitations. Appellant contended that the limitations period in the Medical Liability Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i § 10.01 (Supp. 1994) was unconstitutional as applied to her and that her mental competency was a fact issue.


OVERVIEW: In her third amended petition filed 28 months after she commenced her medical malpractice action, appellant former patient added appellee doctor. Appellant had developed brain damage when she was treated for abdominal pain. Appellee was granted summary judgment based on the two-year statute of limitations in the Medical Liability Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i § 10.01 (Supp. 1994). On appeal, the court noted that the precursor to § 10.01 was held to violate the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 where it barred a medical malpractice action by a plaintiff who had remained continuously mentally incompetent from the injury until the action was commenced. In such a case, the limitation period was tolled. Because there was fact issue as to whether appellant remained continuously mentally incompetent, the court reversed summary judgment for appellee and remanded the cause. The court rejected appellee's claim that appellant's mental state was irrelevant because she filed her action within the two-year period adding him after it expired. The court held that the mere commencement of an action by a legally incapacitated person did not deny the tolling protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment for appellee doctor who was added to a medical malpractice action 28 months after appellant former patient commenced her suit. Because the two-year limitation period violated the open courts provision of the state constitution by barring an action by a plaintiff who was continuously mentally incompetent, the court remanded the cause to determine whether appellant's mental state tolled the limitations period.

Covalt v. State


No. 01-91-01066-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


877 S.W.2d 445; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1159



MAY 19, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
May 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number 9. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9109909.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction by the County Criminal Court at Law Number Nine, Harris County, Texas for perjury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a sworn statement that falsely accused an officer with official misconduct. The court determined that because appellant had made a sworn statement and there were no other citizens who were similarly situated, appellant had not met her burden of proof as to her contention that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.02 had been discriminatorily applied to her. The court found that appellant had failed to show that the statute constituted inhibition upon constitutionally protected conduct, and was therefore not overbroad. The court determined that appellant was not entitled to an instruction as to her belief at the time the statement was made because the state did not have to prove that she believed the statement to have been false. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, having determined that appellant had not shown that the perjury statute constituted any inhibition upon constitutionally protected conduct, and that the state did not have the burden to show appellant knew the statement to be false when it was made.

 

1272 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Green Int'l v. State


No. 3-92-637-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


877 S.W.2d 428; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1182



May 18, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 22, 1994. Released for Publication June 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURTS OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH & 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICTS, NOS. 92-01387 & 93-06886, HONORABLE MARY PEARL WILLIAMS & HONORABLE MARGARET COOPER, JUDGES PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of judgments from the 167th & 299th Judicial District Courts, Travis County Texas, which sustained appellee state's claims of sovereign immunity and dismissed appellant's suits for breach of contract, interference with ability to perform under the contract, taking without adequate compensation, and quantum meruit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contractor's suit for breach of contract, interference with ability to perform under the contract, taking without adequate compensation, and quantum meruit was twice dismissed due to appellee state's claim of sovereign immunity. A legislative resolution granted appellant permission to bring the second suit, but the governor later vetoed the resolution. On appeal, the court affirmed the rulings because although appellee waived its immunity from liability when it entered into the contract, it retained its immunity from suit. Appellant did not allege that appellee acted with the specific intent to take appellant's property for public use and appellant consented to appellee's possession of the property. Therefore, there was no valid taking claim that waived immunity. Nor was immunity waived by the resolution because the governor never approved it as required by Tex. Const. art. IV, §15. The open-courts provision of the state constitution was not applicable to redress appellant's rights because appellant's claims would not have been cognizable at common law and sovereign immunity was not an unreasonable restriction on appellant's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments because the resolution that waived appellee state's sovereign immunity was not approved by the governor and appellee retained its immunity from suit. Appellant contractor did not allege a valid taking claim that would have waived appellee's immunity.

 

1273 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Garth v. Staktek Corp.


No. 3-93-560-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


876 S.W.2d 545; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1183



May 18, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-07974, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 6, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 771.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), which granted appellee's motion for a temporary injunction to protect trade secrets. Appellant complained that no breach of confidence had occurred, appellee had an adequate remedy at law, the injunction was a prior restraint, federal patent law preempted Texas trade secret law, and appellee was guilty of laches.


OVERVIEW: The parties had formerly collaborated on certain technology. When this effort ended, appellant agreed not to use or disclose the technology developed by appellee, except to the extent it became public domain. Appellant began working on a competing product using the trade secrets. Appellee applied for patents, and an abstract of the technology was published. Finding no abuse of discretion in the grant of an injunction, the court affirmed the order. Appellant had made commercial use of the technology simply by attempting to develop a competing product that incorporated the protected information. Injunctive relief was appropriate to prevent appellant from gaining unfair advantage. Lost opportunity to create or gain control of a new market could result in irreparable harm. While this injunction was similar to prior restraint, even prior restraint was not unconstitutional if it was the only means of preventing irreparable harm. State trade secret laws generally were not preempted by patent law if they were not aimed exclusively at the promotion of the invention itself. Generally, not filing a lawsuit at the earliest opportunity was not laches.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that issued an injunction against appellant. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in issuing the injunction, because appellee had demonstrated that it was entitled to relief to protect its trade secrets, the injunction was not unconstitutional, the action was not preempted by federal law, and appellee had not committed laches.

FERGUSON v. MELLON BANK, N.A.


No. 05-92-02459-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3565



May 16, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 160th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-1679-H.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 160th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), granting a judgement not withstanding the verdict in favor of appellee in appellant's counterclaim alleging constructive eviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellee bank brought suit alleging breach of contract. Appellant counter claimed for constructive eviction and for other claims. The jury awarded appellee damages and attorney's fees. The jury also found in favor of appellant on constructive eviction and awarded appellant attorney's fees. The trial court disregarded appellant's favorable answers and entered final judgment in favor of appellee. The court affirmed, reasoning that the jury's answer on constructive eviction was immaterial because it had no effect on the damages that the jury found or on the amount of the judgment. The court rejected several of appellant's claims that were based on the evidence being insufficient concerning appellee's claim for past-due rent. The court reasoned that appellant failed to meet the standards of Tex. R. Civ. P. 93(2), which required verification of allegations that appellee was not entitled to recover in the capacity in which it sued. The court also held that the record contained no evidence of bona fide error on the part of the trial court. The court found that, as a matter of law, appellant was not entitled to attorney's fees based under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-11.05.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court granting a judgement not withstanding the verdict in favor of appellee. The court reasoned that it was proper for the trial court to disregard the jury decision in favor of appellant's counterclaim because the issue was immaterial after the jury found appellant breached its lease.

Mayo v. State


No. 01-93-00566-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


877 S.W.2d 385; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1097



May 12, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
May 12, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number Two. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9320158.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Criminal Court of Harris County (Texas), convicting appellant of operating a sexually oriented business without a permit pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 243.003(a). The trial court assessed punishment at six months' confinement, probated for one year, and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Police investigated a video store for a possible violation of a sexually oriented business ordinance pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 243.003(a). The store did not have an application or permit authorizing it to operate a sexually oriented business. When a police officer entered the store he noticed appellant working behind the counter. The police officer saw video cases that displayed sexually explicit videos. He asked appellant if the sexually explicit videos were for sale and rent, and appellant replied that they were. Appellant was convicted of operating a sexually oriented business without a permit. The trial court assessed punishment at six months' confinement, probated for one year, and a fine. Appellant contended the trial court erred in finding him guilty because there was no evidence that he personally displayed merchandise, goods, entertainment, or other services offered at the store. He also argued that there was no evidence that the video boxes contained any merchandise, goods, or entertainment. The appellate court affirmed the order because appellant was in control of the store and of the sexually explicit videos located behind the counter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of operating a sexually oriented business without a permit because the evidence showed that sexually explicit videos were displayed in the store where appellant worked. That evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding of appellant's guilt. In addition, the ordinance regarding the offense provided clear and adequate warning of the proscribed conduct.

 

1276 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. State


No. 13-92-679-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


877 S.W.2d 809; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1141



May 12, 1994, Delivered  
May 12, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas. (Tr.Ct.No. CR-1263-90-C)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which convicted appellant for murder, on grounds that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 74.053(b) (1994) was unconstitutional, that the murder charge was not specifically named in the indictment, and that appellant was not properly admonished about the possibility of deportation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to murder before a jury and was assessed a punishment of 80 years in prison. Appellant sought review, but the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 74.053(b) (1994) was constitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because the classification between civil and criminal litigants regarding the recusal of assigned former judges was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. Although the offense of murder was not specifically named when appellant was admonished about the plea, there was no error because appellant was represented by counsel and the indictment allegations were read. The trial court was not required to admonish appellant regarding the purported waiver of the rights to self-incrimination, to trial by jury, and to confront the witnesses. The trial court substantially complied with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(c) when it admonished appellant about the possibility of deportation. The issue of voluntary manslaughter was not raised because appellant did not act under the influence of sudden passion. Appellant waived any error regarding an unnecessary deadly weapon issue in the punishment charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant for murder because the statute regarding the recusal of assigned former judges was rationally related to a legitimate state interest, the murder charge did not have to be specifically named because appellant had counsel and the indictment was read, and appellant was admonished about the possibility of deportation.

Manuel v. State


No. A14-92-00877-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1056



May 5, 1994, Rendered  
May 5, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 593050.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted and sentenced him for the felony offense of escape, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.07 (1989), and possession of a controlled substance, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with escape, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.07 (1989), and possession of a controlled substance, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115 (1992). Appellant was found guilty of the controlled substance charge and pleaded guilty to the offense of escape. The trial court assessed punishment accordingly. On review, appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and the constitutionality of various sections of the state penal code. Appellant also claimed ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court affirmed. The evidence was sufficient to convict appellant because he pled guilty to charges in the indictment, stipulated to the evidence, and signed a waiver of rights form. Trial counsel's failure to move to suppress did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel. Tex. Penal Code §§ 38.07(a)(1), 38.09 were not unconstitutional as applied to appellant. Appellant could not complain that failure to apply the exclusionary rule's protections to him was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing appellant for possession of a controlled substance and escape; the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's convictions, appellant was not denied effective assistance of counsel, and various provisions of the state penal code were not unconstitutional as applied to appellant.
