Fuller v. Travelers Indem. Co.


No. 09-92-144 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


874 S.W.2d 958; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1016



April 28, 1994, Delivered  
April 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Filed April 28, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 58th District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. A-117,255F. Hon. J. Michael Bradford, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of December 16, 1993, Previously Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3371.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the District Court of Jefferson County (Texas), which granted appellees' motion for summary judgment in an action brought by appellant alleging appellees were negligent because they failed to alleviate the health and safety hazards at the refinery where appellant's father worked. The trial court held appellees were immune from liability under the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought suit against appellee carrier and appellee auditor, seeking damages for the death of her father. During his years of employment at an oil refinery, appellant's father was exposed to polynuclear aromatic hydrocarbons. Appellant's father died from adenocarcinoma. Appellee carrier provided workers' compensation benefits to the employees of decedent's employer. Appellee auditor performed safety audits and industrial hygiene surveys at the refinery for appellee carrier. Such audits were conducted as part of the workers' compensation insurance coverage for the plant. Appellant alleged that appellees were negligent and grossly negligent because they failed to take action to alleviate the health and safety hazards present at the employer's facilities or warn her father of their existence, despite appellees' knowledge of numerous health and safety hazards present at the refinery. The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment based on immunity under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306. The appellate court reversed the order, holding that the immunity provision did not override appellant's right of recovery under Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 26.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order granting appellees' motion for summary judgment in an action brought by appellant alleging appellees were negligent because they failed to alleviate the health and safety hazards at the refinery where appellant's father worked. The action was remanded because the immunity provision did not override the constitutional provision under which appellees could be held liable for gross negligence.

Jackson v. State


No. A14-92-00367-CR, No. B14-92-00368-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


880 S.W.2d 432; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 973



April 28, 1994, Rendered  
April 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 7. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 9,210,999 and 9,211,000. Shelley Hancock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the County Court at Law No. 7, Harris County (Texas), entering her convictions for prostitution, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. 43.02(a)(2) (1989), and for conducting business in a sexually oriented enterprise without a permit, in violation of Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. 243.010(b) (1994), Houston, Tex., Code of Ordinances 28-122(a) (1991). Defendant claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a dancer in an adult club. Defendant offered to have sex with an undercover officer for money and was observed performing sexually explicit acts. No permit for the club was displayed. At trial, defendant brought a motion for a directed verdict, which the trial court denied. Defendant was convicted of prostitution and conducting business in a sexually oriented enterprise without a permit, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.02(a)(2) (1989), Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. 243.010(b) (1994), and Houston, Tex., Code of Ordinances 28-122(a) (1991). Defendant appealed, claiming, inter alia, that she did not operate the establishment, the state failed to prove all the elements of the permit offense, and the charging ordinance was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed. Although the information's caption charged defendant with operating a sexually oriented business, the caption was not part of the information, and the error was harmless. There was sufficient evidence to support the conviction. Further, the ordinance was not void for vagueness because the ordinance clearly listed specific acts constituting a violation and detailed the permit application process.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's entry of defendant's conviction for prostitution and conducting a business in a sexually oriented enterprise without a permit. Although the information's caption stated defendant operated the business, the caption was surplusage, and the state was only required to prove defendant conducted business. Because the permit ordinance was clear, it was not void for vagueness and was constitutional.

State by and Through Dep't of Mental Health & Mental Retardation v. Roark


No. 08-93-00322-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


876 S.W.2d 514; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 1006



April 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 109th District Court of Winkler County, Texas. (TC# P-6). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. James Rex


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the judgment of the 109th District Court of Winkler County (Texas), that awarded only a portion of the sought damages to the state in its suit against appellee patient for reimbursement of the costs associated with the support, maintenance, and treatment of appellee while he was judicially committed in a mental health facility.


OVERVIEW: Appellee patient was admitted to a mental health facility that was managed by the state. Appellee was admitted as a non-indigent patient because he did possess some property. After appellee's release, the state presented his legal guardian with a claim for reimbursement of the costs and treatments that were incurred as a result of his stay. Appellee's guardian rejected the state's claim, and the state initiated an action for the outstanding amount due. The lower court only awarded a portion of the entire claim, the state challenged its decision to award the lesser amount, and appellee cross-challenged the sufficiency of the evidence. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the state, but reformed it to include the full amount sought by the state for reimbursement because appellee failed to produce any evidence that was contrary to the copy of the account or the affidavit by the facility's superintendent. The court held that, as a matter of law, the state was entitled to the full amount of its claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court in favor of the state, but reformed the award of damages to the full amount of the state's claim because the state met its burden of proof by providing a copy of appellee patient's account and an affidavit from the superintendent that described the course of treatments and maintenance.

Smith v. State


No. 01-91-00195-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


881 S.W.2d 727; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 887



April 21, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
April 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 557,790.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the judgment from the 183rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted and sentenced him for murder after standing trial as an adult.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was certified to stand trial as an adult and convicted of murder. On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because his oral and written statements were given to officers while in "custody" and, thus, his oral statement was inadmissible pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 38.22 (Supp. 1994), and his written statement was inadmissible pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 52.02(a)(2) and (3) (Supp. 1994). The court held that the record indicated the requisites of § 52.02 were complied with before appellant was interrogated because appellant was taken directly to the police department, which was a designated facility for the temporary detention of juveniles consistent with Tex. Fam. Code Ann. 52.025(a), and administered Miranda warnings in compliance with Tex. Fam. Code Ann. 51.09(b). The court held that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's request for a jury charge on lesser-included offenses or in permitting jurors to take notes. The court rejected appellant's arguments regarding improper prosecutorial closing argument and found that the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of murder, holding that the appellant juvenile's statements were not taken before the requisites of the Texas Family Code had been met, and therefore were admissible. The court held that the trial court properly denied appellant's motion to suppress, request for a jury charge on lesser-included offenses, and motion for a mistrial due to prosecutorial closing argument.

Johnson v. State


No. C14-92-00888-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 913



April 21, 1994, Rendered  
April 21, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Court at Law No. 7. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9207960.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Court at Law No. 7, Harris County, Texas, convicting appellant of possession of a dangerous drug, pursuant to the Texas Health & Safety Code Ann. § 483.001(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of violating a provision of a city ordinance that prohibited self-medication of dangerous drugs, as defined by the Texas Health & Safety Code Ann. § 483.001(3). On appeal, the court rejected appellant's argument that his ignorance about the required prescription for the drug indicated that the statute was intolerably vague where prescription requirement for hundreds of medications constantly varies. The court held that it was a matter of common practice to obtain prescription for certain medications, and the statutory language was sufficient to provide fair notice of the prohibited drug as to uphold its constitutionality. Furthermore, the court held that irrespective of the constitutionality of the ordinance, appellant's initial warrantless arrest was legitimate because appellant's engagement in disorderly conduct provided the probable cause for the arrest. It affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: Order convicting appellant of possession of dangerous drug was affirmed because appellant's ignorance of the prescription requirement for the drug was not valid. The court held that the statutory language gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice that possession of the drug was forbidden.

Riley v. Triplex Communications


No. 09-92-318 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


874 S.W.2d 333; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 815


February 3, 1994, Submitted  
April 14, 1994, Delivered  
April 14, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 136th District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. D-131, 311. Honorable Jack R. King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers sought review of the judgment of the 136th District Court, Jefferson County (Texas), which failed to find that appellees bar, bartender, radio station and station owner were engaged in a civil conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officers filed suit against appellees bar, bartender, radio station and station owner for personal injuries they received in a car accident with a drunk bar patron. The trial court entered judgment against appellees bar and bartender under the dram shop statute, but found that appellees were not engaged in a civil conspiracy. Appellants sought review on grounds that the trial court refused to submit their jury questions regarding joint enterprise, negligent promotion and the definition of civil conspiracy. The court determined that the trial court erred in denying appellants' jury question on joint enterprise, as the evidence in the record sufficiently raised the issue. The court also found that the trial court erred in defining civil conspiracy, which only required that a conspirator intended to engage in a course of conduct, and that where in the intended course of conduct a separate tort is committed, co-conspirators were jointly liable. Further, the court held that the evidence showed that the radio station's promotions induced patrons to drink irresponsibly. Therefore, appellants were entitled to have the issue of negligent promotion to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's rulings denying appellant police officers' requests to submit jury questions on joint enterprise, negligent promotion, and the definition of civil conspiracy. The court held that the trial court erred because the evidence was sufficient on the issues of joint enterprise and on negligent promotion to raise and issue for the jury. The court found that the trial court erroneously defined civil conspiracy.

Railroad Comm'n v. Arco Oil & Gas Co.


No. 3-91-504-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


876 S.W.2d 473; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 808; 128 Oil & Gas Rep. 627



April 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-3140, HONORABLE JAMES R. MEYERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of August 25, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2365.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad commission challenged an order of the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), which declared invalid and enjoined the enforcement of a rule, which was promulgated by appellant to regulate the production of oil wells.


OVERVIEW: Appellant railroad commission adopted rule 90(b)(2), which affected the amount of oil that appellee oil companies could produce from their fields. Appellees filed suit challenging the validity of the rule. The trial court declared the rule invalid and enjoined its enforcement. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did have jurisdiction over the suit because appellees were not required to exhaust administrative remedies before initiating a declaratory judgment action, and the primary-jurisdiction doctrine, which forbid a court decision prior to an administrative tribunal's decision of a question within the tribunal's jurisdiction, did not apply because appellant had made the initial decision by adopting the rule. The court held that because appellees' attack on the validity of the rule included constitutional as well as a reasoned-justification challenge, the trial court did not err in receiving evidence outside the four corners of the order adopting the rule. The court found that the rule was invalid because appellant did not use the required procedure in adopting the rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order declaring appellant railroad commission's rule invalid, finding that appellant did not use the required procedure to adopt the rule, and that the trial court had jurisdiction and did not err in receiving evidence outside the four corners of the order adopting the rule.

Closs v. Goose Creek Consol. Indep. Sch. Dist.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA

DISPOSITION: Finding no error requiring reversal, we affirm the trial court's judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the 269th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), which affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee public employer, in an action brought by appellant for malicious prosecution, invasion of privacy, tortious interference with contract, civil conspiracy, and civil rights violations under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.

Blake v. Blake


No. 13-93-172-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


878 S.W.2d 209; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 775



April 7, 1994, Delivered  
April 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 24th District Court of Goliad County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is, in all things, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the judgment of the 24th District Court of Goliad County (Texas), which awarded support payments to appellee, son of appellant, retroactive to the birth date of appellee in connection with an action commenced by appellee state attorney general, son, and appellee son's mother, to establish the parent-child relationship between appellant and appellee son.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father challenged the trial court's judgment that awarded retroactive support payments to appellee, son of appellant, following a finding of paternity. On review, appellant claimed that the award of retroactive support payments was improper because when appellee son was born neither the law nor social mores held appellant responsible. The court found that during the relevant period, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.09 (1986) provided that the effect of a paternity decree was to create the parent-child relationship as if the child were born during marriage, and that because a parent's duty to support begins at birth, there was no error in awarding support retroactive to appellee son's birth. Appellant claimed that as an indigent, the trial court's failure to provide appointed counsel violated his substantive due process rights. The court held that the child's need in establishing paternity overrode the interests of appellant and that because the evidence did not indicate how assistance of counsel would have mattered, there was no error in failing to appoint counsel. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee son, appellee attorney general and appellee son's mother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellees, attorney general, son of appellant, and the son's mother, because the court ruled that a parent's duty to support begins at birth thus the trial court did not err in ordering retroactive support upon the adjudication of paternity, and because the trial court committed no error in failing to appoint counsel for appellant in that there was no real need for appointed counsel in appellant's case.

Jenicke v. City of Forest Hill


No. 2-92-093-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


873 S.W.2d 776; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 747



April 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 352ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. BRUCE AULD



DISPOSITION: We overrule appellant's points of error and affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a worker and his wife, challenged a decision of the 352nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which entered summary judgment favoring appellee city in appellants' suit alleging negligence and violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellant worker was injured in a gas explosion.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a worker and his wife, filed suit against appellee city for injuries appellant worker sustained in a natural gas explosion. Appellant worker had been sent by his employer, a gas company, to investigate a gas leak reported by appellee's department of public safety. The explosion occurred as appellant worker was trying to determine the extent of damage to a gas meter that had been struck by a car. The court affirmed, holding that appellee was immune from liability for its alleged negligence. Appellants claimed that appellee was negligent in not having more fire trucks, more gas detection equipment, more communications equipment, and a better training program. A governmental unit was not liable under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.012(1), (2) (1986) for such omissions in its actual making of decisions on how much, if any, fire protection to provide for a community. Appellee's alleged policy of inadequately training its safety officers was not arbitrary or conscience shocking in a constitutional sense. Appellant's claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 were really negligence claims. The facts did not support a seizure under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of summary judgment for appellee city in a suit by appellants, a worker and his wife, for injuries sustained by appellant worker in a gas explosion. Appellee was immune from negligence liability because it was a governmental unit and was not liable for omissions in its actual making of decisions regarding how much fire protection to provide a community. There was no seizure of appellant under the Fourth Amendment.

Charles v. Tamez


No. 13-93-452-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


878 S.W.2d 201; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 783



March 31, 1994, Delivered  
March 31, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 107th District Court of Cameron County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment denying turnover.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and on behalf of decedent's estate, sought review of the order of the 107th District Court of Cameron County (Texas), denying her request for turnover of two causes of action in an attempt to collect on the judgment that she was awarded against appellee tortfeasor in an underlying case for injuries sustained by and the wrongful death of decedent.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, individually and on behalf of decedent's estate, sued appellee tortfeasor for damages resulting from the personal injuries and wrongful death of decedent in a car accident. After prevailing at trial, appellant tried to collect on the judgment but found that appellee had no exempt assets. Appellant sought turnover of causes of action appellee had a right to pursue against his insurer and against his attorneys for their failure to accept a settlement offer. Appellant's request was denied. Appellant sought review of the denial of her request for turnover. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred when it allowed appellee's attorneys to intervene and in denying turnover of the causes of action against his insurer and his attorneys. The court affirmed and declined to rule on the intervention issue. The court did note that, even if intervention was improper, there was no causal connection between the intervention and the judgment complained of. The court held that the turnover statute did not apply to appellant's claims because unasserted, denied causes of action for legal malpractice for failure to settle were not assets subject to turnover.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order that denied the request for turnover of two causes of action filed by appellant, individually and on behalf of decedent's estate, in her attempt to collect the judgment she received against appellant tortfeasor in an underlying case. The court held that the unasserted causes of action for malpractice, for which appellant sought turnover, were not the kind of assets subject to turnover.

 

1292 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Black v. Dallas County Bail Bond Bd.


No. 05-93-01037-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


882 S.W.2d 434; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2239



March 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 162nd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-4984-I



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety companies challenged an order of the 162nd District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee bail bond board in appellants' action for declaratory judgment regarding the validity of a local rule promulgated by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant surety companies brought a declaratory judgment action against appellee bail bond board regarding the validity of a local rule, which allowed the sheriff's department to make the final determination of rearrest costs to be paid by appellants. Upon cross-motions for summary judgment, the trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee, holding that the rule was valid. The appellate court reversed and rendered judgment in favor of appellants, holding that two sections of the local rule violated the separation of power provision of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. In so ruling, the appellate court stated that the judiciary was granted the power to determine the amount of rearrest costs by the legislature, and cited Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 22.16, 22.17 (1989). However, the appellate court also ruled that appellee did not exceed its authority in promulgating the local rule, because appellee was authorized to enact rules pertaining to any phase of the bail bonding business, which included liability for, and collection of, rearrest costs.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee bail bond board, and rendered judgment in favor of appellant surety companies, because a local rule violated the separation of powers provision of the Texas Constitution because it allowed the sheriff's department to make the final determination of the amount of rearrest costs, which power had been given to the judiciary by the legislature.

 

1293 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Cyr v. Tompkins


No. 05-93-00850-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3302



March 30, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 116th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-1337-F.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant picketers sought interlocutory review and challenged the constitutionality of the temporary injunctions granted by the 116th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, that limited the time, place, and manner of appellants' picketing in the neighborhood of appellees, physician and his wife.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted appellee, physician and wife, temporary injunctions that limited the time, place, and manner of picketing by appellant picketers. Appellants sought interlocutory review but did not file a statement of facts from the hearing for the temporary injunctions. Appellants argued that appellees did not meet the legal requirements for a temporary injunction and the injunctions violated U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held that because appellants failed to file a statement of facts, it presumed that sufficient evidence was introduced to support the entry of the injunctions, to establish actual injury to appellees, and to establish appellees prima facie case. The court ruled that peaceful picketing was not absolutely protected by U.S. Const. amend. I or Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, but was subject to reasonable, content neutral, time-place-manner restrictions. The court affirmed the issuance of the temporary injunctions because the injunctions were content neutral on their face, and without a statement of facts, appellants' failed to show that the restrictions had an unconstitutional chilling effect on their right of free speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the issuance of the temporary injunctions in favor of appellee, physician and wife, because the injunctions were content neutral on their face and without a statement of facts, appellant picketers failed to show that the time, place, and manner restrictions in the injunctions had an unconstitutional chilling effect on their First Amendment right of free speech.

White v. State


No. B14-92-00689-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


874 S.W.2d 229; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 631



March 24, 1994., Decided  
March 24, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 625,269. Brian Rains, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of June 24, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1792.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing overruled


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the 176th District Court Harris County (Texas), which entered a conviction for the crime of aggravated robbery. Defendant asserted that the state improperly amended the indictment, claimed that evidence should have been suppressed as a result of an alleged improper frisk, and that incriminating statements were the product of a custodial interrogation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated robbery in a jury trial. Defendant robbed a woman at knifepoint. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the abandonment of the words "use a" in the indictment against defendant, referring the knife defendant welded, did not constitute an amendment to the indictment, subject to a 10-day notice period, within the meaning of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.10 (1989), but was merely an abandonment of one of the alternative theories as to how the crime was committed. The court held that a knife found on defendant's person during a weapon's frisk was not obtained during an illegal weapons search and subject to suppression as defendant maintained. The court found that defendant was subject to a weapons frisk after he voluntarily agreed to accompany an investigating officer in his patrol car. Defendant was not under arrest when he agreed to accompany the officer and statements he made were not subject to a constitutional safety net. The trial court was not required to make findings under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 6 (1979), because the statements did not stem from a custodial interrogation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for the crime of aggravated robbery. The court held that the abandonment of one theory in the indictment did not constitute an amendment to the indictment. The court found that a weapons frisk was justified before defendant entered an officer's patrol car and held that statements made to the officer were not the product of a custodial interrogation.

The State Bar v. Tinning


No. 13-92-270-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


875 S.W.2d 403; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 647



March 24, 1994, Delivered  
March 24, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of October 14, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2836.



DISPOSITION: We GRANT the State Bar's motion for rehearing, REVERSE the trial court's judgment, and REMAND the case to the trial court for further proceedings. We DENY Tinning's motion for rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state bar sought review of a judgment of the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, arguing that the general four-year statute of limitations did not apply to disciplinary actions and that summary judgment against it in a disciplinary proceeding was error.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state bar filed a disciplinary petition against appellee attorney, alleging that he split fees with a non-lawyer. Appellee moved for summary judgment, appellant state bar did not timely respond, and the trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court held that appellee produced no evidence of the date the allegation against him was brought to the attention of appellant state bar's counsel. Thus, appellee did not establish that the proceeding was barred by limitations, and the trial court erred by granting summary judgment on that issue. Further, summary judgment documents were unsworn statements, were not competent summary judgment evidence, and did not constitute proof of the facts alleged. Finally, the court held that the trial court erred by granting summary judgment on the theory that Tex. Code of Professional Responsibility DR 3-102 was unconstitutionally vague. Thus, it granted appellant state bar's motion for rehearing, reversed the trial court's judgment, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings while denying appellee's motion for rehearing.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellant state bar's motion for rehearing, reversed the trial court's judgment against appellant, and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The court denied appellee attorney's motion for rehearing where appellee had not established that the proceeding was barred by limitations or that summary judgment evidence was incompetent, and where the disciplinary rule at issue was not unconstitutionally vague.

Graham v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


873 S.W.2d 709; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 576



March 17, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeals from 29th District Court of Palo Pinto County



DISPOSITION: The judgments of the trial court are reversed, and both causes are remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was placed on deferred adjudication by the 29th District Court of Palo Pinto County (Texas) pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, in which he entered pleas of guilty to burglary of a habitation and possession of less than 28 grams of methamphetamine. Later, the trial court found that defendant had violated the terms of his probation and revoked the orders of deferred adjudication. Defendant appealed that determination.

The court noted that that was the old law, but the statute changed in 1989.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded two guilty pleas after the trial court revoked defendant's probation and ordered deferred adjudication. Defendant's pleas were not knowingly and voluntarily made because the trial court failed to inform him that he could not appeal a subsequent finding that he had violated the terms of his probation.

McNeese v. State


No. A14-92-01237-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 455



March 10, 1994, Rendered  
March 10, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 639,836.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of possession with intent to deliver cocaine under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 481.112(a),(b) (1992). Defendant complained that the prosecutor engaged in improper argument and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by jury verdict of possession with intent to deliver cocaine. Defendant challenged his conviction and complained that statements made during the prosecutor's final argument improperly injected harmful facts that could not be inferred from the evidence. He asserted that the arguments were sufficiently egregious to warrant reversal, despite his failure to object at trial. Defendant also asserted he had received ineffective assistance of counsel. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the prosecutor's arguments were permissible as answers to argument of opposing counsel, and reasonable deductions from the evidence. The court found that other arguments by the prosecutor may have been improper, but they were not manifestly so, and could have been cured by an instruction to disregard if defendant had objected. The court concluded that considering all the circumstances and the entire representation, the failure to make one objection was not sufficient to render counsel's complete representation unconstitutionally ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession with intent to deliver cocaine, holding that the prosecutor's final arguments were permissible, or could have been cured if trial counsel had objected. The court considered the entire representation of counsel and found defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel.

Smith v. Board of Regents of the Univ. of Houston Sys.


No. 01-93-00108-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


874 S.W.2d 706; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 487



March 10, 1994, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student sought review of judgment from the 125th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the policy of appellees, university and board, for determining whether a nonresident student could be reclassified as a resident to qualify for resident tuition status. Appellant asserted that that the reclassification policy violated his right to due process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant student who challenged the constitutionality of the policy of appellees, university and board, for determining whether a nonresident student could be reclassified as a resident to qualify for resident tuition status asserted that that the reclassification policy violated his right to due process. The court affirmed, reasoning on appeal that though the burden of proof might be difficult for students to overcome, the rules promulgated by appellees did not create irrebuttable presumption. The court held that the evidence presented by appellant was not such that the refusal to reclassify him as a resident was arbitrary and capricious. The court found that the factors set forth in the reclassification statute created a test of bona fide residency for the purpose of resident tuition status. The court reasoned that although it agreed that the Texas Constitution could be interpreted as providing greater rights than the United States Constitution, appellant failed to cite case law to support his contention. The court also held that there was no breach of that contract because appellees correctly classified appellant as a nonresident for purposes of tuition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the court found that the reclassification rules promulgated by appellees, university and board, did not set up an irrebuttable presumption of nonresidency, but in fact created a test of bona fide residency for purposes of tuition.

Tandy Corp. v. Sharp


No. 3-93-339-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


872 S.W.2d 814; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 501



March 9, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 27, 1994. Released for Publication April 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-11674, HONORABLE HUME COFER, JUDGE PRESIDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the decision of the 53rd Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas) which involved the interpretation of former Tex. Tax Code Ann. §171.53(c). The district court had granted appellee comptroller's motion for summary judgment, affirming the imposition of a state franchise tax and denying any refund. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellee comptroller had interpreted former Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.153(c) to require that the surviving corporation report receipts from business done in Texas for the 12-month period ending on the day after the merger, rather than reporting receipts received through the last day of its preceding fiscal year. The Tax Code provided that a corporation must pay the franchise tax in advance, and base the amount of the tax on the corporation's value in the preceding fiscal year. The corporation was taxed only on that portion of its taxable capital corresponding to the percentage of corporate business conducted in the state. Appellant argued that appellee had misinterpreted the directive of former § 171.153(c) in calculating its franchise tax in 1986 following the merger. The court affirmed the judgment because it found that appellee had properly interpreted § 171.153(c) to provide for an alternate reporting period following certain mergers, which required both the surviving corporation's taxable capital and allocation factor representing "business done" in Texas to be calculated for a 12-month period ending the day after the merger.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment because appellant had asked it to reject appellee's proper construction of the tax provision. Although any system of assessing the value of two merging corporations would result in certain receipts being double-counted or excluded, the court agreed that appellee's understanding of the statute was the only rational interpretation.

Taylor v. State


No. 05-92-02092-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3610



March 4, 1994, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 265th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F91-22540-UR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 265th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, that revoked her probation and sentenced her to 10 years' imprisonment for her conviction for attempting to take a weapon from a peace officer in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.17.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of attempting to take a weapon from a peace officer in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.17. She was placed on probation and the state filed a motion to revoke her probation on a number of grounds. The trial court sentenced appellant to 10 years' confinement. Appellant asserted that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. She did not claim that was no evidence to support the conviction and, therefore, could not challenge the sufficiency of the proceeding. She argued that § 38.17 was unconstitutional as applied to her; however, an objection in the trial court was necessary to preserve the error. She claimed that the trial court failed to give her new conditions of probation after a new trial was granted. The court found that at the conclusion of the new trial, she was given new terms of probation, and found no error in the court's ruling. She asserted that the evidence was insufficient to support the revocation of her probation. Evidence was presented that she did not report to her hearing officer, and proof of any of the alleged violations was sufficient to support an order revoking probation. The trial court's order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that revoked appellant's probation and sentenced her to 10 years' imprisonment for attempting to take a weapon from a peace officer. Appellant failed to claim that there was no evidence to support her conviction and could not challenge the sufficiency of the proceedings. Evidence that she did not report to her hearing officer was sufficient to support the revocation.

Tex. Water Comm'n v. City of Fort Worth


No. 3-92-502-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


875 S.W.2d 332; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 407



March 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 13, 1994. Released for Publication June 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-11240, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of July 7, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1923.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water commission and appellee city both sought review of the judgment from the 167th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which reversed appellant water commission's order and remanded the docket to appellant water commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city of Arlington and appellee city of Fort Worth had entered into a contract allowing appellant city's wastewater to flow into appellee city's system for transportation to appellee city's treatment facility. Appellee city sent notice of the new yearly rate. Appellant city filed a petition with appellant water commission contesting the rate increase. The commission ordered the rates reduced and concluded that the rates in its order were just and reasonable. Appellee city filed suit for judicial review with the lower court. The lower court reversed the commission's order because the commission could not modify the contractual rate unless it first found that such a rate adversely affected the public interest. This appeal followed. The commission had jurisdiction to review appellant city's petition. The appropriate scope of appellate review under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 13.043(f) required that appellant water commission first make a finding that the rates affected by a decision of the provider adversely affected the public interest by being unreasonably preferential, prejudicial, or discriminatory. The commission made no such finding and so the matter was properly reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment because the lower court correctly determined that appellant water commission had jurisdiction to review appellant city's petition and correctly concluded that appellant commission could not modify the contractual rate unless it first found that such a rate had adversely affected the public interest.

Ainsworth v. State


No. B14-92-00686-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 392



February 24, 1994, Rendered  
February 24, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 431,740.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the 339th District Court Harris County (Texas), which entered a conviction for burglary of a habitation, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §30.02(a)(1) (1989), with intent to commit aggravated assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §22.01 (Supp.1994). Defendant complained that the evidence was insufficient, the jury instructions were improper, and he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary of a habitation, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §30.02(a)(1) (1989), with intent to commit aggravated assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §22.01 (Supp.1994). The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction because the combined and cumulative force of all the incriminating circumstances warranted a conclusion of guilt. Evidence showed that defendant kicked down the door of his wife's parent's house and fired shots into the residence. The court found that there was no evidence that if defendant were guilty at all that he was only guilty of criminal trespass and consequently he was not entitled to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of criminal trespass. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel. Because there was no basis to justify a self-defense instruction, the court held that counsel was not deficient in failing to request one. Finally, an error by the trial court in giving a jury instruction on parole and good-conduct time was found to be harmless because the court found that it did not contribute to defendant's punishment, Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the crime of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit aggravated assault. The court held that the conviction was supported by sufficient evidence, that defendant was not entitled to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of criminal trespass, and that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel.

 

1306 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of San Antonio v. Winkenhower


Appeal No. 04-93-00192-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


875 S.W.2d 388; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 936



February 23, 1994, Delivered  
February 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Court at Law No. 7 of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 202,290. Honorable Shay Gebhardt, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from County Court at Law No. 7 of Bexar County (Texas) that found for appellee and awarded damages in a personal injury action. Appellant contended that sovereign immunity was not waived under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.021 (1986) for an automobile accident that did not involve its employee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee hit a pothole and wrecked their car. As this accident did not involve the operation or use of a motor-driven vehicle or equipment by appellant city's employee, the judgment was error. The court first debunked appellees' theory that liability in this case was governed not by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.021 (1986), but by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.0215 (Supp. 1994). Section 101.0215, the court held, merely classified pothole filling as a governmental, as opposed to proprietary, municipal function, and was not an independent basis for liability. As a governmental function it was subject to the immunity scheme of the Texas Tort Claims Act, of which § 101.021 controlled. Although not specific, § 101.021 had been interpreted to require operation or use by a municipal employee for the waiver of immunity to apply, and the court followed this rule. Although pothole filling was once classified as a proprietary function, its reclassification as governmental, which reflected the reality of modern municipal duties, did not violate the constitutional access to courts rule, as such power was in the legislature by virtue of Tex. Const. art. XI, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for appellees and rendered a take-nothing judgment. Road maintenance was a governmental function, and as such, appellee city was immune from liability for an action predicated on the failure to keep the road in repair. The waiver of immunity for motor vehicle related injuries was inapplicable, as it applied only to motor vehicles operated or used by municipal employees.

 

1307 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mendel


Nos. B14-92-01283-CR, C14-92-01284-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


871 S.W.2d 906; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 312



February 17, 1994, Rendered  
February 17, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 629,106 & 629,107. C.V. Wilburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order from the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which dismissed indictments against appellees for keeping a gambling place and possessing a gambling device, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 47.04 and 47.06 (1989), on grounds that the statutes were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellees were charged with two counts of keeping a gambling place and possessing a gambling device in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 47.04, 47.06 (1989), for keeping video slot machines in their club. The trial court dismissed the indictments on the grounds that the statutes were unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed, applying a two-part test. First, the court determined that an ordinary citizen could get sufficient information from the criminal statutes to know that keeping a game of chance which needed little skill and gave a pay out was a violation of the statutes. Secondly, the court found that the statutes were sufficiently definite to avoid erratic or arbitrary arrests and convictions on the part of officials. The court accordingly held that the statutes were not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the indictments against appellees for keeping a gambling place and possessing a gambling device, holding that the statutes under which they were charged were not unconstitutionally vague where they provided sufficient information to let an ordinary citizen know what conduct was proscribed, and were sufficiently definite to avoid arbitrary arrests.

 

1308 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Adkins v. Tafel


No. 2-93-104-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


871 S.W.2d 289; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 304



February 16, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 153RD DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. KEN CURRY



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardians sought review of the order of the 153rd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee physician and pharmacist on the basis that the statute of limitations under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1994), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant guardians filed a medical malpractice suit against appellees, physician and pharmacist, for a personal injury that their ward sustained as a result of the side effects of medication. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees on grounds that the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, barred appellants claim. Appellants sought review of the trial court's judgment alleging that material fact issues existed about whether the statute of limitations violated the Texas Constitution and whether appellee physician fraudulently concealed a cause of action from appellants. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the statute of limitations was constitutional because appellants learned of the alleged malpractice approximately eighteen months prior to the end of the two-year limitations period. Failing to find an attorney to bring suit until after their claim was time-barred did not affect the constitutionality of the statute. The court also found that appellants did not prove that appellee physician fraudulently concealed anything that he should have disclosed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the two-year statute of limitations in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act was constitutional as applied to appellants because they learned of the alleged malpractice approximately eighteen months prior to the end of the period. Failing to suit until after their claim was time-barred did not make the statute unconstitutional.

Spears v. State


No. 05-93-00754-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3871



February 11, 1994, OPINION FILED


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 203rd District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F93-24104-WP.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 203rd District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of burglary of a building pursuant to a guilty plea, and assessed a 50-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to the offense of burglary of a building. The trial court accepted appellant's plea and assessed a 50-year sentence. Appellant sought review, contending that the trial court erred because it assessed punishment, but did not sentence him. Appellant also claimed that his sentence was cruel and unusual punishment. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, concluding that the trial court sentenced appellant, and that appellant's sentence did not violate statutory or constitutional requirements. The court found that both the statement of facts and the judgment showed that the trial court sentenced appellant. Thus, appellant's sentence met the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 42.03, § 1(a) (1994) and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.02 (1994). The court concluded that appellant's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (1994) specifically authorized appellant's punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court's judgment convicting appellant of burglary of a building pursuant to a guilty plea and assessing a 50-year sentence because the statement of facts and the judgment showed that appellant was sentenced as required by the rules of criminal procedure. Appellant's sentence was specifically authorized by statute, and therefore did not violate statutory or constitutional requirements.

Taylor v. State


No. 01-91-01053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 274



February 10, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 577, 906



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle from the 183rd District Court, Harris County (Texas) which the court affirmed. The Court of Criminal Appeals then remanded the case to the court for consideration of appellant's complaints that his arrest and search were illegal.


OVERVIEW: After remand from a higher court, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that appellant's arrest was justified to ensure his appearance and that the argument that an arrest pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d § 153 (1977) violated the Texas and U.S. Constitutions was without merit and that no authority to arrest under state law was required to be further guided by departmental policy. The court also stated that § 153 was not violative of the separation of powers because although it granted discretion to officers on whether to arrest, it did not allow officers to set the range of punishment. The court held that appellant's arrest did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because U.S. Const. amend. VIII is not applicable until the state has secured an adjudication of guilt and that appellant's due process or equal protection rights were not violated because he was arrested to ensure his appearance, which was a rational basis for the arrest, and not to punish him. Finally, the court held that appellant failed to meet his burden that he had standing to raise the issue of illegal search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, finding that appellant's contention that he was illegally arrested had no merit because he had no identification when he was stopped and he gave a false name. The court held that appellant had no standing to contest the search because he failed to meet his burden to prove standing.

Stanul v. State


NO. 3-92-619-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


870 S.W.2d 329; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 204



February 2, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 1994. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Dismissed May 18, 1994. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing On Petition for Discretionary Review Granted June 29, 1994. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 21, 1994. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied September 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BELL COUNTY, 264TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 40,721, HONORABLE JOE CARROLL, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 264th Judicial District Court of Bell County (Texas) convicting him for the murder of his eight-month-old son, arguing that the jury improperly found that a deadly weapon had been used in the commission of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with the murder of his eight-month-old son. He was found guilty of murder and sentenced to seven years' imprisonment. Appellant argued that the jury improperly found that a deadly weapon had been used in the commission of the offense. The evidence showed that appellant, intending to cause serious bodily injury, struck the victim's head with or against something large, flat, and hard, probably the floor, with such force as to cause fatal brain trauma. The court determined that the jury rationally found that the floor was capable of causing death or serious bodily injury in the manner of its use by appellant and, therefore, was a deadly weapon. Therefore, the judgment of conviction rendered against appellant was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for the murder of his eight-month old son was affirmed because the jury rationally found that the floor was capable of causing death or serious bodily injury in its use by appellant and, therefore, was a deadly weapon.

Ward v. State


Nos. 01-93-00294-CR, 01-93-00301-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


870 S.W.2d 659; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 181



January 27, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
January 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 18, 1994. On Remand from the United States Supreme Court January 29, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 406. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 7, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 344th District Court. Chambers County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 7837, 7838. Judge: Carroll E. Wilburn, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 344th District Court, Chambers County, Texas, which denied his writ of habeas corpus, which he filed after being indicted for both aggravated possession of marijuana and for possession of marijuana on which no tax had been paid, because he had already received an assessment of tax due on the marijuana plus a penalty for failure to pay tax.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for both aggravated possession of marijuana and possession of marijuana on which no tax had been paid. He also received a tax assessment and penalty, and the state seized a radar detector and $ 2,165 cash. Defendant filed a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that the tax assessment and forfeiture constituted punishment for the same offenses for which he was indicted, so that prosecution of the indictments would violate U.S. Const. amend. V, the double jeopardy clause, and the Texas Constitution. The trial court denied the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of the writ, holding that because defendant did not pay the tax assessment, and because the forfeiture of the property was remedial under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 59.06 and the value of the property forfeited was not overwhelmingly disproportionate to the damage defendant caused, neither was punishment within the meaning of the double jeopardy clause. The court held that prosecution of the indictments would not violate defendant's rights under either the federal or state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the writ of habeas corpus, because the forfeiture of defendant's property and the tax assessment did not constitute a punishment within the meaning of the double jeopardy clause of either the U.S. Constitution or the Texas Constitution, so prosecution for possession of marijuana and possession of marijuana on which no tax had been paid would not subject him to multiple punishment.

Dietz v. State


No. 05-92-01467-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3438



January 24, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 9. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MA91-45163-K.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Dallas County Criminal District Court No. 9 (Texas), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of promoting obscene material, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(a), upon evidence that defendant sold a videotape showing explicit homosexual acts and expert testimony from a police detective that, in his opinion, the material was obscene and defendant knew of its content and character.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with promotion of obscene material, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(a). Evidence was presented at trial that, while working at an adult bookstore, defendant sold a videotape to an undercover police detective. The videotape showed explicit homosexual acts. Two expert witnesses for the state gave opinions that the videotape was obscene and the undercover detective gave an expert opinion that defendant knew of its content and character. Two defense experts opined that the videotape was not obscene and would not appeal to the prurient interest of homosexuals or heterosexuals. The trial court gave a jury instruction concerning the prurient interests of any person and refused defendant's requested instruction requiring consideration of the prurient interest of homosexuals. Defendant was convicted and he appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that it was proper not to require the jury to consider prurient interests of homosexuals, rather than the prurient interest of any person, and it was not an abuse of discretion to admit the detectives' expert opinions. Moreover, § 43.23(a) did not violate freedom of speech under Tex. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because the jury was properly instructed to consider the prurient interest of any person and the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's requested instruction regarding appeal of the material to the prurient interest of homosexuals; the statute did not violate defendant's speech rights and was not unconstitutional; and the admission of expert opinion was not an abuse of discretion.

Regalado v. State


No. A14-93-00022-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


872 S.W.2d 7; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 45



January 13, 1994, Rendered  
January 13, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number 8. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9246106. Neel Richardson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law, Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of possession of obscene devices with the intent to sell. Appellant claimed that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.21(a)(7), 43.23(c)(1) were unconstitutional for overbreadth and that his due process rights were violated by the presumption created by the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an adult bookstore clerk, was arrested and convicted of possession of obscene devices with intent to sell. Appellant challenged his conviction on grounds that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.21(a)(7), 43.23(c)(1) were overbroad and unconstitutional. Appellant claimed that the statutes, without justification, criminalized the conduct of physicians, psychologists, and therapists. Appellant also claimed that the presumption created by the statute violated his due process rights. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that the statute had previously been upheld and that appellant failed to show that he possessed the devices for any medical reason either as a patient or as a health care practitioner. The court further determined that appellant's due process rights were not violated because there was a sufficient connection between the proven facts that appellant was a clerk in the store and possessed 17 dildos and the presumption that a person with six or more obscene devices was presumed to possess them with intent to promote them. The court further noted that there was no implication that appellant had to present any evidence to rebut the presumption.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for possession of obscene devices with intent to sell was affirmed because he had no constitutional right to possess the devices. Appellant failed to show that his possession was medically-related, and his due process rights were not violated by the promotion presumption created by the statute because he was not required to present evidence to rebut it.

Skinner v. Commissioners' Court


No. 05-92-02913-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 3643



January 12, 1994, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 68th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-11788-C.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant constable challenged the order of the 68th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which denied his application for a temporary injunction to prevent appellee commissioners' court from reducing the number of deputy constables in appellant's precinct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant constable applied for a temporary injunction to enjoin appellee commissioner's court from revising staffing standards and reducing the number of deputy constables in appellant's precinct. Appellant contended that he would suffer probable injury because a staff reduction in his precinct would prevent his deputies from performing their job functions. Appellant also claimed that appellee's staffing standards were arbitrary and capricious and were applied in an arbitrary and capricious manner. The trial court denied appellant's request for injunctive relief. Appellant challenged that denial. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellant failed to establish imminent harm, irreparable injury, and no adequate remedy at law. The evidence showed that, despite the staff reduction, appellant's tasks would not be neglected. Also, appellant's claims of irreparable injury were based on speculation, and appellant could always apply for the appointment of additional deputies at a later date. The record did not reflect that appellant had established a probable injury due to appellee's actions, and, thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the temporary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant constable's application for a temporary injunction to prevent appellee commissioners' court from making staff reductions in appellant's precinct. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the temporary injunction because appellant failed to establish probable injury due to appellee's actions.

Ford v. State


No. A14-92-01210-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


868 S.W.2d 875; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3395



December 23, 1993, Rendered  
December 23, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 85th District Court. Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 19,920-85. J.D. Langley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the 85th District Court of Brazos County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of a short-barrel firearm under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.01 (1989), sentenced him to confinement, and imposed a fine. The sentence was suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a "short-barrel firearm" that police found on the floor of his car. Defendant unsuccessfully moved to quash the indictment on the ground that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 46.01(5), 46.01(10) were so ambiguous that they violated his due process rights, that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.06(3) violated his right to bear arms, and that he was improperly charged because he was in possession of a "handgun." The appellate court affirmed because defendant failed to properly preserve for appeal the issues raised by his motion to quash. In any event, defendant's positions on the issues were without merit. The standards set forth in Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 46.01(5), 46.01(10) were sufficiently clear that an ordinary person knew what constituted proscribed conduct. The right to bear arms is not absolute and is subject to legislative regulation to prevent crime. The fact that the sawed-off shotgun that was in defendant's possession could be fired with one hand did not transform it from a "short-barrel firearm" into a "handgun."


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant of possession of a short-barrel firearm was affirmed The statute under which defendant was charged was not unconstitutionally vague, and did not violate his right to bear arms. The evidence was sufficient to support the verdict, as a sawed off shotgun was not a handgun.

OVERVIEW: Appellee employees were exposed to asbestos-containing products. Appellants, employer and others, was sued in a negligence and products-liability action due to appellees' ailments. Browning v. State


No. 01-93-00244-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3313



December 16, 1993, Rendered  
December 16, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 626858



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 178th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle after a guilty plea with no plea bargain. The trial court overruled defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. The motion asserted that defendant did not enter his guilty plea knowingly and intelligently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to unauthorized use of a motor vehicle. Defendant received no agreement on a recommended sentence from the state in exchange for the plea. Defendant made a motion to withdraw the plea after he was sentenced to a long term of confinement. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. On appeal, defendant argued that he did not enter a knowing and intelligent guilty plea because his counsel misinformed him that his sentence would be time served since his arrest. The court held that a defendant was not entitled to withdraw his guilty plea just because after the plea he discovered that he miscalculated the strength of the state's case or the probable penalties. The court found that defendant signed a confession that said that the state did not agree to any recommended sentence, and the court found that defendant answered yes when the trial court asked him if he understood that he had no plea bargain with the state. The court also held that, by entering a valid guilty plea, a defendant waived all non-jurisdictional defects and that included federal and state due process claims. Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that defendant's plea was not vulnerable to attack on the basis that he might not have accurately considered every relevant factor in coming to his decision to plea guilty. Defendant waived all non-jurisdictional defects by voluntarily pleading guilty, and that included federal and state due process claims.
