Caswell v. State


No. 01-90-01132-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3343



December 16, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 546383.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas that convicted him upon his no contest plea of sexual assault of a child under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(1)(B)(iii) (1974) and that sentenced him to 25 years imprisonment. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, 9 (Supp. 1993), and his counsel's effectiveness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual abuse of a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(1)(B)(iii) (1974) upon his plea of no contest, and, after a sentencing hearing, was sentenced to 25 years imprisonment. On appeal, the court held that because appellant signed two documents waiving his constitutional rights and agreeing that witnesses would testify that appellant committed the crime, and because it was necessary to have allegations and proof of only one of several means of committing the crime, the evidence was sufficient for the conviction. The court held that because appellant's due process rights were not violated when the trial court considered the presentence report authorized by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, 9 (Supp. 1993) before sentencing him, the statute was not unconstitutional. Because there was no evidence that the inclusion of appellant's proposed supervision plan in the presentence report would have led to a deferred adjudication, appellant's counsel's assistance was not ineffective for not objecting to its exclusion. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for sexual assault of a child. The court held that appellant's written statements that witnesses would testify he committed the crime was sufficient evidence for the conviction, the statute authorizing the trial court to review a presentence report before sentencing him did not unconstitutionally deprive him of due process, and lack of evidence that he was prejudiced by his counsel's assistance made it effective.

Fuller v. Travelers Indem. Co.


No. 09-92-144 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


867 S.W.2d 164; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3371



December 16, 1993, Delivered  
December 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 58th District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. A-117,255F. J. Michael Bradford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a deceased worker's survivor, sought review of the judgment from the 58th District Court, Jefferson County (Texas), which granted appellee employer's insurers' motion for summary judgment on appellant's wrongful death claim. Appellant claimed that the Texas Workers Compensation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, § 3(e), giving appellees immunity violated Tex. Const. art. 16, § 26 and art. 1, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's decedent died from cancer caused by exposure to toxins at his place of employment in an oil refinery. Appellant, the decedent's survivor, brought a wrongful death action against appellees, the employer's insurers, and the trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that Tex. Const. art. 16, § 26 permitted exemplary damages in wrongful death actions only where such actions already existed but did not create a new cause of action, and that Tex. Const. art. 1, § 13 preserved the right to sue for common law actions and therefore did not apply to appellant's claims. Thus, the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, § 3(e), that granted appellees immunity for their alleged failure to discover the toxins, was not unconstitutional. Because appellant's decedent did not preserve his right to sue appellees, and because appellant's action was a derivative of the decedent's right to recover under Tex. Civ. Prac. and Rem. Code Ann. § 71.003(a) (1986), appellant's claim was barred. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the motion of appellees, an employee's insurers, for summary judgment on the wrongful death claim of appellant, the survivor of a deceased worker. The court held that because appellant's claim was derivative and did not exist at common law, the Texas Workers' Compensation Act giving appellees immunity was constitutional and barred appellant's claim, as did her decedent's waiver of his right to sue.

 

1322 of 1793 DOCUMENTS



Wright v. Ector County Indep. Sch. Dist.


No. 08-93-00043-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


867 S.W.2d 863; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3337



December 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 70th District Court of Ector County, Texas (TC# A-91,450). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. R. L. McKim


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of orders of the 70th District Court of Ector County (Texas), which denied appellant's application for a writ of mandamus to compel appellee school district to admit her minor child to first grade in the public schools, and which granted appellee summary judgment in appellant's suit for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1343 for wrongfully denying the application for admission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that the trial court abused its discretion in failing to find that appellee school district's policy -- excluding from first grade children under the age of six -- was arbitrary. The court disagreed, noting first that appellant's five-year-old was excluded without consideration of his qualifications. The legislative discretion given to appellee with respect to the admission of over and underage children was across-the-board and not limited to distinguishing between qualified and unqualified applicants. No error occurred when appellant was denied a due process hearing, given the policy's strict exclusion, noting that appellant had been allowed to present her case to appellee. Although "exhaustion of remedies" was not a judicial prerequisite to appellant's claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, summary judgment for appellee was proper when appellant failed to raise a factual issue regarding the strict application of the underage rule; nor was appellant deprived of an equal protection right to have her child in first grade when all five-year-olds were similarly treated. The gifted and talented program did not create an policy exception, absent statutory support.


OUTCOME: Orders affirmed denying appellant's writ of mandamus to compel appellee school district to admit her minor child to first grade in public school and granting summary judgment to appellee in appellant's suit for damages under § 1983, as appellee's policy of excluding underage children from first grade was not arbitrary, as appellant was not entitled a due process hearing, and as gifted and talented program did not create a policy exception.


 

1323 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Sowell v. Dresser Indus.


No. 09-92-249 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


866 S.W.2d 803; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3298



December 9, 1993, Delivered  
December 9, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 217th District Court. Angelina County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 24,934-91-05. David Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SUMMARY JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife and personal representative challenged an order from the 217th District Court, Angelina County (Texas), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in a wrongful death claim under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.003 on the ground that the action had not been filed within the two year statute of limitations pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code ann. § 16.003.


OVERVIEW: An employee was diagnosed with silicosis attributable to exposure to silica while working for appellee employer. Nearly three years after his death, appellant wife and personal representative filed a wrongful death claim under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.003, and the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of appellee, finding that the claim was barred by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.003. On appeal, the court affirmed that order, holding that the two year requirement for filing a wrongful death action was not extended by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §16.062 (1986) because that statute had no application to wrongful death claims. The court also found that the appropriate statute of limitations had already run against the employee prior to his death because his cause of action accrued upon the discovery of his injury and ran before his death. Therefore, there was no wrongful death upon which appellant could file a claim because the employee could not have brought an action for personal injury had he lived. The court also held that appellant had accepted benefits under the Workers' Compensation act, thereby precluding her action against appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment in favor of appellee employee in a wrongful death action because the complaint had not been filed within the Texas two year statute of limitations.

Weck v. Sharp


No. 3-93-168-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


884 S.W.2d 787; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3547



December 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled January 19, 1994. Released for Publication October 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-16504, HONORABLE JAMES R. MEYERS, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the order of the 200th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which granted appellee state officials' plea to dismiss the complaint seeking a review of a tax assessment pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 112.051, 112.108 (1992).


OVERVIEW: After appellant taxpayer exhausted his administrative remedies, and he filed a complaint seeking a review of a tax assessment and a declaration that the Controlled Substances Tax Act, Tex. Tax. Code Ann. §§ 159.001-159.206 (1992), and Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 112.051, 112.108 (1992) were unconstitutional. The trial court granted appellees' plea to the jurisdiction and dismissed the action for want of jurisdiction. The court affirmed the dismissal because § 112.108 prohibited declaratory judgment actions against the state in tax matters, and pursuant to § 112.051, as a prerequisite to jurisdiction, appellant was required to pay the taxes due and then make a written protest. No grounds existed at common law to sue the state in tax matters; thus, appellant could challenge the tax assessment only in the manner provided by the statute that created the right.


OUTCOME: Order of dismissal affirmed because the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief to appellant taxpayer who failed to comply with the jurisdictional prerequisites to challenging a tax assessment.

Kaye v. Harris County Mun. Util. Dist. No. 9

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the orders of the District Court for Harris County, Texas, which issued summary judgment in favor of appellee county in a case concerning a taxing dispute and denied appellants' motion to set aside judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellee district denied appellant property owners' petition to have their property excluded from taxation under Tex. Water Code Ann. 54.701(b) (Supp. 1993), after learning that water and sewer service could not be provided to the property. The court held that appellant failed to preserve the constitutionality issue for appeal.

Geringer v. State

December 2, 1993, Filed

Eleftheriadis v. State


No. 08-92-00407-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


868 S.W.2d 11; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3238



December 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 2 of Ector County, Texas. (TC# 92-1083-C). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. J.A. "Jim" Bobo



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nightclub manager challenged a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2 of Ector County (Texas), which convicted appellant of permitting a person to expose her person on premises licensed by the Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission for the retail sale of beer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nightclub manager was convicted under Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01 (1993), which prohibited an employee of a licensee from permitting a person to "expose her person" on premises licensed for the retail sale of beer. Appellant argued that the trial court applied the wrong definition and standard with regard to the term "expose her person" and that the "indecent exposure" statute in the Tex. Penal Code Ann. governed the analysis of the "expose her person" element. The court affirmed, holding that the "custom and decency" standard, not the "indecent exposure" standard, was to be used in interpreting the Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01 (1993). Having viewed all of the evidence in a light most favorable to the verdict, a rational trier of fact could have found that a woman did "expose her person," an essential element of the crime as alleged, beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant nightclub manager was properly convicted for permitting a person to expose her person on premises licensed for the retail sale of beer, because a rational trier of fact could have found each element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 23rd District Court of Brazoria County (Texas), convicting appellant on two counts of burglary of a habitation under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction on two counts of burglary of a habitation. The court affirmed appellant's conviction on the first count of burglary, because the state proved the essential elements of burglary under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02(a) (1989). Appellant failed to establish any record evidence that he was denied a speedy trial. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. Although correctly convicted for one count of burglary, appellant was improperly convicted of a second count of burglary of a habitation, because the state failed to prove all the essential elements for the second offense.

Cedar Crest Funeral Home v. Lashley


No. 05-93-00003-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


889 S.W.2d 325; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3550



November 29, 1993, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 336th Judicial District Court. Grayson County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-1183.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a class of funeral homes and associated individuals, sought interlocutory review of the order of the 336th Judicial District Court, Grayson County (Texas), that certified plaintiff customers as a class under Tex. R. Civ. P. 42. Defendants contended that the named plaintiffs lacked standing to represent the unnamed members of the class.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, a class of funeral homes and associated individuals, sought interlocutory review of the trial court's order that certified plaintiff customers as a class under Tex. R. Civ. P. 42. The court affirmed and held that the trial court abused its discretion when it certified a single class of plaintiffs when none of the representative plaintiffs' claims were typical of the entire class. Plaintiffs alleged facts that gave the trial court jurisdiction, and a review of the pleadings showed that each of the named plaintiffs clearly alleged a direct injury caused by wrongful conduct. However, the court held that the claims of the representative parties were not typical of the claims of the unnamed members of the class. All defendants had not harmed the representative. Plaintiffs did not allege a conspiracy or concerted scheme among defendants, and there was no juridical link among the defendants that allowed a single resolution of the liability.


OUTCOME: The order that certified plaintiff customers as a class in their suit against defendant funeral homes and associated individuals was reversed as an abuse of discretion. The claims of the representatives were not typical of the claims of the unnamed members of the class, and plaintiffs did not allege a conspiracy among defendants.

Valencia v. State

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for delivery of at least 400 grams of cocaine in the 263rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, claiming that appellee state's closing argument was improper and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel in violation of his U.S. Const. amend. VI. rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of delivery of at least 400 grams of cocaine. VI. standards and that there was a reasonable probability that, but for the alleged deficiencies, the outcome would have been different.

Ex parte Delcourt


No. 01-93-00862-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


868 S.W.2d 373; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3086

November 18, 1993, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Habeas Corpus Relief granted in part and denied in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus for relied from a judgment by the trial court (Texas) that found relator in contempt of its orders and ordered him committed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found relator in contempt of its agreed temporary order that ordered relator to pay his wife's automobile note, and ordered him committed. Relator was discharged and incarcerated after he violated a new commitment order. Relator filed a writ of habeas corpus and contended that the first commitment order was void because it violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 18, which prohibited imprisonment for debt. The court accepted relator's constitutional argument and held that he should be released from custody under the first order. Relator next argued that the new commitment order was void because his contempt charges could have resulted in 44 years of prison and the court did not inform him of his right to a jury trial in violation of U.S. Const. amend. The court also rejected relator's argument that his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV were violated and held that relator's 2 months notice of the contempt charges and 13 days notice of the hearing was adequate.


OUTCOME: The court granted the habeas corpus relief from relator's contempt charges in part and denied it in part. The court granted relator's release from custody under the first order because obligations to make payments were not enforceable by contempt because to do so would amount to unconstitutional imprisonment for debt. The court denied relator relief from the new order because it did not violate the Sixth Amendment or the Fourteenth Amendment.

Palomares v. State


No. 01-92-00814-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3026



November 10, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 622,233



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of the decision of the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of aggravated sexual assault and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of his conviction for aggravated sexual assault and his sentence of life imprisonment and argued that the jury improperly considered the effects of the parole law on the sentence it assessed. The jury was given verbatim the parole instruction required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.07, 4(a) which informed it that while it could consider the existence of the parole law, it could not consider the manner in which the law might apply to appellant. The court found that a jury note to the lower court containing a crossed-out reference to parole rebutted the evidence that the jury considered parole in assessing punishment. The court also considered appellant's criminal record and the facts of the case. It concluded that because the jury was presented with evidence of the appellant's criminal record, which involved the offenses of attempted sexual assault, indecency with a child, and indecent exposure, it reasonably might assess the maximum punishment because of its abhorrence of the perpetrator of the crime. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence for aggravated sexual assault and held that the jury did not consider the effect of the parole law in assessing appellant criminal defendant's sentence because when it submitted a question to the court, it crossed out a reference to parole, which indicated to the court that it did not disregard the court's instructions not to consider parole in making its sentencing decision.

Scurlock Permian Corp. v. Brazos County

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil transporter challenged the judgment of the 361st District Court, Brazos County, Texas, which denied appellant's request for a declaration that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d-11 (1993) preempted appellee county's power to require a vehicle with a state permit also to have a county permit and that the appellee's traffic regulations were void. Instead, the district court sua sponte declared art. 6701d-11 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee county issued citations to appellant oil transporter for failing to buy county permits for its overweight vehicles. Appellant argued that it had state permits for overweight vehicles under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d-11 (1993). Appellee relied on the County Road and Bridge Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6702-1, §§ 2.301(a)(1), (b)(2) (1993), which did not expressly authorize the county permits for overweight vehicles. Appellant filed suit against appellee seeking a declaratory judgment that art. 6701d-11 preempted appellee's power to require the issuance of county permits. The district court denied relief and held sua sponte that art. 6701d-11 violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 56. Ann. art. 6701d-11, § 2(b)(1) (1993) limited the power of appellee to issue permits for overweight vehicles, and that appellee could not issue a permit, charge any additional fee for, or otherwise regulate or restrict the operation of a vehicle with a permit issued under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d-11, § 5B (1993).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying appellant oil transporter a declaration as to appellee county's power to require overweight vehicles with state permits also to have county permits and declared that appellee's power to issue permits for overweight vehicles was limited. The court ordered that appellant recover fees paid to appellee for such permits and remanded. The court affirmed the denial of injunctive relief.

Burgett v. State


NO. 2-93-053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


865 S.W.2d 594; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3059



November 9, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled December 21, 1993. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 97TH DISTRICT COURT OF CLAY COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Roger E. Towery



DISPOSITION: Because each of appellant's points of error is overruled, we affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentence for delivery of amphetamines in violation of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 481.103(3), 481.113 (1992) following a jury trial in the 97th District Court of Clay County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for delivery of amphetamines in violation of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 481.103(3), 481.113 (1992). Appellant fled shortly after the indictment was handed down. He was arrested in Alabama five years later and brought back to Texas for trial. The jury found him guilty and assessed an enhanced sentence of 40 years' imprisonment because appellant had a prior felony conviction. Appellant claimed that he was denied his right to a speedy trial, he was denied notice of the sentencing enhancement, and that the amended indictment was defective. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court denied appellant's speedy trial claim because the delay was caused by appellant's efforts to evade apprehension, the state was diligent in its efforts to locate appellant, and appellant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the delay. The court also found that the indictment gave appellant proper notice of the state's intent to seek an enhanced penalty. Further, the court found that appellant was given proper notice of the amended indictment because it was presented to the trial judge more than 10 days prior to trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for delivery of amphetamines because the state did not deprive appellant of his right to a speedy trial where appellant fled to evade apprehension, the state gave appellant proper notice of its intent to seek an enhanced sentence, and appellant was given proper notice of the amended indictment.

State v. Fry


Nos. B14-92-01196-CR, B14-92-01197-CR, B14-92-01198-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


867 S.W.2d 398; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2956



November 4, 1993, Rendered  
November 4, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 180th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 621,410, 621,411, 621,412. Jimmy James, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the 180th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which dismissed three separate indictments that were filed against appellee club owners. The dismissed indictments alleged that appellees committed the offenses of keeping a gambling place and possessing a gambling device pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 47.04, 47.06 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellee club owners maintained an establishment where people could play video slot machines. While at appellees' club, an undercover police officer discovered a "knock off switch" on the video machine, and when he hit switch the video machine became a gambling device. Based on this information, the state indicted appellees on three separate charges of keeping a gambling place and possessing a gambling device pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 47.04, 47.06 (1989). After the undercover police officer testified at the indictment hearing, the trial court dismissed appellees' indictments, holding that the gambling statutes were unconstitutional because they were overbroad. On appeal the court reversed the trial court's decision, holding that the trial court erred in finding that the gambling device statutes were overbroad because the overbreadth doctrine was inapplicable with regard to conduct that was not protected by the U.S. Const. amend. I. The court also disregarded appellees' argument that they could not be charged with possession of a gambling device because according to the statutory definitions, the machine could not be designed for gambling purposes without requiring a bet.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the case to the trial court, holding that the trial court erred in dismissing the state's gambling indictments against appellant club owners. The court held that gambling statutes could not be held unconstitutional for being overbroad because the overbreadth doctrine was inapplicable with regard to conduct that was not protected by the First Amendment.

Caulder v. State


No. C14-92-00912-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2960



November 4, 1993, Rendered  
November 4, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 552,995.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the 339th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that sentenced defendant to 75 years for the shooting death of her former boyfriend after defendant violated her terms of probation. Defendant complained that the sentence was cruel and unusual for only a technical violation of probation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to 75 years in prison for the shooting death of her former boyfriend. The court adjudicated defendant's guilt and imposed the sentence after defendant violated the terms of her probation. On appeal the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court held that defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment under either the U.S. Constitution or the Texas Constitution because the sentence was within the statutorily prescribed range. The court also concluded that there was no abuse of discretion because the trial court sentenced defendant for her criminal offense and not for the violation of probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. It was not cruel and unusual punishment to sentence defendant within the statutorily prescribed range for murder after defendant violated probation, and the sentence was for the criminal offence and not for the probation violation.

Carrillo v. State


No. 01-92-01181-CR, No. 01-92-01182-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2888



October 28, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 14. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 9205398 and 9205399.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of the decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 14, Harris County (Texas), which entered judgment against appellant after a jury found him guilty of possession of obscene devices with the intent to sell, and guilty of selling an obscene device in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant was convicted by a jury for possession of obscene devices with the intent to sell, and selling an obscene device, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (1989). Appellant challenged his convictions and the court affirmed. The court held that appellant did not have a right to privacy regarding the obscene devices and that the court would not recognize an overbreadth doctrine regarding the statute because attacks on overbreadth were reserved for complaints concerning U. S. Const. amend. I violations. The court also held that appellant was not entitled to a definition of obscene in the jury instructions because the devices were specifically defined by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.21(7) (1989) as obscene. Finally, the court held that appellant was not entitled to his special requested jury instruction and that the trial court did not err in the jury instructions given because the jury was instructed according to the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's convictions for possession of obscene devices with the intent to sell and selling an obscene device and held that appellant did not have a right to privacy in the obscene devices, he was not entitled to a definition of obscene in the charge to the jury, and the trial court instructed the jury according to the law and did not err when it did not grant appellant's special requested jury charge.

Cantu v. State


No. A14-92-01099-CR, No. A14-92-01107-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


866 S.W.2d 647; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2925



October 28, 1993, Rendered  
October 28, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 339th District Court Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 609,578 and 621,946. John Ackerman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 339th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of third-degree felony theft pursuant to the third offender provision of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(E) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to the theft of a pair of shoes, in addition to the theft of a camera and 10 containers of nasal spray. As a result of two prior theft convictions, appellant was convicted of third-degree felony theft pursuant to the third offender provision of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(E) (1993). Appellant's conviction was enhanced under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 2.42(d) (1993) because of a previous conviction for burglary of a building and possession of cocaine. Appellant contended that the application of §§ 31.03(e)(4)(E) and 12.42(d) resulted in double jeopardy, and that it was a disproportionate punishment in relation to the offense in violation of U.S. Const. Amends. V, VIII, and XIV and the corresponding provisions of Texas Constitution. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that appellant's charge under § 31.03(e)(4)(E) could be enhanced pursuant to § 12.42(d) so long as two of the offenses alleged were prior felony convictions for nontheft offenses. The court also held that appellant's punishment was not disproportionate for the offense because appellant had five felony convictions and was sentenced to 25 years with the possibility of parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted appellant of third-degree felony theft, holding that appellant's charge could be enhanced under the applicable statute so long as two of the offenses alleged were prior felony convictions for nontheft offenses. The court also held that appellant's punishment was not disproportionate for the offense he committed.

City of Grand Prairie v. Sisters of the Holy Family of Nazareth


No. 05-92-01962-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


868 S.W.2d 835; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3505

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Reversed and Rendered in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a partial summary judgment of the 134th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), invalidating appellant's assessment ordinance and awarding appellee property owner attorneys' fees. Appellant asserted that the ordinance was supported by evidence of special benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city assessed appellee property owner for street improvements based on a study of the value of benefits to abutting property owners. Appellee brought suit against appellant, challenging the ordinance, and won judgment invalidating the ordinance and awarding appellee attorneys' fees. Appellant sought review of the adverse judgment. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee and held that the ordinance was null and void, but reversed judgment as to the award of appellee's attorneys' fees, finding that appellant acted arbitrarily, violating U.S. Const. amends. Ann. art. 1105b, (1993).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment for appellee property owner and invalidated appellant city's special assessment ordinance, because the ordinance was not supported by substantial evidence of special benefit, but the court reversed judgment assessing attorneys' fees to appellee, because appellee was not entitled to attorney's fees as it had not paid the assessment.

The State Bar v. Tinning


NUMBER 13-92-270-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2836



October 14, 1993, Delivered  
October 14, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn March 24, 1994. Substituted Opinion of March 24, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 647.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, state bar, sought review of an order by the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee attorney in a disciplinary proceeding appellant brought against appellee for splitting fees with a non-lawyer.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee attorney in appellant state bar's disciplinary action for fee-splitting with a non-lawyer and remanded for further proceedings. The court applied the state bar's limitation period, upon which appellant relied, as if it were a statute and held the action was not time barred because appellee attorney did not negate the applicability of the limitation period at trial, did not show that the general statute applied instead, did not show when the limitation period began to run, and therefore did not establish his affirmative defense that the action was barred by limitation. The court found that the documents supporting appellee's motion for summary judgment were unsworn statements and thus were not competent summary judgment evidence, and did not constitute proof that he was not engaged in fee-splitting. The court held that the disciplinary rules in question did not violate appellee's right to due process because they were civil in nature, they gave attorneys adequate notice of the prohibited conduct, and there was no evidence that the state bar administered them in an arbitrary fashion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment in favor of appellee attorney because appellant state bar's disciplinary action against him was not time barred, insufficient evidence supported appellee's summary judgment motion, and the disciplinary rule applied did not violate his right to due process as it was not vague or arbitrarily applied. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Garcia v. State


No. 08-93-00044-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


874 S.W.2d 688; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3522



October 13, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Discretionary Review Refused on or about February 18, 1994. Released for Publication March 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 5 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 910C09726). Trial Court Judge: Hon Herb Cooper



DISPOSITION: Having sustained Appellant's sole point of error, the judgment of the trial court is reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 5 of El Paso County, Texas, which convicted him for the misdemeanor offense of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: A trial court convicted appellant for driving while intoxicated and appellant sought review. The court reversed the trial court's judgment because the trial court erred in failing to submit appellant's special requested jury charge. The court found that appellant's charge was incorrect because it wholly failed to make reference to the requirement that appellant be observed for 15 minutes prior to the administration of an intoxilyzer test. The record showed that the trial court understood that appellant was objecting to the omission of an instruction regarding the failure of law enforcement officials to observe appellant for the required 15 minute period. Thus, the trial court was apprised of appellant's objection to omissions in the charge, and the trial court's failure to submit the special requested jury charge pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 38.23(a) (1993) constituted error. A factual dispute existed as to the validity of appellant's intoxilyzer results regarding whether appellant was observed for the required statutory period of time. The court found that appellant showed some harm to require reversal of his conviction, irrespective of an automatic reversal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a trial court's judgment convicting appellant of driving while intoxicated because the trial court erred in failing to submit appellant's special requested jury charge. Appellant's charge was incorrect because it failed to refer to the statutory requirement that appellant be observed for 15 minutes prior to the administration of an intoxilyzer test. Appellant also showed some harm to require reversal of his conviction.

Hartman v. Sirgo Operating


No. 08-93-00030-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


863 S.W.2d 764; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2694; 127 Oil & Gas Rep. 380

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled November 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 142nd District Court of Midland County, Texas. (TC# A-38,560)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged an order of the 142nd District Court of Midland County (Texas), which declared a contract for the sale and exchange of oil and gas properties void and awarded attorney's fees to appellee corporations.


OVERVIEW: The trial court declared a contract for the sale and exchange of certain oil and gas properties in New Mexico void. The contract was between appellee corporations and appellant owner but was void because appellant's wife had not signed the contract and the property at issue was community property. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court had jurisdiction to determine if certain conditions precedent had been met, if the contract was valid, and if the parties' obligations were valid and enforceable. The court also held that because appellees sought a determination of rights and obligations under the contract and not specific performance of any obligation involving the title to land, other individuals were not necessary parties. The court also found no error in the Texas court proceeding to judgment prior to any decision by the New Mexico court nor an abuse of discretion in awarding attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaration of a contract for the sale and exchange of oil and gas properties void because the trial court had jurisdiction to determine if the contract was valid and other individuals were not necessary parties because the issue was a determination of rights and obligations and not specific performance involving land.

McDonald v. State


No. 01-92-01074-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


863 S.W.2d 541; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2631



September 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number 5 of Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-39897. Hannah Chow, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law Number 5 of Harris County (Texas), after he was convicted of driving while intoxicated, under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(b) (1993), on the grounds his due process rights were violated when the police destroyed evidence, that the trial court erred in denying his lesser included instruction request, and that art. 67011-1(b) violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated (DWI), under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(b) (1993). Appellant argued that his due process rights were violated when the police destroyed evidence, that the trial court erred in denying his request for a lesser included offense instruction, and that art. 67001-1(b) violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that appellant's due process rights were not violated, as appellant did not show that the destroyed evidence was material or favorable. The trial court did not err in refusing appellant's request for a lesser included offense instruction, as consumption of alcohol while driving, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 107E(b) (1993), could not be established by proof of the same facts required to establish DWI. The DWI statute, when read in conjunction with the adult probation statute, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 §13(a) (1993), did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as mandatory 30-day confinement as a condition of probation for those convicted of DWI with an open container enhancement was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in the safety of its citizens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated (DWI), holding that the DWI statute, when read in conjunction with the adult probation statute, did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment, as mandatory 30-day confinement as a condition of probation for those convicted of DWI with an open container enhancement was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in the safety of its citizens.

Johnson v. State


No. 05-89-01086-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


864 S.W.2d 708; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3144



September 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied November 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 283rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F89-83817-HT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the court had reversed appellant's conviction for aggravated possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, the Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) vacated the court's judgment and remanded the matter for the court's reconsideration of appellant's suppression argument.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated possession of cocaine with intent to deliver and was sentenced to 50 years' confinement. Originally, the court held the trial court erred in overruling appellant's motion to suppress because the police had neither a reasonable, articulable suspicion nor probable cause to make a warrantless search and because there was insufficient specific articulable facts to justify a temporary detention. The court's judgment was vacated on appeal and the matter was remanded for the court to reconsideration appellant's argument. Appellant challenged the overruling of his motion to suppress under the U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 9. The court determined appellant was seized under the constitutional provisions when he dropped the contraband. Appellant did not voluntarily abandon the contraband. However, the police had probable cause to arrest him for an offense committed within their view and the contraband was recovered in a search incident to that lawful, warrantless arrest. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion. The court held that appellant's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for aggravated possession of cocaine with intent to deliver after finding that the lower court did not err in denying appellant's motion to suppress and appellant's sentence of 50 years' imprisonment did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.

Chong Yee Meng v. State


No. 01-91-01294-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2534



September 16, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 577661.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting and sentencing him for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, on grounds that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (Supp. 1993) was unconstitutional and that he was denied his right to compulsory process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, but his adjudication of guilt was deferred by the lower court. On the prosecution's motion to revoke probation, the lower court adjudicated appellant's guilt and sentenced him to 10 years in prison. Defendant appealed his conviction on grounds that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (Supp. 1993) was unconstitutional as a violation of due process because it denied him his right to compulsory process under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Tex. Const. art. X. The court found that art. 1.15 provided that if defendant entered a voluntary guilty plea, the prosecution was required to provide evidence of defendant's guilt. The plea would be accepted if defendant knowingly waived his constitutional rights. The court found that art. 1.15 was not unconstitutional because it did not prohibit defendant from offering evidence or prohibit the court from considering evidence offered by defendant. The court noted also that there was no requirement that defendant had to specifically waive the right to compulsory process in the record when entering his guilty plea. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle was affirmed because his voluntary guilty plea did not prohibit him from offering evidence in his defense or prohibit the lower court from considering evidence he offered in violation of his state and federal constitutional right to compulsory process. This right was not denied because there no requirement that he specifically waive it when he entered his guilty plea.

Missouri Pac. R.R. Co. v. Lemon


No. A14-91-00652-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


861 S.W.2d 501; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2442



September 2, 1993, Rendered  
September 2, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 239th District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90G0046. J. Ray Gayle, III, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of July 22, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2039.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a railroad company and a train driver for that company, sought review of the judgment of the 239th District Court of Brazoria County, (Texas), which awarded appellees, the husband and representatives of a woman's estate, damages in a suit filed by appellees after a train owned by appellant railroad and driven by appellant driver struck and killed a woman at a crossing that had no signals, gates, or flagman.


OVERVIEW: A train operated by appellant railroad company (railroad) and driven by appellant driver (driver) struck and killed a woman at a crossing that had no signals, gates, or flagman. Appellees, the woman's husband and estate, filed suit against appellants. A jury in the court below determined that the collision was proximately caused by both driver's and railroad's negligence. The jury also determined that the crossing was extra-hazardous, that the collision was proximately caused by railroad's gross negligence in failing to provide automatic signals or a flagman. Actual damages were awarded against both appellants and exemplary damages against railroad. The lower court's judgment in favor of appellees was affirmed on appeal because it the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support the jury's findings, because appellees' state common law claim regarding the absence of proper warning devices was not preempted by federal law, and because the issue of the woman's contributory negligence was properly submitted to the jury. However, the trial court's judgment was modified so the award of exemplary damages would comply with Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.007.


OUTCOME: Damage award in favor of appellees, deceased woman's husband and estate, in appellees' suit against appellants, railroad company and train driver, for negligence was affirmed. While the evidence was sufficient to support the lower court's findings regarding appellants' negligence, the court modified the award of exemplary damages in accordance with a Texas law that allowed such an award to be no more than four times the actual damages.

Christian v. State


No. 05-91-01551-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


865 S.W.2d 198; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3142



August 31, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 195th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F90-50862-N



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 195th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), convicting him, upon revocation of his probation, of unlawful possession with intent to deliver cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of unlawful possession with intent to deliver cocaine and sought review of the judgment revoking his probation. The court affirmed, finding that, absent some evidence that the trial court in fact conducted the review of the magistrate's recommendation after signing the adoption order, appellant had not overcome the presumption of regularity of court proceedings and had not shown noncompliance with the Dallas County (Texas) Magistrates Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 54.301-.313 (1988). The court found that appellant's challenge of the constitutionality of the act was an impermissible collateral attack, as was appellant's attack on the sufficiency of the evidence supporting the underlying judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment revoking appellant's probation and sentencing him to eight years for unlawful possession with intent to deliver cocaine because appellant did not show irregularity in trial court's adoption of magistrate's recommendation.

Southwest Airlines Co. v. Texas High-Speed Rail Auth.


No. 3-92-552-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


863 S.W.2d 123; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2364



August 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled November 10, 1993. Released for Publication November 10, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-3367, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airline challenged a decision of the District Court Of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed, for lack of jurisdiction, appellant's claim for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee Texas High Speed Rail Authority, seeking judicial review of the appellee's decision in awarding a franchise.


OVERVIEW: Appellant airline challenged the trial court's dismissal of its claim for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee Texas High Speed Rail Authority, seeking judicial review of a decision by appellee. Appellee was empowered to award a high-speed rail franchise, and sought applications from potential franchisees, under rules adopted by appellee under the Administrative Procedure and Texas Register Act (Act). Appellant filed a discovery request, which was denied, and then filed suit in the trial court. Appellee awarded the franchise, and appellant filed a second suit for review of appellee's final order. The trial court dismissed both suits. On appeal, the court held that an action for declaratory relief required a real controversy that could be addressed by the court, and that under the facts before it, any decision would merely be an advisory opinion. The court also held that appellant's second suit seeking to declare appellee's action null and void was an attempt to try the case piecemeal, and that the provisions of the Act were not intended to allow appellant that opportunity. The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of appellants' claims for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of appellant airline's claim for declaratory and injunctive relief, holding that because the trial court had not denied appellant's request while an agency proceeding was pending, appellant was not entitled to the relief sought.

Railroad Comm'n v. Arco Oil & Gas Co.


No. 3-91-504-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2365



August 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Corrected September 1, 1993. Withdrawn April 13, 1994. Substituted Opinion of April 13, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 808.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-3140, HONORABLE JAMES R. MEYERS, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad commission sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District (Texas), which declared Statewide Rule 90(b)(2) invalid and enjoined its enforcement. Appellee oil companies had challenged the validity of the rule.


OVERVIEW: Appellee oil companies filed suit pursuant to the Administrative Procedure and Texas Register Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 12 (Supp. 1993), challenging the validity of Statewide Rule 90(b)(2) promulgated by appellant railroad commission. Appellees were operators in a large water-driven oil reservoir and rule 90(b)(2) set the lawful allowable for oil fields. Following a bench trial, the trial court declared the rule invalid and enjoined its enforcement. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, declared the rule valid, and rendered judgment that appellees take nothing by their suit. The court reviewed the adequacy of appellant's reasoned justification under an arbitrary-and-capricious test. The court found that because appellant's final order adopting rule 90(b)(2) contained a facially reasonable explanation of the necessity of the rule to protect correlative rights, and because it appeared that appellant considered the relevant factors in reasoned decisionmaking, the order met the legislative objectives of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 5(c-1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment which found appellant railroad commission's statewide rule invalid because its reasoned justification was adequate under an arbitrary-and-capricious test. The court declared the rule valid and ruled that appellee oil companies take nothing by their suit.

Smith v. Costello


NO. 2-92-170-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


861 S.W.2d 56; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2377



August 25, 1993, Decided  
August 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 153rd DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Sidney C. Farrar, Jr.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the summary judgment and remand for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision from the 153rd District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, physician and hospital, in appellants' medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant parents brought suit against appellees, physician and hospital, alleging acts of medical malpractice in connection with the birth of their son. The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment, holding that the action was barred by the statute of limitations despite appellants' statement by affidavit they did not discover the damage caused to their son until after the limitations period had run. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case because the statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to appellants. They did not discover the possible relation of their son's condition to any alleged negligence on the part of the appellees until the statute of limitations had run, and appellees failed to plead and prove that there was no material fact issue as to whether appellants filed the lawsuit within a reasonable time after they learned of their son's condition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment for appellees, physician and hospital, and remanded the case. The statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to appellant parents where they did not discover the cause of action until the statute of limitations had run, and appellees did not plead or prove that appellants' lawsuit was not filed within a reasonable amount of time after they learned of their son's condition.

United States Brass Corp. v. Andraus


No. 01-89-00614-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2737



August 19, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
August 19, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Overruled December 2, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 3230.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 151st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 87-21479



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed and in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, plumbing suppliers and installers, challenged the judgment of the 151st District Court, Harris County, Texas, which held that they were liable to appellees homeowners, for installing faulty plumbing equipment in their homes, and therefore owed actual and exemplary damages under the theory of gross negligence, and the Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.45(4) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Appellee homeowners bought ready-made houses that contained faulty plumbing equipment from appellants, construction company and plumbing manufactures. Appellees sued appellants for the damages plumbing under the Deceptive Trade Practices Act (DTPA), Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.45(4) (1987), and gross negligence, seeking actual and exemplary damages. The trial court found in favor of appellees, and appellants challenged the ruling. The court held that appellees' actions were not barred by the statute of limitations, as they filed suit within two years of discovering the faulty plumbing. The court also determined that appellees were liable under the DTPA and for gross negligence, even though they did not directly sell the plumbing to appellees, and appellees did not rely on appellant's advertising prior to purchasing the houses. Finally, the court upheld the exemplary damages, stating that it was reasonable to appellants' misconduct, and in proportion to the harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellants, plumbing suppliers and installers, were liable to appellees homeowners for actual and exemplary damages, under the Deceptive Trade Practices Act and for gross negligence on the sale and installation of faulty plumbing equipment in the houses, even though appellants did not directly sell to appellees.

Tyson v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 1ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. SAN AUGUSTINE COUNTY, TEXAS



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 1st Judicial District Court, San Augustine County (Texas), which convicted him of engaging in organized criminal activity, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02 (1989), and assessed punishment at 75 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of engaging in organized criminal activity, namely manufacture and delivery of methamphetamine, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02 (1989), and sentenced to 75 years imprisonment. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant intentionally and knowingly engaged in the criminal conduct. The court found that a rational jury could have found the essential elements of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also determined that when the prosecutor commented on the fact that defendant did not call witnesses to refute the state's theory of the case, he was not improperly commenting on defendant's failure to testify. The court held that the affidavit for the search warrant reflected sufficient probable cause because there was cooperation between law enforcement agencies, and the sum of the information known to the agencies was included in the affidavit. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing a facsimile into evidence because the trial court impliedly found that the state had satisfied the authenticity requirement of Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 901.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of engaging in organized criminal activity and sentenced him to 75 years imprisonment. The evidence was sufficient to prove defendant intentionally and knowingly engaged in the criminal conduct. Further, the prosecutor did not improperly comment on defendant's failure to testify, and the search warrant affidavit reflected sufficient probable cause.

Office of Pub. Ins. Counsel v. Texas Auto. Ins. Plan


No. 3-93-054-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


860 S.W.2d 231; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2230



August 11, 1993, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 92-09771, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state board of insurance and office of public insurance counsel, challenged a summary judgment of the 167th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), finding that appellee agency could amend the rules governing the assigned risk plan for apportioning coverage of high risk applicants among automobile liability insurance companies.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, state Board of Insurance (Board) and Office of Public Insurance Counsel (OPIC), challenged a summary judgment rendered in favor of appellee Texas Automobile Insurance Plan, the administrative agency charged with operating the assigned risk plan for providing motor vehicle liability insurance. Specifically, the trial court found that appellee could amend the rules governing the assigned risk plan for apportioning coverage of high risk applicants among insurance companies providing automobile liability insurance in Texas. Appellee agency was authorized to amend the rules governing the assigned risk plan for apportioning coverage of high risk applicants among automobile liability insurance companies, because such authority was vested in appellee by a valid constitutional statute.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art.4413, §36, appellant sought judicial review by direct appeal of an order issued by appellee Texas Motor Vehicle Commission that required appellant to repurchase parts in connection with the termination of a franchise held by appellee franchisee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant franchisor sought review of an order of appellee Texas Motor Vehicle Commission (Commission) that required it to repurchase parts in connection with the termination of a franchise held by appellee franchisee. Appellant alleged that appellee commission erred in retroactively applying Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 4413, § 36, there was no substantial evidence to support appellee commission's order, and appellee commission acted arbitrarily, abused its discretion, and exceeded its statutory authority in issuing its order. OUTCOME: The order of appellee commission was affirmed because there was no retroactive application of the statute, because appellee commission's order was supported by substantial evidence, and because there was no abuse of discretion by appellee commission in issuing its order.

Tex. Workers' Comp. Comm'n v. Garcia

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


862 S.W.2d 61; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2502



August 11, 1993, Delivered  
August 11, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1]  THIS OPINION WAS RENDERED ON AUGUST 11, 1993 AND A MOTION FOR REHEARING IS PENDING. BECAUSE OF WIDESPEAD INTEREST IN THIS PARTICULAR DECISION, THE COURT WILL RELEASE THE OPINION WITH THE STIPULATION THAT IF THE OPINION IS WITHDRAWN ON REHEARING, THERE WILL BE AN IMMEDIATE WITHDRAWAL OF SAME UPON THIS COURT'S INSTRUCTIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 365th District Court of Maverick County. Trial Court No. 99-11-10301-CV. Honorable Rey Perez, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the decision from the 365th District Court of Maverick County (Texas), which found that plaintiffs had standing to sue and that the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. §§ 8308.1.01-8308.11.01, was unconstitutional because it compensated on the basis of impairment, rather than disability, loss of income or loss of earning capacity.


OVERVIEW: Several plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment that the Workers' Compensation Act (act) was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs contended that portions of the act violated the open courts, due course of law, equal protection, and right to jury trial of the state constitution. The trial court declared the act unconstitutional. On appeal, the commission argued that none of the workers had standing to sue and, therefore, that the court had no jurisdiction. The court found the act was unconstitutional, and that one of the three workers and the union had standing. The court then found that the act violated the open courts doctrine. The court concluded that the act was unconstitutional because it compensated on the basis of impairment, rather than disability, loss of income, or loss of earning capacity. The court also concluded that the use of the American Medical Association guidelines violated the equal protection provisions of the state constitution. The court then concluded that the act's judicial review provisions, which replaced the state's unusual trial de novo system with a system of administrative hearings, denied injured workers their right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that found the Workers' Compensation Act unconstitutional. The court held that the act violated the open courts doctrine and the equal protection clause of the state constitution. The court reversed the trial court's judgment finding that the hybrid judicial review was appropriate.

Wisenbaker v. State


No. 3-91-443-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


860 S.W.2d 681; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2251



August 11, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 22, 1993. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 101,819, HONORABLE BOB JONES, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attacked a jury verdict from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), that found him guilty of failing to remit motor fuel taxes he collected "while acting as a supplier" pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 153.221(a). The state charged that appellant devised and implemented a scheme to avoid paying state fuel taxes by setting up sham corporations and securing illegal purchasing agreements.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned truck stops. He was indicted for avoiding payment of state motor fuel taxes by establishing sham intermediary corporations and obtaining the agreement of a fuel supplier to sell diesel fuel to the truck stops tax free. A jury found appellant guilty of failing to remit motor fuel taxes he collected "while acting as a supplier" pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 153.221(a). The court found, however, that the trial court should not have allowed the extraneous-offense testimony and so reversed the judgment and remanded for a new hearing on punishment.


OUTCOME: The court rejected appellant's various arguments that attacked the substantive bases for his conviction, but reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new hearing on punishment. The court found that the trial court had erred when it allowed extraneous-offense testimony during the punishment phase of the trial.

1363 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Milligan v. State


No. 11-92-268-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


859 S.W.2d 117; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2163



July 29, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 266th District Court of Erath County



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for aggravated assault of a peace officer, entered by the 266th District Court of Erath County (Texas), challenging the constitutionality and application of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02(a)(2)(A) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated assault on a peace officer under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.02(a)(2)(A) (1993). Appellant challenged the constitutionality of § 22.02(a)(2)(A) because it proscribed the same conduct as Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.03 (1993). The court affirmed, finding that the statutes' elements were distinct and defined different offenses: § 38.03(a) proscribed resisting with force a peace officer effecting an arrest or search, and § 2.02(a)(2)(A) proscribed threatening a peace officer with a deadly weapon or threatening to cause or causing bodily while the peace officer was lawfully discharging an official duty. Moreover, § 22.02(a)(2)(A) was sufficiently definite to be understood and sufficiently described what constituted an offense so as to give a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice that his contemplated conduct was forbidden by statute. Finally, the doctrine of in pari materia did not apply, given that the two statutes had different objectives and were not intended to be considered together, and because neither was a special statute, the prosecutor had the discretion to prosecute under the statute he believed to be more appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated assault on a peace officer, holding that the existence of another statute proscribing similar conduct did not violate the constitutional prohibition against legislating different punishments for the same offense where the two acts had different elements and objectives, and the state was free to prosecute under the more appropriate statute to the circumstances.

Nueces County Appraisal Dist. v. Corpus Christi People's Baptist Church


No. 13-92-411-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI

July 29, 1993, Delivered  
July 29, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 117th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order of the 117th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) that ruled that appellee church was entitled to an ad valorem tax exemption for certain portions of its real property for tax years 1986 through 1989, under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.433 (1992). Appellant contended that § 11.433 violated the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.433 (1992), appellee church was entitled to an ad valorem tax exemption for certain portions of its real property for tax years 1986 through 1989. Appellant county sought review, alleging that § 11.433 violated the state constitutional prohibition against forgiveness of taxes. The court reversed, holding that appellant had standing to bring a constitutional challenge. The court found that Tex. Const. art. Thus, the court held that § 11.433 was unconstitutional because it operated to forgive delinquent ad valorem taxes and rendered judgment in favor of appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that entitled appellee church to an ad valorem tax exemption pursuant to a statute which extended the time period for religious organizations to apply for property tax exemptions on property that would otherwise be taxable. The court held that the enabling statute was unconstitutional because it operated to forgive taxes and rendered judgment in favor of appellant county.
