Missouri Pac. R.R. Co. v. Lemon


No. A14-91-00652-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2039



July 22, 1993, Rendered  
July 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn September 2, 1993. Substituted Opinion of September 2, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2442.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 239th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90G0046.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Modified


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a railroad and its engineer, sought review of the judgment of the 239th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas), which awarded over $ 2 million in actual damages and $ 10 million in exemplary damages to appellees, decedent's family and estate, after a jury trial in their wrongful death action after decedent's car was hit by a train at an extra-hazardous railroad crossing.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, the decedent's family and estate, brought a wrongful death action against appellants, a railroad and its engineer, after decedent's car was hit by a train while driving her car across railroad tracks which had no warning lights or gates and where appellant railroad's employees often illegally parked tank cars too close to the crossing. The trial court awarded over $ 12 million in actual and exemplary damages on a jury verdict in which the jury found appellants were negligent in causing the death of decedent. On appeal, the court affirmed, with minor modifications to the award, and found no error by the trial court in the broad form submission jury questions, including the issue of negligence. The court found that jury questions regarding excessive rate of speed were not preempted by the Federal Railroad Safety Act (FRSA), because illegally parked tank cars which obstructed the engineer's view were not a hazard considered when train speed limits were determined under FRSA. Appellants' knowledge that the crossing was dangerous and refusal to remedy the problem raised their conduct from negligent to malicious and, therefore, exemplary damages were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellees, the decedent's family and estate, because appellants, a railroad and its engineer, engaged in malicious conduct by failing to act on their knowledge of a dangerous crossing and were subject to exemplary damages. The court deleted prejudgment interest on future damages as violative of due process and lowered the exemplary damages to conform to four times actual damages as required by statute.

Carraway v. State


No. B14-92-00758-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2028



July 15, 1993, Rendered  
July 15, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9206706.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2 of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of unlawfully carrying a handgun. The trial court denied a motion to suppress evidence of an automatic weapon that was in the back seat of defendant's vehicle and was seized during a temporary detention of defendant for a traffic violation.


OVERVIEW: A police officer heard gunfire from an apartment complex and observed two vehicles exit the complex at an excessive speed. He and other officers surrounded the vehicles. As an officer approached defendant's car, he observed an automatic weapon on the back seat in plain view. Defendant was convicted of unlawfully carrying a handgun under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence because the gun was seized after a warrantless arrest and illegal search. He also argued that the evidence was insufficient to show that a gun in the back seat was carried on his person. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the sound of gunfire and defendant's high rate of speed justified a temporary detention. A traffic violation committed in an officer's presence authorized the initial stop. A warrantless seizure was proper where the officer lawfully made the initial intrusion, the discovery of incriminating evidence was inadvertent, and it was immediately apparent to the police that the seized item was evidence of a crime. A person carried a weapon where he could get his hands on it without materially altering his position.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for unlawfully carrying a handgun was affirmed because a warrantless seizure of the weapon was permitted when a police officer lawfully made the initial intrusion, incriminating evidence was discovered inadvertently, and it was immediately apparent to the police that the item was evidence of a crime.

State v. Gambling Device


No. 01-92-00045-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


859 S.W.2d 519; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1944



July 8, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 590,324.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the 184th District Court for Harris County (Texas) denying its petition for forfeiture filed pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 18.18.


OVERVIEW: The state instituted forfeiture proceedings pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 18.18, to seize a gambling device. The trial court denied the petition on the grounds that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 47.06 and 47.01(3) -- the statutes prohibiting possession of a gambling device and defining gambling device -- were unconstitutionally vague. The court of appeals reversed. Contrary to appellee's assertions, the statutes were not vague merely because they failed to specify the degree of chance necessary for an award to be determined by chance. The statutory definition of a gambling device clearly encompassed any contrivances that incorporated any element of chance, even if the exercise of skill also influenced the outcome.


OUTCOME: The order denying the state's petition for forfeiture of a gambling device was reversed because the statute prohibiting the possession of a gambling device was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1368 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Texas Water Comm'n v. City of Fort Worth


No. 3-92-502-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1923



July 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 2, 1994. Released for Publication March 2, 1994. Withdrawn March 2, 1994. Substituted Opinion of March 2, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 407.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-11240, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and state commission, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), that found for appellee city and reversed an order of appellant state commission in a dispute regarding a wastewater treatment contract. Appellants contended that appellant commission had authority to reform the contract without making certain findings under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 13.043(j) (Supp. 1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellee city provided wastewater treatment services under contract to appellant city. Appellee raised the rate for these services, and appellant city challenged the increase before appellant commission. Appellant commission established a rate more favorable to appellant city, but on district court review this order was reversed and remanded to appellant commission. The court affirmed this judgment. The court held that appellant commission had the authority to establish the rate for the service, but only after it had made a factual determination under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 13.043(j) (Supp. 1993) that the existing rate was unreasonably preferential, prejudicial, or discriminatory. Remand for a hearing on this point was proper. Appellant commission had jurisdiction to hear appellant city's petition pursuant to Tex. Water Code Ann. § 13.043(f) (Supp. 1993), and this review did not impair the obligation of contracts in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 16. The court also held that appellee's objection to the rate modification was not procedurally barred, as appellee had adequately raised the "public interest" finding grounds before appellant commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that reversed and remanded the order of appellant state commission. The court held that although appellant commission had jurisdiction to review the wastewater treatment contract rate, before it could modify that rate it had to find that the existing rate was unreasonably preferential, prejudicial, or discriminatory.

 

1369 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Risk Managers Int'l v. State


No. 3-93-022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


858 S.W.2d 567; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1925



July 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 25, 1993. Released for Publication August 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 299TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 471,568, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order of the 299th District Court for Travis County (Texas) granting a permanent injunction in favor of the State of Texas and the State Board of Insurance that prohibited appellants from engaging in the unauthorized business of insurance in Texas.


OVERVIEW: The State of Texas and the State Board of Insurance sought a permanent injunction to prevent appellants from engaging in the unauthorized business of insurance in the state. The trial court granted the injunction and the court affirmed. Appellants did not fall within the exemption of Tex. Ins. Code Ann. § 2(b)(4). That section provided that the insurance business did not include transactions involving contracts of insurance independently procured through negotiations occurring entirely outside of the state. However, the insureds in this case were physically located in Texas and appellants sent insurance information to and negotiated contracts with prospective clients in Texas. Therefore, Texas had the right to regulate appellants' conduct.


OUTCOME: The order granting a permanent injunction against appellants and prohibiting them from engaging in the unauthorized business of insurance in Texas was affirmed because the State of Texas was authorized to regulate insurance transactions where an insured domiciled in Texas obtained insurance by negotiations occurring in whole or in part inside Texas borders.

Ortega v. State


No. 3-91-251-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


860 S.W.2d 561; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2228



July 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 11, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97,702, HONORABLE BOB JONES, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the District Court, Travis County (Texas) that revoked his probation. Appellant asserted that the conditions of probation requiring him to perform community service and submit to urine testing at the direction of a probation officer were invalid, and the finding that his probation should be revoked because he failed to pay fines was not supported by the evidence.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed an order that revoked appellant's probation, holding that the trial court abused its discretion in revoking appellant's probation when the state failed to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that appellant had violated the terms of his probation. The court held that the condition that required appellant to perform community service was not valid because it did not designate a community service program nor specify the organization or organizations for which appellant would work. The court held that the condition that appellant submit to urine testing at the direction of his probation officer was not valid, because it was an improper delegation of authority to the probation officer. Finally, with regard to delinquent balances on costs and fines, the court held that the state had not established that appellant willfully failed or refused to work at suitable employment or that appellant's failure to make these payments was intentional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the revocation of appellant's probation, holding that the condition that appellant perform community service was not valid because no organization was designated, and the condition that appellant submit urine samples for testing at the direction of the probation officer was an improper delegation of authority. The court found that the state failed to prove that appellant's failure to pay fines was intentional.

Raitano v. Texas Dep't of Pub. Safety


No. 01-90-00096-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


860 S.W.2d 549; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1904



July 1, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
July 1, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Civil Court At Law. No. 3 of Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 534,434. Carolyn Day Hobson, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged a judgment of the Harris County Civil Court at Law (Texas), which held that appellant was a habitual reckless or negligent driver under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 22(b)(3) (Supp. 1993), and ordered a one year suspension of appellant's driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver challenged the suspension of his driver's license for one year under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6687b, § 22(b)(3), which authorized such a suspension upon a finding that appellant was a habitual reckless or negligent driver. The court affirmed. The statute was not rendered unconstitutionally vague by its failure to further define "habitually reckless or negligent driver," because the vagueness test was less strict where the statute did not impose a criminal penalty or threaten the exercise of any constitutional rights. The statutory language provided appellant with fair warning that an average of eight traffic violations per year for three years could result in license suspension. The trial court permissibly relied upon 15 speeding convictions as evidence of negligence. Finally, two claimed points of error were rejected, because appellant failed to include citations to supporting authority in his brief pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 74(f).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that appellant was a habitual reckless or negligent driver whose license should be suspended for one year, because the statute authorizing the suspension was not unconstitutionally vague and the judgment was supported by appellant's numerous speeding and other traffic violations.

Albertson's, Inc. v. Ortiz

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN

June 30, 1993, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 489,043, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grocery store challenged a judgment from the 126th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), awarding appellees, two union supporters, damages on a jury verdict for appellant's infringement of appellees' free-speech rights under the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant grocery store challenged an adverse judgment rendered on a jury verdict that awarded damages to appellees, two voluntary union supporters, for infringement on appellees' free speech rights under the Texas Constitution. Appellees were stationed on the sidewalk outside of appellant's main entrance handing out leaflets and soliciting signatures in support of a national boycott of California grapes. The manager of the store called the police after appellees refused to leave the premises. Appellees were arrested for criminal trespass and later acquitted. Appellees filed suit against appellant and were awarded damages for appellant's unreasonable interference with their freedom of speech. The court reversed, declining to recognize a compensatory cause of action to redress a wholly private entity's infringement of free speech rights guaranteed by the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. Appellee union supporters were not entitled to damages for appellant grocery store's alleged infringement of their constitutional free speech rights, because the state constitution did not create such a cause of action to support the award of damages against appellant.

Nieto v. State


NUMBER 13-92-134-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


857 S.W.2d 149; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1899



June 30, 1993, Delivered  
June 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from County Court at Law No. 4 of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: We reverse and remand.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, after a bench trial in the County Court at Law No. 4 of Nueces County (Texas), of unlawfully carrying a weapon. The trial court sentenced him to 90 days in jail. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the search and seizure that uncovered the weapon was illegal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a member of a motorcycle gang, was stopped at a police checkpoint. The officers were attempting to locate certain gang members with outstanding warrants and were checking the driver's licenses of all individuals wearing gang jackets. An officer performed a patdown search of defendant and found a handgun. Defendant was convicted of unlawfully carrying a weapon after the trial court denied his motion to suppress. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding the search and seizure violated defendant's constitutional rights. The checkpoint intruded on drivers' privacy without a reasonable public interest justification. The police did not know whether the wanted individuals were in the area of the checkpoint, and targeting individuals according to their attire was impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction for unlawfully carrying a weapon and remanded because the stop of defendant's vehicle was illegal.

Villarreal v. State


No. 13-91-598-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


860 S.W.2d 529; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1913



June 30, 1993, Delivered  
June 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled August 31, 1993. Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 36th District Court of San Patricio County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Having overruled all points of error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 36th District Court of San Patricio County, Texas, that convicted him of carrying an illegal knife on school grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for carrying an illegal knife on school grounds. He assigned error to the procedures surrounding the finding that he was competent to stand trial at his original guilty plea and at the adjudication of guilt. The court affirmed, finding that appellant was examined at a previously scheduled Texas Rehabilitation Commission (TRC) examination, not by court order. There was no evidence that the prosecutor had any knowledge of the examination or its result; therefore, the prosecutor had not improperly withheld such information. The trial court had not duty to sua sponte examine retroactively appellant's competence and mens rea at his previous plea. Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 46.02 was not unconstitutional. The standard for incompetence, as set out in Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 46.02, § 1, was the same whether the person was mentally ill, mentally retarded, or both. Each category was equally protected.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant's conviction for carrying an illegal knife on school grounds was upheld, because there was no error in finding that appellant was competent to stand trial both at his original plea and at the adjudication of guilt.

Texas Water Comm'n v. Boyt Realty Co.


No. 3-91-279-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


10 S.W.3d 334; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2037



June 23, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-1519, HONORABLE JOE DIBRELL, JUDGE PRESIDING.

Originally Published April 7, 1993 and Withdrawn by Order of the Court May 20, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 974.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered in Part; Affirmed in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, water commission, water reserve, and rice producers, all challenged orders by the 126th District Court for Travis County (Texas), which prohibited appellant water commission from setting water rates for any year after 1990 because it lacked jurisdiction. Appellant water reserve claimed error on evidentiary, procedural, and constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, group of customers, challenged the water prices set by appellant water reserve. Appellees then took their grievances to appellant water commission for review. After hearing evidence, appellant water commission set a price at about $ 18 less than appellant water reserve's price and also held that until future contracts were negotiated the prices would remain in effect. Appellant water reserve cross-appealed to the district could, claiming that appellant water commission lacked jurisdiction to set prospective rates. The district court affirmed the price set by appellant water commission but also agreed with appellant water reserve that it overstepped it's jurisdiction. Appellant water commission appealed along with appellant rice grower. The court held that a customer could file a petition under Tex. Water Code § 11.041(a), which would then invoke appellant water commission's jurisdiction to set reasonable rates without time restrictions. It also held that the supplier was then free to contract with that customer for future water prices. The court reversed only the portion of district court's order limiting appellant water commission's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The district court's order that found that the price set by appellant water commission was proper was affirmed, but the portion of the order that found that appellant water commission lacked jurisdiction to set prospective rates past the year 1990 was reversed. It held that because appellant water commission's findings were appealable by way of petition, and because it set reasonable rates, the prospective nature of the order was permissible.

Felan v. Ramos


No. 13-92-007-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


857 S.W.2d 113; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1657



June 10, 1993, Delivered  
June 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled July 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, family of decedent, sought review of an order of the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which granted a motion for summary judgment to appellees, surgeon and hospital, dismissing appellants' medical malpractice, survival, and wrongful death claims as being barred under the two-year statute of limitations period under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Decedent was left mentally incapacitated after a surgery that had been performed by appellee surgeon and later died. Appellants, family of decedent, filed suit against appellees, surgeon and hospital, asserting claims for medical malpractice, survival of decedent's cause of action, and wrongful death. The lower court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment dismissing appellants' claims as being barred under the two- year statute of limitations period under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1993). The court reversed and remanded the order of the lower court because the application of the two-year statute of limitations to decedent's medical malpractice claim violated the Open Courts Provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court held that the application of the two-year statute of limitations restricted decedent's claim for malpractice because her mental incapacity hindered the awareness of the existence of the claim until after of her death. The court further held that appellants' survival and wrongful death claims were viable because the malpractice claim was not barred under the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's granting of a motion for summary judgment to appellees surgeon and hospital dismissing appellants' medical malpractice, survival, and wrongful death claims as being barred under the two-year statute of limitations because decedent's mental incapacity, until the time of her death, tolled the statute of limitations.

Roberts v. State


No. A14-92-01042-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1601

June 3, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 624154.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of carrying a weapon on a premises licensed to sale alcoholic beverages, felony mischief, and possession of a controlled substance, and assessed punishment at thirty years confinement.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed appellant walking away from a nightclub in a suspicious manner and saw appellant tossing an object. The officer detained appellant, retrieved the object, and found that it was a gun. The trial court convicted appellant of carrying a weapon on a premises licensed to sell alcoholic beverages, and appellant sought review. The court held that appellant's admissions that he was on premises of the nightclub together with the officer's testimony was clearly sufficient to sustain the conviction. Appellant also contended trial counsel's assistance was ineffective because counsel did not obtain a hearing on a pretrial motion to suppress allegedly illegal evidence before its introduction to the jury, and did not object to officer testimony that enabled state to bolster witness credibility concerning drug activity in the nightclub area. The court determined that appellant's seizure occurred after he voluntarily abandoned the gun, therefore seizure was legal, and witness testimony was admissible to explain the circumstances of appellant's arrest. Therefore appellant did not show that trial counsel was deficient. Accordingly the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because the evidence was clearly sufficient to support the conviction and appellant did not show that he was prejudiced by trial counsel's defense.

McMahan v. Naylor


NUMBER 13-92-397-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


855 S.W.2d 193; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1541



May 27, 1993, Delivered  
May 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court of Refugio County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the county court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the County Court of Refugio County, Texas, that granted summary judgment to appellees on appellant's petition to declare heirship under Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 48 (1980). Appellants were the named beneficiaries of their deceased father's will, and appellant's petition sought to establish that the decedent was also his father.


OVERVIEW: A father wrote a will leaving property to appellees. After the father died, appellant filed a petition under Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 48 (1980) in a county court to declare heirship. Appellant alleged that the decedent was also his father. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that § 48, which governed proceedings to declare heirship, applied only to matters of intestacy. However, the decedent had died undisputedly with a will and, therefore, § 48 was inapplicable. The court noted that even if appellant had established that he was an heir, the probated and executed will was the only means through which title could be vested and property transferred. The court also noted that, as a matter of law, if a will described legatees as a class but also identified them by name or number, then the devise was not to a class but to individuals. The will in this case specifically addressed each appellant by name. The court did not make a determination as to whether or not Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01(a) (1993) regarding establishment of paternity had an unconstitutional time limitation for establishing paternity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for appellees in appellant's action to declare heirship. The court held that the statute under which appellant filed his petition to establish heirship only governed property that passed intestate. Because the decedent, appellant's alleged father, did not die intestate, the court held that the statute was inapplicable to appellant's case.

Kellum v. State


No. 01-92-00743-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1557



May 27, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 617,511.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance: cocaine. The trial court overruled defendant's motion to suppress evidence on the basis of the protection granted by U.S. Const. amend IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance: cocaine. Evidence was obtained from defendant's bag at a bus station. The police asked defendant some questions, and he responded that he had no identification and that he had no drugs on him or in his bag. Defendant consented to a search of his bag, and cocaine was found. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress made under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that because defendant was not stopped illegally and because he consented to the police search of his bag, the police search without a warrant or probable cause was reasonable. The court determined that defendant was not illegally detained because there was no confrontation between him and the police. In the absence of a confrontation, a reasonable person would have believed that he was free to go, and no seizure occurred. The court rejected defendant's argument that the statute under which he was charged, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(a) (1992), was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, cocaine. The court found that there was no confrontation between defendant and the police prior to the search of his bag. The court also found that the search was consensual. Therefore, the court held that defendant was not illegally detained and that there was a reasonable search in the absence of a warrant or probable cause.

Watts v. State


No. 09-92-228 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


856 S.W.2d 246; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1824



May 26, 1993, Delivered  
May 26, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 217th District Court. Angelina County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 16,313. David Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the 217th District Court, Angelina County (Texas) of aggravated sexual assault, and the 40-year sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. The state's motion to allow the testimony of appellant's victim, a 10-year-old boy, to be taken in a room other than the courtroom and viewed by the jury via closed circuit television was granted pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 38.071 (1993). Appellant sought review, arguing that his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to be confronted with the witness against him was violated, as well as his right of confrontation pursuant to Tex. Const. art. 1, § 10. In affirming his conviction, the court held that the right of confrontation did not afford the right of face-to-face confrontation. Appellant posed no objection to the testimony or to the procedure employed to conduct the examination. Because article 38.071 was not facially unconstitutional, a timely objection was necessary to preserve the complaint of denial of confrontation. Appellant did not object to the testimony of the child's treating psychiatrist on the grounds that he was not the first outcry witness, therefore, he could not complain that the psychiatrist's testimony was considered in determining whether the child was available to testify for article 38.071 purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault, holding that appellant failed to preserve any objection because he did not object at the time of trial to the viewing by the jury of the victim's testimony via closed-circuit television. The court ruled that because the statute was not facially unconstitutional, a timely objection was necessary to preserve his complaint of denial of confrontation.

 

1384 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Glyn-Jones v. Bridgestone/Firestone, Inc.


No. 05-91-01704-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


857 S.W.2d 640; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2189



May 21, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 134th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-12292-G



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, Reversed and Remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a summary judgment from the 134th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), entered on appellee manufacturer's motion in appellants' product liability action. Appellants contended that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 107C(j) (Supp. 1992), did not prohibit introduction of seat belt evidence in a crashworthiness case, or alternatively, this statute violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sustained injuries when a seat belt system in their car failed on impact with another vehicle. The application of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 107C(j) (Supp. 1992) by the trial court to bar evidence of seat belt use effectively precluded appellants from prosecuting their action on a crashworthiness theory. The court held that § 107C(j) barred the type of evidence appellants sought to introduce. The language of the statute was clear and unambiguous that it applied to all civil actions, and the court would not make an exception for product liability cases. The court sustained, however, appellant's constitutional challenge to the application of the statute in this case. Applying a two-part test under the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, the court found that the statute restricted a well-recognized cause of action, in that crashworthiness had been recognized for some years. The court then held that as the overriding purpose of § 107C(j) was to save lives, abolition of the crashworthiness doctrine was unreasonable and contrary to the legislative intent of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that the seat belt law was unconstitutional to the extent it prohibited the introduction of seat belt evidence in a crashworthiness action. The court affirmed the judgment to the extent of appellants' breach of warranty claim.

 

1385 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Thanheiser v. State


NO. B14-92-00824 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


855 S.W.2d 112; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1370



May 13, 1993, Rendered  
May 13, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petitions for Discretionary Review Refused October 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court. at Law No. 8. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-21040.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of operating his automobile on a public street with an expired inspection sticker. Appellant contended it was error for the trial court to deny his motion that contended Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 140 (Supp. 1992) was violative of Tex. Const. art. 3, § 56 as a special law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with operating his automobile on a public street with an expired inspection sticker in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 140 (Supp. 1992). Appellant filed a motion to dismiss, contending the statute was in violation of Tex. Const. art. 3, § 56 as a special law because it provided certain exceptions from the inspection requirement that did not have a rational basis. The trial court denied the motion, appellant was convicted, and he thereafter sought review. The court affirmed the conviction and the denial of appellant's motion to dismiss, finding that the statute was not unconstitutional because there was a rational and reasonable basis for the exceptions from its inspection requirement. The court determined that the vehicles excepted from inspection were not specifically designed or intended to transport people and property over the roads of the state, while the vehicles that were required to be inspected were so specifically designed and operated. The court concluded that the statute was directed to insure that those vehicles whose primary purpose was to transport people and property over the public streets were safe to operate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant for operating his automobile on a public street with an expired inspection sticker, finding that the charging statute was not unconstitutional. The court determined that the exceptions from the vehicle inspection requirement in the statute pertained to those vehicles not specifically designed or operated to transport people and property over the roads of the state.

Marchal v. Webb


No. 01-92-00897-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


859 S.W.2d 408; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1377



May 13, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
May 13, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-019737.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of March 18, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 792.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the judgment of 11th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor in a medical malpractice case; appellant filed a motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient challenged the summary judgment granted in favor of appellee doctor in a medical malpractice case. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred because the statute of limitations had not run, and because appellee failed to show no genuine issue of material fact concerning appellant's allegations of fraudulent concealment and lack of discovery. The court found that appellant's alleged injury occurred on the date of either of two surgeries. Thus, it would have been incorrect to apply the date of appellant's last visit to appellee as the trigger for the statute of limitations, as she argued. Appellant's first point of error was overruled. Appellant also argued that if the limitations began to run on the date of her second surgery, her suit was still timely because of the doctrines of fraudulent concealment and lack of discovery. The court found that appellant failed to plead that the application of the statute of limitations to her was unconstitutional and in violation of the open courts provision of the state constitution. It also found that her reliance on the discovery rule was misplaced. Appellant's second point was overruled. The judgment below was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment granted in favor of appellee doctor was affirmed, and appellant patient's motion for rehearing was denied because the court found that appellant's claims were barred by the strict two-year statute of limitations pertaining to medical malpractice cases.

 

1387 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bank One, N.A. v. Ameritrust Tex., N.A.


No. 05-92-01324-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


858 S.W.2d 516; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2173



May 7, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Probate Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-3744-P2B



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank challenged an order of the Probate Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee subsidiary trust company in an action to determine the proper executor of a decedent's will.


OVERVIEW: Appellee subsidiary trust company filed an application for probate of a will, and sought a declaration that it was the proper executor of such will. Appellant bank answered, and also counterclaimed for declaratory judgment. The probate court granted summary judgment to appellee. The decedent had appointed an affiliated bank, and its successors, as executor of his will. The affiliated bank entered into a substitution agreement with appellee, prior to the death of the decedent, pursuant to the substitute fiduciary act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 548h, § 2(a) (1993). Subsequently, the affiliated bank was declared insolvent, and the FDIC transferred all its obligations and assets to a bridge bank, which later became appellant. The appellate court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of appellee, holding that appellee acquired the right to the will when it entered into the substitution agreement with the affiliated bank. In so ruling, the court held that the will, as an inchoate right to a contingent future benefit, constituted property which could be acquired in such a transaction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the probate court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee subsidiary trust company, which ruled that appellee and not appellant bank, was the executor of a will, because appellee acquired the right to the decedent's will under the substitute fiduciary act when it entered into a substitution agreement with the affiliated bank, named as executor in the will, even though the decedent was not yet dead at that time.

Vuong Van Nguyen v. State


NO. 01-92-00734-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1330



May 6, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 584,610.  



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant on a charge of aggravated robbery based on his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with aggravated robbery and entered a guilty plea. The trial court found that the evidence presented by the state substantiated appellant's guilt and deferred adjudication, and assessed a fine. The state later filed a motion to adjudicate guilt, alleging three subsequent aggravated robberies. Appellant pled not true. The trial court adjudicated appellant's guilt and assessed punishment. Appellant argued that the trial court committed fundamental error in convicting him under the provisions of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1993), contending that the statute was unconstitutional because it allowed a bench trial in which the trial judge could not consider any evidence offered by the defense, denying appellant his right to compulsory process and violating due process of law. Appellant also argued that the trial court committed fundamental error in entering a judgment of guilt after his bench trial in which the record was silent on a waiver of appellant's right to compulsory process. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that appellant waived his right to compulsory process and that express waiver of such right was not required in Texas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted appellant of aggravated robbery based on his guilty plea. The court held that appellant waived his right to compulsory process and that express waiver of such right was not required in Texas.

 

1389 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Root v. Brodhead


NO. 3-92-189-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


854 S.W.2d 706; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1631



May 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion to Publish Granted June 9, 1993. Released for Publication June 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 91-7910, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured in an accident involving insured, appealed a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), that granted summary judgment to defendant receiver for insurance carrier in an action filed under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28, § 3(h) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Insurer was in receivership when injured plaintiffs filed claims with defendant receiver, pursuant to Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28, § 3 (1993), seeking approval of their claims against the insurer and payment for injuries plaintiffs sustained in a collision with the insured. Plaintiffs received written notice from the receiver that he rejected their claims so they brought a de novo action in court under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28, § 3(h) (1993). The court held that a receiver could have approved such a claim if plaintiffs had presented evidence that they would have been able to obtain a judgment against the insured. In an earlier case against the insured, a jury declined to find that insured's negligence, if any, caused the collision and plaintiffs' resulting injuries. Plaintiffs took nothing. The court affirmed the summary judgment order for defendant, holding that plaintiffs' claims were barred by collateral estoppel as a consequence of the earlier judgment in which plaintiffs failed to recover on their negligence action. It was sufficient that plaintiffs were parties in the first suit and therefore collateral estoppel was proper against them in the second.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for defendant receiver in a suit filed by plaintiffs upon a rejected claim, holding that plaintiffs were barred by collateral estoppel after failing to prove the negligence of an insured in a separate negligence action. A showing of negligence of the insured was a requirement for defendant's liability. Defendant did not need to be a party in the first proceeding to be protected by collateral estoppel.

Smith v. State


No. 05-91-01264-CR, No. 05-91-01265-CR, No. 05-91-01266-CR, No. 05-91-01267-CR, No. 05-91-01268-CR, No. 05-91-01269-CR, No. 05-91-01270-CR, No. 05-91-01271-CR, No. 05-91-01272-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


857 S.W.2d 71; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1909



April 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 5. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. F91-30181-L, F91-33881-L, F91-31646-IL, F91-40385-JL, F91-41390-JL, F91-41607-L, F91-41631-HL, F91-41834-HL, F91-42661-NL. Hon. Pat McDowell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of the judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 5, Dallas County (Texas), convicting him of nine separate cases of robbery and aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, appellant criminal defendant pleaded guilty to nine separate cases of robbery and aggravated robbery. The trial court assessed a 35-year sentence in each case, to run concurrently. On review, appellant contended the trial court erred in accepting his guilty pleas because the trial court did not properly admonish him; the sentence imposing court costs was unconstitutional; and the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions. The court held the admonishments the trial court gave complied with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13 (Vernon 1989), and found that appellant voluntarily entered his pleas of guilty and the trial court's acceptance of appellant's guilty pleas did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights. The court did not decide whether appellant's confinement for costs violated his due process and equal protection rights because the costs were not the cause of appellant's confinement. Further, the court held appellant's sworn testimony that he was guilty as charged in the indictment, without elaboration, was enough to sustain the court's verdict of guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's convictions because the trial court properly admonished him; the trial court's acceptance of appellant's guilty pleas did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights; the provision of his sentence imposing court costs was not unconstitutional; and the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions.

Brink v. Ayre


NO. B14-91-01278-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


855 S.W.2d 44; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1186



April 29, 1993, Rendered  
April 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 312th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 87-36100. Richard Millard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of the judgment of the 312th District Court, Harris County (Texas), denying his application for turnover relief of money which a receiver returned to appellee debtor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant creditor was an intervening party in appellee debtor's divorce proceeding and obtained a judgment against appellee for $ 6,000. The divorce decree established a receivership in which appellee paid the receiver the money distributed to him by virtue of his partnership interest in his law firm. Appellant filed an application for turnover relief, requesting payment of the unpaid debt out of the balance of any money which the receiver returned to appellee. The trial court denied the turnover request. On review, appellant contended the trial court abused its discretion in denying appellant turnover relief. The court found the balance of appellee's distribution was non-exempt property because legal fees did not qualify as current wages. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that it was not automatically mandated to order a turnover of the funds because under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 31.002 (1986), the trial court had the discretion to consider other relevant factors in deciding whether to grant, deny, or modify turnover relief. Because the trial court could have decided the matter in favor of either party, the court found no abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying appellant creditor's application for turnover relief because the trial court did not abuse its discretion.

Parker v. White


No. 12-91-00189-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


852 S.W.2d 748; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1227



April 28, 1993, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 123RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PANOLA COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioners sought review of a decision from the 123rd Judicial District Court, Panola County (Texas), granting appellee taxpayer's application for writ of mandamus requiring appellants to hold a tax rollback election pursuant to Tex. Tax Code § 26.07 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant commissioners adopted a tax rate that exceeded the rollback tax rate. As provided in Tex. Tax Code § 26.07 (1992) (§ 26.07), appellee taxpayer petitioned appellant to hold a rollback election to allow voters to decide whether or not to reduce the tax rate to the rollback rate. Appellants found that appellee's petition was invalid because conflicting precedent held that § 26.07 did not apply to counties. After § 26.07 was declared constitutional as applied to counties, the lower court found the petition valid, granted appellee's application for writ of mandamus, and ordered appellants to hold the election. Appellants argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the findings that appellee presented them with a petition that was adequate under § 26.07. The court noted that appellee had the burden to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he had submitted a valid petition. Appellants timely found under § 26.07 that the petition was invalid due to constitutional concerns. That did not relieve appellee of his burden to prove the validity of the petition. Because the evidence was legally insufficient, the judgment was reversed and rendered for appellants.


OUTCOME: The judgment that appellee taxpayer's petition was valid and required appellant commissioners to hold a rollback tax election was reversed and rendered in appellants' favor. Appellee did not meet his burden under statute to prove that the petition was valid; thus, the evidence was insufficient to support the lower court's judgment.

Knighton v. International Business Machs. Corp.


No. 01-91-01285-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


856 S.W.2d 206; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1136



April 22, 1993, Rendered and Delivered  
April 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-02548. Mark Davidson, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband appealed from the order of the 11th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, ex-wife, employer and employer's retirement plan, in appellant's declaratory action to enjoin enforcement of a Florida judgment which included an income deduction order. Appellee ex-wife sought review of the trial court's denial of her motion for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-husband sought a declaratory judgment action to enjoin enforcement of a Florida court garnishment judgement obtained by appellee ex-wife. The judgment ordered appellees, employer and employer's retirement plan, to deduct alimony from his income. Appellant argued that the Florida order was an illegal garnishment under the laws and the Texas Constitution. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, and awarded attorney fees to appellees, employer and retirement plan. On appeal, the court held that it was required to give full faith and credit to rulings of foreign courts even if the order offended Texas public policy. The grant of summary judgment was affirmed because Texas courts were not being asked to issue an order to garnish wages for a foreign judgment, which would violate Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 8, they were only being asked to allow a garnishment to occur. The court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court in awarding attorney fees to appellees, employer and retirement plan, as "innocent stakeholders," and in denying attorney fees to appellee ex-wife.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellees, ex-wife, ex-husband's employer, and employer's retirement plan, because Texas courts were not being asked to issue a garnishment order for a foreign judgment, which would violate the law and Texas Constitution, they were only being asked to allow a garnishment to occur. The court found no abuse of discretion in the denial of attorney fees to appellee ex-wife.

Naughton v. Burr/Krest Invs.


No. 01-92-01010-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1088



April 15, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Denied September 16, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2564. Withdrawn September 16, 1993. Substituted Opinion of September 16, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 2564.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 91-028436.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as reformed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of an order of the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that granted appellee investment bank's motion for summary judgment in its suit to recover under a promissory note and that awarded appellee attorney fees and post-judgment interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant debtor executed a promissory note to a bank, which became insolvent and assigned the note to appellee investment bank. After appellant defaulted, appellee filed suit to recover under the note. Appellee's motion for summary judgment was granted, and appellee was awarded attorney fees and post-judgment interest. Appellant sought review. The court held that appellant waived the objections he raised on appeal to appellee's summary judgment motion because he did not raise the same objections before the trial court. The court determined that appellant also waived his challenge to the award of attorney fees because he raised the challenge for the first time on appeal and did not raise it by written motion, answer, or response to appellee's motion for summary judgment. Appellee conceded that the post-judgment interest awarded had to be reduced to the contract rate under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 5069-1.05 because the contract rate was lower than the statutory rate. The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment and attorney fees to appellee and reformed the judgment to reflect the correct interest rate.


OUTCOME: The order granting summary judgment and awarding attorney fees to appellee investment bank was affirmed because appellant debtor waived the challenges to the motion and the attorney fee request by failing to present the challenges to the trial court. Based on appellee's concession, the portion of the order awarding appellee post-judgment interest was reformed to reflect the lower contract rate required by statute.

Texas Water Comm'n v. Lindsey


No. 09-91-300 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


855 S.W.2d 750; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1642



April 15, 1993, Delivered  
April 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 13, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 1st Judicial District Court. Jasper County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 15,088. Joe Bob Golden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Texas Water Commission, challenged a final declaratory judgment entered by the 1st District Court of Jasper County, Texas, which clarified a prior order that declared Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 361.181 through 361.202 and §§ 361.230 through 361.345 unconstitutional in an underlying action involving appellant's determination that appellees were "potentially responsible parties" for a Superfund site.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the Texas Water Commission, determined that appellees were "potentially responsible parties" (PRP) liable for costs, fees, and duties on a proposed Superfund site pursuant to Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 361.181 through 361.202 and §§ 361.230 through 361.345. In a declaratory judgment action brought by appellees, the trial court determined the sections were unconstitutional. Appellant challenged the order entered by the trial court on remand, that clarified the basis for its prior declaration. Because appellees' basic complaint went directly to appellant's PRP determination, the appellate court held that the judgment constituted a direct declaration regarding an attack on the constitutionality of appellant's PRP decision and not an attack on the constitutionality of the legislation itself. In accordance with its prior holding that the statutory sections established venue in the District Court of Travis County, Texas, for appeals relating to actions taken by appellant, the appellate court reversed the judgment entered by the trial court and remanded to the trial court with instructions to dismiss for want of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment that declared the statutes at issue unconstitutional was reversed and remanded with instructions for the trial court to dismiss for want of jurisdiction because the declaration actually concerned the constitutionality of the "potentially responsible party" determination made by appellant, the Texas Water Commission, which fell within the exclusive jurisdiction of another court, and not the constitutionality of the statute itself.

 

1396 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. State


No. 13-92-042-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


853 S.W.2d 157; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1003



April 8, 1993, Delivered  
April 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 15, 1993. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied October 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Court at Law of Kleberg County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: We REVERSE the judgment of the trial court and REMAND the case to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the County Court at Law of Kleberg County (Texas), which denied defendant's motion to suppress and convicted defendant for driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (1993) pursuant to a guilty plea. Defendant alleged the evidenced was illegally obtained during an unconstitutional roadblock.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff's office operated a checkpoint to conduct a driver's license and insurance check on all vehicles at the checkpoint. Defendant was arrested at the checkpoint after a sobriety test and later appealed his conviction for driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (1993), alleging the roadblock was for general investigatory purposes violating the U.S. Const. amend IV. The state argued the checkpoint was for the legitimate purpose of examining drivers' licenses and was based on the department's written policy. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction and judgment denying the motion to suppress and remanded to the trial court, finding that the seizure of defendant violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV, and holding that the checkpoint was unconstitutional, a subterfuge for general investigation, and there was no evidence it was legislatively developed. The court balanced a law enforcement practice against the promotion of legitimate governmental interests.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction for driving while intoxicated and denial of defendant's motion to suppress, and remanded to the trial court, holding that the evidence was illegally obtained because the seizure violated the Fourth Amendment and that the state failed to prove the roadblock was a policy legislatively developed and that the permissiveness of law enforcement practices was balanced against legitimate governmental interests.

 

1397 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence v. Kohl


NO. 01-92-00133-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


853 S.W.2d 697; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 1005



April 8, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1]  CERTIFIED FOR PARTIAL PUBLICATION.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 246th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 84-67711.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, ex-wife and her attorney, sought review of a judgment of the 246th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted sanctions against appellant ex-wife's attorney and held appellant ex-wife in contempt for failure to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: Appellee ex-husband filed a motion to enforce a child support order against appellant ex-wife. Appellant ex-wife's attorney filed a response and attached a proposed order awarding sanctions against ex-husband and his attorney, which was signed by the trial judge. Appellees filed a motion to set aside the sanction order against them sought sanctions against appellant ex-wife's attorney. The sanction order against appellee ex-husband and his attorney was set aside. Appellee ex-husband and appellant ex-wife settled the child support issues and a judgment was entered. The trial court sanctioned appellant ex-wife's attorney for fees incurred by appellee ex-husband in setting aside the sanctions order it erroneously signed. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of sanctions against appellant ex-wife's attorney. The court held that the trial court's action was not arbitrary or unreasonable in light of all the circumstances of the case and that sanction was appropriate under the trial court's inherent power to administer. The court reversed the child support judgment against appellant ex-wife because it did not reflect the parties' agreement as articulated before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of sanctions against appellant ex-wife's attorney, holding that it was appropriate under the trial court's inherent power to administer, but reversed the order of contempt against appellant ex-wife, because the child support judgment did not reflect the parties' agreement. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1398 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


San Antonio v. Texas Attorney Gen.


NO. 3-91-461-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


851 S.W.2d 946; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 975



April 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 12, 1993. Released for Publication May 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 474,803, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a summary judgment for appellee Attorney General (Texas) and appellee publisher and its employee from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), arguing that the trial court erroneously compelled disclosure of police department personnel records under the Texas Open Records Act.


OVERVIEW: In a declaratory judgment action brought by appellant city, appellee Attorney General (Texas) and appellee publisher and its employee filed counterclaims upon which the trial court granted summary judgment. The trial court held that personnel records kept by the municipal police department was subject to compelled disclosure under the Texas Open Records Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 6252-17a (Supp. 1992). The disputed information included complaints of misconduct against police officers that resulted in no disciplinary action. On appeal, the court reversed the decision and remanded, holding that the records were confidential under Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 143.089(g) (Supp. 1992) and, thus, not subject to compelled discovery under the Act. Based on the plain, simple, and unambiguous terms of § 143.089(g), the court concluded that the legislature intended to deem confidential the information maintained by the municipal police department for its own use. The court explained that there was no other reasonable explanation for the explicit prohibition against releasing such information under § 143.089(g).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment for appellee Attorney General (Texas) and appellee publisher and its employee and remanded based on its holding that personnel files of the appellant city's police department were deemed confidential and, thus, exempt from compelled disclosure under the Texas Open Records Act.

 

1399 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Austin


NO. 3-92-173-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


852 S.W.2d 71; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 991



April 7, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 12, 1993. Released for Publication May 12, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 493,373, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants parents challenged, in an appeal of the 345th District Court of Travis County (Texas), the ethnic and racial composition of the jury as unconstitutional in their wrongful death suit against appellee city.


OVERVIEW: A boy was shot and killed by officers responding to a report of gunfire in a residential area. Appellant parents brought a wrongful death action against appellee city for the shooting of their son. A jury was selected, sworn, and empanelled after which appellants moved to quash the original panel on the ground that appellants were denied the opportunity to select a jury from a panel composed of a fair cross-section of the community as guaranteed by the Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 3a, 13, 15, 19, 29, and Tex. Const. art. V, § 10. Judgment was rendered that appellants would take nothing on their wrongful death claim. The trial court held appellee liable for $ 1,000 in damages for emotional distress caused appellant father by appellee's actions after his son's death. Appellants alleged there was a defect in the composition of the jury panel. The court found appellants did not present data to establish a prima facie case of disparity and the issue was not preserved because appellants had information regarding racial and ethnic makeup of array and did not object until the jury was empanelled. The court concluded the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court did not err in denying appellant parents' motion to quash the panel because they had information of the racial and ethnic makeup of the array and the panel before voir dire and did not object.

 

1400 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. State


NO. C14-92-00027-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


852 S.W.2d 665; 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 888



April 1, 1993, Rendered  
April 1, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 230th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 598,557.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 230th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that convicted him for the offense of illegal investment of funds that were intended to further the commission of an offense, namely, possession of a controlled substance, to wit: marijuana, weighing more than 50 pounds by aggregate weight, including any adulterants and dilutants. Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Undercover officers met appellant on several occasions and told him they were marijuana suppliers looking for a buyer. Appellant found someone to purchase 1,000 pounds of marijuana at $ 625 per pound. Appellant drove with undercover officers to Houston where the exchange was to take place. They met with the buyer, the money was given to one of the undercover officers, and appellant along with buyer was arrested for the illegal investment of funds that were intended to further the commission of an offense, possession of a controlled substance, to wit: marijuana, weighing more than 50 pounds by aggregate weight, including any adulterants and dilutants. Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126 (1992). A jury found appellant guilty and assessed punishment at 12 years confinement with a $ 50,000 fine. Appellant challenged the conviction based on that § 481.126 was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to define the term "believes." The court found the term was readily understood by a person of common intelligence, which made the statute capable of being determined with reasonable precision what conduct the statute prohibited. The trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's sole point of error was overruled and the trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed. The statute was not vague because the term "believes" could have been readily understood by a person of common intelligence to determine with reasonable precision what conduct the statute prohibited.
